# Deep quality + correctness hunt -- findings register

Adversarial multi-agent sweep of `app/` (2026-06-07) for issues the pylint-10 cleanup, R0801, and disable re-audit cannot catch: semantic duplication, SOLID/cohesion, financial correctness, Decimal/rounding, IDOR/security, test-quality. 15 reviewers (11 subsystem clusters + 4 cross-cutting specialists) -> adversarial refute-by-default verification per finding -> this register. **Run TWICE** (independent samples); this register is their UNION (deduped).

**Ground rule:** every row cites `file:line`; each survived an independent verifier that read the code, tests, and callers and tried to refute it. `kind`: DEFECT = objectively wrong; CORRECTNESS-RISK = financial logic that may be wrong, needs domain confirmation; JUDGMENT = design/DRY/SOLID improvement needing a developer decision. `verdict`: CONFIRMED vs NEEDS-DECISION (accurate + real, fix is a developer judgment). **Runs:** `both` = independently found in both sweeps (highest confidence).

**Totals (union):** 88 unique verified findings -- 6 HIGH, 34 MED, 48 LOW; 21 corroborated by both runs.  Pre-existing OPEN items tracked elsewhere (NOT listed): P-1 (loan escrow threshold), P-3 (negative paycheck deduction).

## Status / dispositions (as of 2026-06-07)

**FIXED -- Batch C5 SOLID/TEST-QUALITY, non-financial (shipped on `dev` 2026-06-08; verified with a revert-proves-regression cycle, full suite 5814, `pylint app/` 9.97 held):**
- [x] **SOLID/#82 (error-masking half) + TEST-QUALITY/#86** (developer-selected "targeted DO #82a") removed the broad `except (ValueError, KeyError, AttributeError) -> return None` from `dashboard_service._get_debt_summary`, making it a thin honest wrapper over `savings_dashboard_service.compute_dashboard_data(...).get("debt_summary")`. The except conflated the designed no-debt `None` (which `_compute_debt_summary` returns natively, surfaced through the wrapper's `.get`) with a genuine programming bug -- silently blanking the debt panel and hiding real debt (rule 4). **Decisive evidence it was over-catching:** the savings route (`savings.py`) calls the same producer unguarded, as does every sibling dashboard section (`_get_savings_goals`/`_get_spending_comparison`/`_compute_cash_runway`); the lone broad-except was the inconsistent one. Its only `logger.warning` was the swallowed message, so the now-dead `logger`/`import logging` were removed. **#86:** added `test_debt_summary_with_debt` (loan-seeded success path through the wrapper -- total_debt/weighted_avg_rate/payment/payoff + the three DTI keys) and `test_debt_summary_propagates_errors` (patches the producer to raise `KeyError`, asserts it propagates; proven to fail under the restored masking). **Efficiency/SRP half of #82 DEFERRED** (developer decision 2026-06-08): a narrow debt-only producer cannot skip the heavy work -- DTI's `gross_biweekly` needs the full `calculate_paycheck` call and `_compute_debt_summary` needs the loan projections from `_compute_account_projections`; the genuinely-wasted work (goals/EF/archived/grouping) is a bounded one-page recompute, so a parallel producer is moderate-risk for modest gain (rule 13) -- `4ef36af`.

Extracted one private `_fold_income_expense(entries)` helper (income = signed sum of `is_income`; expense = sum of `abs` over non-income; both legs seed `Decimal("0")`), added a `day_totals: dict[int, tuple[Decimal, Decimal]]` field to `MonthSummary` built per-day from it, and derived the month headline totals as the sum of those per-day folds -- so the per-day cells and the month total come from one rule. `_build_calendar_weeks` now reads `data.day_totals.get(day_num, (Decimal("0"), Decimal("0")))`, replacing its two bare `sum()` folds (which also fixed the int-0 seed: an all-one-sign day previously yielded an int, inconsistent with the route's own `Decimal("0")` empty-cell branch). **Behavior-preserving:** month totals unchanged (the existing classification/total tests guard equivalence; only the real `MonthSummary` constructor at `_build_month_summary` was touched -- the CSV tests use a separate `FakeMonthSummary` duck-type). **FIXED -- Batch F CORRECTNESS/SECURITY, non-money-math (developer-selected track "Non-money defects + logging"; shipped on `dev` 2026-06-08; each verified against live code with a revert-proves-regression cycle, full suite 5830, `pylint app/` 9.97 held):**
- [x] **CORRECTNESS/#15** `restore_transfer`'s drift-correction loop re-synced only amount/status/period; it now re-syncs every field the service mirrors parent->shadow on create/update -- adding `category_id`, `due_date` (the finding), and `is_override`. **Completing the loop was a developer decision** ("Complete all 6"): the loop re-synced 3 of 6 mirrored-with-canonical-parent fields; `actual_amount`/`paid_at` stay excluded by design (the `Transfer` parent has no canonical column). A shadow whose `due_date` drifted via direct ORM mutation during the soft-deleted window was restored stale and mis-rendered calendar/dashboard/year-end/spending-trend (they read the SHADOW `Transaction.due_date`). 3 drift tests (due_date/category/is_override), each proven to fail without the fix; docstring lists all six + documents the exclusions -- `b372ccf`.
- [x] **CORRECTNESS-RISK/#27** `authenticate`'s no-user branch ran no bcrypt while the wrong-password branch ran a full `bcrypt.checkpw`, leaking account existence via response timing -- the enumeration oracle the generic message closes on the content axis, left open on the timing axis (the codebase already equalizes the lockout branch, so the no-user gap was the inconsistent one). The no-user branch now runs one throwaway `verify_password` against a fixed module-level `_DUMMY_PASSWORD_HASH` (generated at import with `gensalt()` so the cost tracks the same default real hashes use) and discards the result. `verify_password` (not a raw `checkpw`) keeps the input-validation short-circuits symmetric for every input shape. Locked-account bcrypt-skip kept (anti-lockout-oracle, out of scope). 2 tests (spy proves the dummy verify runs on the no-user branch; dummy is a parseable 60-char bcrypt digest so checkpw does real work), both proven to fail without the fix -- `c4db396`.
- [x] **SECURITY/DRY/#47** (un-deferred) the 9 inline `Account` ownership checks (`accounts/anchor.py` x6, `investment.growth_chart`, `accounts/detail.checking_detail`, `loan/_helpers._load_loan_account`) now call `get_or_404` -- emitting the F-144 `resource_not_found` / `access_denied_cross_user` event -- and keep `if account is None: return <original body>, 404`. `get_or_404` returns None for BOTH missing-PK and cross-user, exactly matching the inline `or` check, so every response body ("Not found"/"Account not found"/"") and status is byte-identical; only the log is new. **The deferral's sole blocker (preserving the differing HTMX fragment bodies) is resolved by keeping the original `return`, not the suggested `abort(404)`.** Trust-but-verify: F-087 was NOT actually in scope -- those sites already 404, whereas F-087 covers the 302-redirect routes; the STALE_CONFLICT re-fetches in anchor.py are not ownership checks and stay `db.session.get`. Route-level test pins a cross-user inline-anchor-form probe now emits the event (proven to fail with the routes reverted) -- `809e537`.
- [x] **SECURITY/#85** `get_accessible_transaction` -- the lone `auth_helpers` branch that violated the module's own "every ownership-failure branch emits a structured log_event" F-144 contract -- now emits `resource_not_found` (INFO) on missing PK and `access_denied_cross_user` (WARNING) on the owner and companion-visibility denials, reads the requester id via `_safe_user_id()`, and uses `getattr` fallbacks on `role_id`/`linked_owner_id` so an anonymous / misordered-decorator call denies-and-logs (`user_id` None => anonymous probe) instead of raising `AttributeError`. The access decision is unchanged for authenticated callers. 4 tests in the F-144 contract class (incl. the companion-visibility branch -- the finding's headline -- isolated to the not-visible denial); the 3 event-emitting ones proven to fail without the fix -- `a4736f2`.

**FIXED -- Batch G deterministic DRY/normalization, non-financial (developer-selected track "Deterministic DRY/norm"; shipped on `dev` 2026-06-08; each verified against live code, full suite 5834, `pylint app/` 9.97 held -- the three touched `app/` files at 10.00/10):**
- [x] **DRY/#72 + #73** the three bare `annual_rate / 12` rate-conversion divisors in `amortization_engine` (`calculate_monthly_payment`:217, `_recast_for_rate_change`:512, `project_forward` state init:624) now use the canonical `app.utils.money.MONTHS_PER_YEAR`, matching `rate_period_engine`/`interest_projection`/`escrow_calculator` and honoring money.py's "defined exactly once here; any future 26/12 inlining is a regression of D6-05". Value-identical (verified bit-identical incl. `str()` across 9 rates -- `Decimal/int == Decimal/Decimal`), so no test change; 176 engine + loan/rate/debt-strategy/loan-payment consumer tests green. Pure naming; NOT the closed-won't-fix ARM recast path (`_recast_for_rate_change`'s `calculate_monthly_payment` derivation is untouched) -- `9857435`.
- [x] **DECIMAL/NORMALIZATION/#65** `RecurrenceRule.interval_n`/`offset_periods` -- logic-bearing integer divisors (`interval_n` is the modulus in `recurrence_engine.match_periods`) that carried a Python `default=` only while DB-nullable, with CHECK constraints (`interval_n > 0`/`offset_periods >= 0`) that accept NULL (a NULL operand makes the predicate UNKNOWN, which PostgreSQL treats as satisfied) -- are now `nullable=False` + `server_default=text('1')/('0')`, the same F-068 storage-tier lock the C-25 sweep applied to the boolean/sort_order columns (these two were outside that sweep's scope). Migration `73e20c46de83` backfills NULLs to the logical default first (matching the model `default=` and the consumers' `or 1`/`or 0`), then ALTERs; tested up->down->up on the live DB (notnull/default flip + clean revert), `flask db check` reports no phantom diff. Added both columns to the C-25 `F_068_LOCKED_COLUMNS` catalog + a raw-insert behavioral test proving the server_default fires. **Fallback removal (developer decision 2026-06-08, fail-loud):** the four scattered `or 1`/`or 0` consumer coalesces (`recurrence_engine.match_periods` x2, `obligations._frequency_label`, `savings_goal_service.amount_to_monthly`) were REMOVED in a follow-on (`d30820c`). They silently coerced an invalid `interval_n=0`/None into "every period" -- masking a bug that in a budget app would over-generate projected transactions -- so `match_periods` now fails loud (ZeroDivisionError / TypeError) on an invalid in-memory rule. **Trust-but-verify catch:** removal broke two deliberate `TestMatchPeriodsEdgeCaseSafety` tests that pinned the `or 1` coerce-to-1 behavior by name; rather than silently rewrite safety tests (rule 5), this was surfaced to the developer, who confirmed the coerce->raise contract change -- the two tests were retargeted to assert the raise, the `day_of_month` coalesce + tests stay (that column is genuinely nullable), and a new model test pins that a persisted rule's `interval_n`/`offset_periods` are never None (full suite 5835) -- `55be9a8` (storage lock) + `d30820c` (fallback removal).
- [x] **DRY/EFFICIENCY/#74** `balance_as_of_date` built the live override map twice per call (prefix span inside `_project_to_period_before`, then the target period), re-running the live paycheck (`project_salary`) + loan-PITI recompute each time. Now builds ONE map over the prefix-union-target txn set and threads it into both helpers (the grid's build-once-and-thread pattern); `_project_to_period_before` drops its `account`/`scenario_id` params and its internal load/build -- the parent owns transaction loading and the single override build. Behavior-identical: the engine consumes the map via `.get(txn.id)`, so keys outside a span's own txns are never looked up, making the union map equivalent to the prior per-span maps; the boundary (`test_calendar_equals_resolver_at_period_boundary`) + cross-page balance-equality invariants stay green. New guard test asserts `live_amount_overrides` runs exactly once (proven to fail `assert 2 == 1` against the old double-build) -- `1c665c4`.

**FIXED -- Batch H present-balance CORRECTNESS + its bound test (developer-selected track "anchor true-up scope"; shipped on `dev` 2026-06-08; verified against live code with a revert-proves-regression cycle + independent code-reviewer ACCEPT, full suite 5836, `pylint app/` 9.97 held -- the touched `app/` files 10.00/10):**
- [x] **CORRECTNESS/#8 + TEST-QUALITY/#40** `entry_service.clear_entries_for_anchor_true_up` now takes `account_id` and adds `Transaction.account_id == account_id` to the subquery, so a checking true-up reconciles ONLY the trued-up account's past-dated projected entries. The prior owner-only filter (`PayPeriod.user_id == owner_id` alone) flipped `is_cleared=TRUE` across ALL the owner's checking accounts -- for a user with a 2nd checking account, trueing up A dropped B's reservation while B's anchor was never raised, silently inflating B's projected balance (the one present-balance money defect in the open set). All three call sites thread `account.id` (`anchor_service.apply_anchor_true_up`:235, `routes/accounts/crud.update_account`:367, `routes/accounts/anchor.inline_anchor_update`:113); the grid `true_up` + canonical inline anchor paths are covered transitively through `apply_anchor_true_up`. Revert-proved: with the `account_id` filter removed the test fails `assert True is False` and the log shows `cleared_count=2` (the over-clear); restored -> passes -- `095d1ad`.

  - **current-period double-count (#9/#10/#14) is DONE (Batch L):** un-paused 2026-06-08; the cross-reference confirmed the audit's `F-045` is a single-path producer verdict that never analyzed the YTD-window-vs-projection-window overlap, so the finding is fresh. Seed = `end_of_current - current_period_transfer_contribution`; YTD engine seed is strictly-before-current; fixed across investment/retirement/savings dashboards + synthetic paths. The savings dashboard was an un-named 3rd site (register-completeness catch). See the Batch L entry.
  - **rounding-mode consistency (#16/#19/#63 + #18 mode-half) is DONE (Batch M):** un-paused 2026-06-08; the cross-reference confirmed these are the unfinished residual of the audit's locked `E-26`/`HIGH-04` (NOT fresh, NOT ratified-as-banker's), so the fix -- route the bare banker's money quantizes through `round_money` -- is exactly what the audit prescribes. The value-changing "full-precision intermediate" half of E-26, the escrow rounding (#17/#67), the `period_subtotal` legs (#62), and the broader 19-file/99-site E-26 DRY tail across the rest of `app/` remain. See the Batch M entry.
  - **estimated-vs-effective (#11) STILL PAUSED:** it collides with the audit's ratified `F-027 S18` (`estimated_amount` contract-safe for transfer shadows by Invariant 3). The Batch L double-count fix is independent of the accessor and did NOT change it; #11 needs its own F-027-S18 cross-reference before any change.

## HIGH severity

### 1. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] project_forward ignores recorded recast P&I (RateChangeRecord.monthly_pi); schedule rows diverge from the loan card payment for a future ARM recast
- **Location:** `app/services/amortization_engine.py` :: 486-518, 644-654 (_recast_for_rate_change / project_forward); confirmed unread at grep monthly_pi -> only 98-142
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** loan-amort
- **Claim:** RateChangeRecord carries monthly_pi (the lender's recorded recast P&I), and build_rate_periods/period_for_date honor it for LoanState.monthly_payment, but project_forward's ARM handler _recast_for_rate_change (lines 508-518) ALWAYS derives the new payment via calculate_monthly_payment(state.balance, period_rate, months_left) and never reads RateChangeRecord.monthly_pi (grep confirms monthly_pi appears only in the dataclass definition/validation lines 98-142, never in the projection loop). I ran resolve_loan on a 5/5 ARM at $400k/6%/360 with a recorded recast monthly_pi=$2500.00 effective 2031-01-01 (the exact shape of test_arm_second_period_uses_recorded_recast_held_constant, test line 805): LoanState.monthly_payment = $2500.00 but the schedule's projected rows for that same period report payment=$2582.13.
- **Why it matters:** The entire amortization-engine-split architecture exists to guarantee the loan card and its schedule/chart cannot diverge (PayoffScenarios docstring, _payoff.py lines 40-62). For a mid-life ARM whose current recast P&I was recorded at setup (the documented production case for RateHistory.monthly_pi per loan_features.py lines 89-100), the loan card shows the lender's true statement payment while the schedule's projected rows for that period show a re-derived value ~$82/month different. That feeds wrong principal/interest splits, a wrong payoff_date, and a wrong total_interest into every consumer (savings dashboard, year-end liability, debt strategy) that reads the schedule -- real-money mismanagement on the exact loans that most need the recorded value.
- **Suggested fix:** Thread recorded recast P&I into the projection: have _recast_for_rate_change consult the matching RateChangeRecord.monthly_pi (when present) for the new period instead of always calling calculate_monthly_payment, mirroring rate_period_engine._recorded_pi_at_date.
- **Verifier evidence:** VERIFIED BY READING + RUNNING THE CODE.

(1) Factually accurate. grep confirms `monthly_pi` appears in app/services/amortization_engine.py ONLY at lines 98-142 (the RateChangeRecord dataclass field + __post_init__ validation); it is never referenced in project_forward (521-704) or _recast_for_rate_change (486-518). _recast_for_rate_change ALWAYS derives the new payment via calculate_monthly_payment(state.balance, period_rate, months_left) at lines 516-518 and never consults RateChangeRecord.monthly_pi. The recorded recast IS honored elsewhere: rate_period_engine._recorded_pi_at_date (314-342) + build_rate_periods (478-484) set period_pi to the recorded value, and that flows to LoanState.monthly_payment via period_for_date (_state.py:242). The two paths disagree.

(2) Real issue (empirically reproduced). I ran resolve_loan on the exact shape of tests/test_services/test_loan_resolver.py:805 (5/5 ARM, $400k/6%/360, origination 2026-01-01, recast 2031-01-01 @7% with monthly_pi=$2500.00, no payments). At as_of=2032-06-01: LoanState.monthly_payment = $2500.00 (correct, from period_for_date) but every second-period schedule row reports payment=$2582.13 -- exactly the finding's claim. Root cause traced: with no confirmed payments, replay.next_pay_date = 2026-02-01, so _remaining_rate_changes (_payoff.py:187) does NOT filter out the 2031 change; project_forward reaches it and _recast_for_rate_change re-derives $2582.13, ignoring monthly_pi=$2500. (A future-recast variant at as_of=2026-06-01 gives $2631.30 -- same bug.) LoanState.schedule = history_rows + committed_forward (_state.py:223), and payoff_date + total_interest are both derived FROM that schedule (_state.py:246-250). So the over-paid recast yields wrong P/I splits, wrong payoff_date, and wrong total_interest. Downstream consumers read these: app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_projections.py, debt_strategy_service.py, year_end_summary_service/_balances.py. This directly violates the engine-split architecture's stated invariant that the loan card and its schedule cannot diverge (PayoffScenarios docstring _payoff.py:34-62).

NOT test-covered: the cited test (test_loan_resolver.py:805-854) asserts ONLY state.monthly_payment and state_early==state_late; it never inspects state.schedule rows. No test anywhere asserts a schedule row payment of 2500/2582/2631 under a recorded-recast ARM (grep of tests/ returned none). So the divergence is genuinely uncovered. The ARM-recast test that DOES exist (test_amortization_engine.py:1041 test_arm_rate_change_during_projection) passes a RateChangeRecord WITHOUT monthly_pi and asserts re-derivation -- it does not contradict this finding.

(3) Not already known. F-8 (remediation_follow_up.md:593) is a DIFFERENT, RESOLVED bug (legacy generate_schedule anchor-reset recompute, gated on using_contractual for fixed-rate loans). F-27 (line 2005) is about projected recurring transfers (monthly_override), not recast P&I. Quality-pass.md:120 marks amortization_engine.py clean but the project_forward work (commit c4f01e6) was explicitly behavior-preserving decomposition. Not P-1 (escrow threshold) or P-3 (negative deduction). No accepted register entry covers this.

NOTE on verdict shape: the divergence between the card and its own schedule is unambiguously a bug under the stated invariant (CONFIRMED), but the precise fix -- threading recorded monthly_pi into _recast_for_rate_change (mirroring _recorded_pi_at_date) vs. some other reconciliation -- is a financial-correctness choice the developer should make; the suggested_fix is sound.

### 2. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] annual_cap on deductions is stored, validated and rendered but NEVER enforced in the paycheck calculation
- **Location:** `app/services/paycheck_calculator.py` :: 701-758
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** paycheck-tax
- **Claim:** PaycheckDeduction.annual_cap (model app/models/paycheck_deduction.py:122; validated app/schemas/validation.py:809; in the update allowlist app/routes/salary/_helpers.py:66; rendered app/templates/salary/_deductions_section.html:55) is never read in any calculation path -- `grep -rn '\.annual_cap' app/` outside growth_engine/templates/app.js returns nothing, and `_calculate_deductions` (lines 701-758) computes amount, applies the 24/12 per-year filters and inflation but contains NO cap logic. Yet its own docstring at line 713 lists '- annual cap tracking' as a handled responsibility.
- **Why it matters:** A user who caps a 401(k) at, e.g., $23,000/yr will have the full per-period amount subtracted every period for all ~52 projected periods with no ceiling. Projected net pay is understated once the cap should have been hit, YTD employer-match / contribution math built on this is wrong, and the projection silently implies contributions exceeding the legal limit -- a real-money error in a budgeting app, with no test catching it (no annual_cap test exists in test_paycheck_calculator.py).
- **Suggested fix:** Either implement cap enforcement in _calculate_deductions (track cumulative per-deduction YTD across prior periods and clamp the period amount so the annual sum <= annual_cap), or, if out of scope, fix the lying docstring and remove the dead column/UI -- but the cap is a user-set financial control and should be enforced.
- **Verifier evidence:** I was asked to refute F1 but the committed code independently confirms every claim, so it stands as CONFIRMED.

FACTUAL ACCURACY (all verified by reading the code):
- app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:701-758 -- read _calculate_deductions in full. It computes `amount = Decimal(str(ded.amount))` (736), applies percentage calc (737-740), the 24-per-year/3rd-paycheck skip (727-728), the 12-per-year first-of-month skip (731-733), and inflation (743-751), then appends a DeductionLine (754-756). There is NO reference to ded.annual_cap and NO cap-clamping logic anywhere in the function.
- Docstring at line 713 explicitly lists "- annual cap tracking" as a handled responsibility. It is not handled -> the docstring is inaccurate.
- Column exists: app/models/paycheck_deduction.py:122 `annual_cap = db.Column(db.Numeric(12, 2))` with DB CHECK at :51-54 (`annual_cap IS NULL OR annual_cap > 0`).
- Validated: app/schemas/validation.py:809-815 (Range min 0 exclusive, max 100M).
- In update allowlist: app/routes/salary/_helpers.py:66.
- Rendered in UI: app/templates/salary/_deductions_section.html:55, 72, 180.
- `grep -rn '\.annual_cap' app/` -> only template (55,72) and the column/allowlist/CHECK; `grep -rn 'annual_cap' app/services/` returns ZERO hits. The column is never read by any calculation path.
- I ruled out a false-negative: growth_engine.py:113 cap_contribution_at_limit DOES implement YTD-based capping, but it caps on InvestmentAccount.annual_contribution_limit (the IRS limit, growth_engine.py:132-135 docstring), an entirely separate concept from PaycheckDeduction.annual_cap. The deduction cap has no equivalent.

REAL ISSUE (not intended / not safe / not gold-plating):
- Not intended: tests/TEST_PLAN.md:133 flags this row as "Deduction with annual_cap (not yet enforced -- verify behavior)", confirming the team knows it is unenforced, and the function docstring claims to handle it -- so it is an unfinished feature, not deliberate design.
- Not test-covered: `grep -c annual_cap tests/test_services/test_paycheck_calculator.py` = 0. No calculator test exercises cap enforcement; the only annual_cap tests (test_c25_boundary_inclusivity.py:191-239, test_c24_range_check_sweep.py:315-320) cover schema validation, not enforcement.
- Impact: calculate_paycheck/_calculate_deductions is the sole deduction path (DeductionLine constructed only at paycheck_calculator.py:754). A user who caps e.g. a 401(k) at $23,000/yr gets the full per-period amount subtracted for every projected period with no ceiling, overstating contributions and understating projected net pay once the cap should bind -- a real-money projection error in a budgeting app, silent (no error, no test).

ALREADY KNOWN: No. Distinct from P-1 (loan escrow compute_monthly_payment_baseline) and P-3 (negative deduction). It is not a documented pylint disable nor a quality-pass ACCEPT row; the TEST_PLAN parenthetical is a test-plan note, not a tracked acceptance.

Severity HIGH retained: silent, incorrect financial projection for any capped deduction, no guard, no test. The fix direction (implement YTD per-deduction cap tracking + clamp, vs. remove the dead column/UI and correct the docstring) is a financial/design call for the developer, but the defect itself is unambiguous.

### 3. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] Spending-trend regression mislabels clearly-increasing categories as decreasing when early periods are zero (negative intercept unguarded)
- **Location:** `app/services/spending_trend_service.py` :: 362-376, 531-543
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** _trend_change uses first_predicted = intercept (regression value at period 0) and last_predicted = intercept + slope*(n-1); _safe_pct_change only guards first_predicted == 0, not negative. For a category that starts at zero then ramps up (e.g. period_totals [0,0,0,350,350,350]), OLS gives slope=+90, intercept=-50, so pct_change = (last-first)/first*100 = (220-(-50))/(-50)*100 = -900%. _direction_from_pct then returns 'down' even though slope (absolute_change) is +90. Verified by reproducing the regression math: [0,0,0,350,350,350] -> slope +90, intercept -50, pct -900%, direction 'down'.
- **Why it matters:** A user whose spending in a category is sharply rising is shown a large DECREASE and the item is routed into top_decreasing instead of top_increasing -- the trend tab gives the exact opposite of reality, which can drive a wrong budgeting decision. absolute_change (positive slope) and trend_direction ('down') are mutually contradictory in the same row.
- **Suggested fix:** In _safe_pct_change, treat first_predicted <= 0 (not just == 0) as the no-meaningful-base case (e.g. fall back to sign-of-slope direction or return None), or base pct_change on a non-negative reference such as period_average instead of the regression intercept.
- **Verifier evidence:** Cited code matches the claim. app/services/spending_trend_service.py:372-374 (_trend_change) sets first_predicted=intercept and last_predicted=intercept+slope*(n-1), then calls _safe_pct_change. _safe_pct_change (lines 531-543) ONLY guards first_predicted == _ZERO (line 540); a negative intercept divides through normally, flipping the sign of pct_change. _direction_from_pct (lines 546-553) returns "up"/"down" purely from the sign of pct_change, ignoring slope. is_flagged (line 413) uses abs(pct_change) >= threshold, and _build_top_lists (lines 471-483) routes by trend_direction.

Reproduced the regression math (Decimal, identical closed-form OLS from lines 514-528): period_totals [0,0,0,350,350,350] -> slope=+90 (absolute_change=90.00), intercept=-50, first_predicted=-50, last_predicted=+400 (NOT 220 as the finding states -- minor arithmetic slip in the intermediate value), pct_change=(400-(-50))/(-50)*100 = -900.00, direction="down", flagged=True. So a sharply-RISING category is shown as -900% DECREASE and routed into top_decreasing, while absolute_change in the SAME row is +90.00/period (template app/templates/analytics/_trends.html:88,127 and 221-222 render absolute_change beside the down direction -> self-contradictory row). Also reproduced with a softer ramp [0,0,100,200,300,300] -> slope +71.43, intercept negative, pct -1250%, dir "down". The bug requires the OLS intercept to go negative (steep early-zero ramp), which is a plausible real pattern (a new recurring bill activating mid-window).

Tests do NOT cover it: test_zero_start_handling (tests/test_services/test_spending_trend_service.py:431-462) sets up exactly a zero-start Car category but asserts ONLY "car is not None" and its comment ("pct_change is 0 due to zero-start guard") is itself wrong -- the guard only fires when intercept==0, not when it's negative. test_regression_with_zeros (lines 178-184) asserts only slope>0, never pct_change. No test asserts direction=="up" for a rising-from-zero category, so the contradiction passes the suite silently.

Not already known: quality-pass.md row 409 covers spending_trend_service only for the pylint too-many-locals decomposition and explicitly certifies the arithmetic was kept "byte-identical" -- it validated refactor-equivalence, NOT the correctness of the negative-intercept pct logic. Unrelated to P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative paycheck deduction). Verdict is CONFIRMED; could equally be NEEDS-DECISION since the correct base (sign-of-slope fallback vs. period_average reference vs. None) is a developer financial-design choice, but the defect itself -- positive absolute_change with "down" direction and top_decreasing routing -- is unambiguous and user-facing.

### 4. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] _get_window_periods has no upper date bound, so future projected periods pollute the trend window
- **Location:** `app/services/spending_trend_service.py` :: 218-249, 339-359, 396-403
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** The docstring says 'The window ends at the end of the current month and extends back window_months months,' but the query filters only `PayPeriod.start_date >= first_day` with no `<= today`/end-of-month upper bound and orders by period_index. The app generates ~2 years of forward pay periods, so this returns the window start through every future period. _period_totals_for_item zero-fills those future periods (settled expenses can never exist for the future), and _compute_item_trend divides total_spending by n_periods (the inflated count incl. ~50 future zeros) for period_average and feeds the long zero tail into the regression.
- **Why it matters:** period_average is understated by dividing by an inflated period count, and the trailing block of zero future periods biases every category's regression slope/pct_change toward 'decreasing'. The whole trends tab is systematically skewed and the documented behavior does not match the code.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an upper bound to the query (e.g. `PayPeriod.start_date <= last_day_of_current_month`) so the window only spans the intended historical months.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUAL: app/services/spending_trend_service.py:241-249 -- _get_window_periods's query has only ONE date filter, `PayPeriod.start_date >= first_day` (line 245), and orders by `period_index` (line 247). There is NO upper bound. The docstring at lines 224-225 claims "The window ends at the end of the current month and extends back window_months months," but the code never implements the upper bound. compute_trends (line 159) passes these periods straight to _query_paid_expenses and _build_item_trends with no further date filtering; the route (app/routes/analytics.py:299-302) calls compute_trends directly with no window narrowing.

FORWARD PERIODS EXIST IN PRODUCTION: app/services/pay_period_service.py:26,35 -- generate_pay_periods defaults to num_periods=52 (~2 years forward), assigning period_index monotonically in chronological order (lines 79-84), so order-by period_index == chronological and the future periods form a trailing block.

IMPACT (numerically reproduced via the service's own _compute_linear_regression / _trend_change / period_average math): a steadily-rising grocery category over a bounded 6-month window (13 real periods, 400..640) yields slope=+20, pct_change=+60% ("up"), period_average=$520. With 50 trailing future zeros appended (the unbounded behavior), the SAME data yields slope=-7.94, pct_change=-139.27% ("down"), period_average=$107.30. The zero tail both understates period_average ~5x (division by n_periods=63 incl. ~50 zeros, spending_trend_service.py:399-401) AND inverts the regression direction (lines 362-376). This is a systematic correctness defect across the whole trends tab.

NOT TEST-COVERED: every fixture in tests/test_services/test_spending_trend_service.py creates exactly `num_periods` periods all in the past relative to today=2026-06-07 (e.g. test_trend_increasing line 327 starts 2025-06-06; last period start = 2026-01-02 < today). I simulated _get_window_periods against that fixture: only 3 past periods land in the window and ZERO future periods exist in the test DB, so the missing upper bound is structurally invisible to the suite. Several tests (lines 236-246, 496-508) mock date.today precisely because the window slides, but none create future periods.

NOT INTENDED / DIVERGENCE: the sibling app/services/budget_variance_service.py (which _count_distinct_paid_months docstring at line 191-192 cites as "consistent with") bounds BOTH ends (first_day AND last_day, lines 264-269), and pay_period_service itself uses `start_date <= as_of` / `start_date <= last_day` patterns (lines 115, 253) -- so bounding the upper end is the established pattern and its omission here is the defect.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction). No documented disable covers this; the only inline disable in the file (line 276, duplicate-code on _query_paid_expenses) is unrelated to the window bound.

Verdict CONFIRMED. Corrected severity HIGH (the fix's exact upper bound -- end-of-current-month vs today vs end-of-current-period -- is a minor design choice, but the defect itself is unambiguous; not NEEDS-DECISION because adding any upper bound is plainly correct vs the current unbounded behavior).

### 5. [SECURITY/DEFECT] Pension create/update accepts cross-user salary_profile_id with no ownership check (cross-user salary disclosure)
- **Location:** `app/routes/retirement.py` :: 133, 261-263
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-idor
- **Claim:** create_pension builds PensionProfile(user_id=current_user.id, **data) at line 133 and update_pension copies fields in _PENSION_FIELDS (which includes 'salary_profile_id', defined at retirement.py:35-36) onto the pension at lines 261-263. salary_profile_id arrives from the form via PensionProfileCreate/UpdateSchema (app/schemas/validation.py:1983 and :2043) as a plain `fields.Integer(allow_none=True)` with no ownership validation, and neither route re-checks it against current_user. retirement_dashboard_service.py:431-435 then dereferences pension.salary_profile.annual_salary and profile.raises to project the benefit, so linking a pension to a victim's salary_profile_id reads the victim's salary and raise history into the attacker's retirement projection.
- **Why it matters:** This is an IDOR that leaks another user's annual salary and raise schedule (sensitive financial data) into the attacker's own dashboard, and lets an attacker attach their pension to a foreign salary profile. It is the same class of route-boundary FK probe that create_inline / update_transaction / create_transfer_template already enforce for account_id/category_id/pay_period_id; the pension routes were missed.
- **Suggested fix:** In both create_pension and update_pension, when salary_profile_id is present and non-None, verify db.session.get(SalaryProfile, id).user_id == current_user.id (404 per the security rule) before persisting, mirroring _resolve_owned_fks.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every claim verified against committed code.

FACTUAL ACCURACY (all confirmed):
- app/routes/retirement.py:133 -> `pension = PensionProfile(user_id=current_user.id, **data)`. `data` is the schema-loaded form, so a user-supplied salary_profile_id flows straight in.
- app/routes/retirement.py:35-39 _PENSION_FIELDS includes "salary_profile_id"; :261-263 update_pension does `for field_name, value in data.items(): if field_name in _PENSION_FIELDS: setattr(pension, field_name, value)` -- so update also writes salary_profile_id verbatim.
- app/schemas/validation.py:1983 (Create) and :2043 (Update): `salary_profile_id = fields.Integer(allow_none=True)` -- plain integer, NO ownership/@validates check.
- Neither route re-checks salary_profile_id against current_user. update_pension's only ownership check is get_or_404(PensionProfile, pension_id) on the PK (:201); the salary FK is never probed. create_pension has no FK probe at all.
- app/services/retirement_dashboard_service.py:431-434 in _compute_pension_benefit: `if pension.planned_retirement_date and pension.salary_profile: profile = pension.salary_profile; ... Decimal(str(profile.annual_salary)), profile.raises ...` -> a foreign profile's salary + raise history is projected into the attacker's benefit. pensions are loaded filter_by(user_id=user_id) (:255-258), but the salary_profile relationship (model :83 `db.relationship("SalaryProfile", lazy="joined")`) follows the raw FK with no user filter.

NO SAFETY NET: app/models/pension_profile.py:64-67 -- salary_profile_id is a plain FK to salary.salary_profiles.id (ondelete SET NULL), no composite (user_id, salary_profile_id) constraint, so PostgreSQL accepts a foreign id. SalaryProfile has a direct user_id column, so an ownership check is trivial.

REAL ISSUE (not intended/safe/covered): The comparison the finding draws is correct -- app/routes/transactions/create.py:75-82 (create_inline) and :121-127 (create_transaction) call _resolve_owned_fks([(Account,...),(Category,...),(PayPeriod,...),(Scenario,...)]); update_transaction uses _verify_owned_fks_in_update (app/routes/transactions/_helpers.py:338-376) which probes pay_period_id/category_id. The helper _resolve_owned_fks (:293-335) is the established route-boundary IDOR probe (404 for both not-found and not-yours). The pension routes do not use it.
NO TEST COVERAGE for this vector: tests/test_routes/test_retirement.py:368-422 (test_edit_pension_idor / test_delete_pension_idor) and tests/test_integration/test_access_control.py:686-742 (TestRetirementAccessControl) only protect the pension RESOURCE (User B cannot edit/update/delete User A's pension). None tests User B creating/updating their OWN pension with User A's salary_profile_id. The test_c24 sweep uses profile.id of the same user only.

ALREADY KNOWN = NO: docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:433 has a "retirement F2" row but it is the B1 type-precision item (bare list/dict -> precise element types), a different "F2" (rubric letter, not this reviewer's finding id) -- unrelated to ownership. Not P-1 (loan escrow baseline) or P-3 (negative deduction). Not a documented disable.

Severity HIGH stands: cross-user disclosure of annual salary + raise schedule plus attaching a pension to a foreign salary profile. Fix is mechanical (mirror _resolve_owned_fks: when salary_profile_id is present and non-None, verify db.session.get(SalaryProfile, id).user_id == current_user.id, 404 otherwise), so CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION.

### 6. [SECURITY/DEFECT] create_transaction (POST /transactions) does not ownership-check category_id -- write-side IDOR
- **Location:** `app/routes/transactions/create.py` :: 110-143 (FK probe at 121-127)
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** The ad-hoc create route `create_transaction` calls `_resolve_owned_fks` for only Account, PayPeriod, and Scenario (create.py:121-125), with the comment 'this route carries no category' -- but `TransactionCreateSchema.category_id` is a REQUIRED field (validation.py:250) and `Transaction.category_id` is a real FK to budget.categories with `ondelete=SET NULL` (transaction.py:162-164). A foreign user's category_id therefore passes the FK constraint (the row exists), raises no IntegrityError, and `Transaction(**data)` (create.py:92->133) persists the attacker's transaction referencing victim B's category. The sibling route `create_inline` DOES check Category ownership (create.py:75-83), and the GET form partials all check it (forms.py:133-137, 177-181, 223-229), and the PATCH path checks it via `_verify_owned_fks_in_update` (_helpers.py:371-374) -- only this one mutating route omits it.
- **Why it matters:** Violates the project's mandatory route-boundary FK ownership rule (C-29/F-029) and the IDOR/404-for-both security rule. An authenticated owner can attach another user's category to their own transaction, leaking the victim's category display name onto the attacker's grid and corrupting category-scoped reporting. It is a confirmed cross-tenant data-integrity hole on a money record.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `(Category, data["category_id"], "Category not found")` to the `_resolve_owned_fks([...])` spec list in `create_transaction` (mirroring create_inline) and import Category.
- **Verifier evidence:** CONFIRMED -- write-side IDOR: create_transaction (POST /transactions) omits the Category ownership check.

1. create.py:110-127 -- create_transaction calls _resolve_owned_fks([(Account,...),(PayPeriod,...),(Scenario,...)]) ONLY, with the comment at create.py:119-120 "this route carries no category". That comment is factually false.

2. category_id IS required and IS loaded. The finding cited app/routes/transactions/validation.py:250, but the actual file is app/schemas/validation.py:250 (path wrong, line number correct): `category_id = fields.Integer(required=True)` in TransactionCreateSchema (validation.py:241-250). So data["category_id"] is always present and flows into Transaction(**data) at create.py:133.

3. transaction.py:162-164 -- category_id is a real FK to budget.categories.id with ondelete="SET NULL" and is nullable (no nullable=False). Category is UserScopedMixin (category.py:17), i.e. user-scoped. The FK constraint enforces row existence only, NOT ownership; a victim's category_id passes the constraint, raises no IntegrityError, and the attacker's transaction persists referencing the victim's category (HTTP 201).

4. Asymmetry confirmed: create_inline DOES check Category (create.py:77 (Category, data["category_id"], "Category not found")); the GET partials check it (forms.py:134, 178, 224); PATCH checks it via _verify_owned_fks_in_update (_helpers.py:373-374). Only create_transaction omits it.

5. TEST GAP (this is why it shipped): tests/test_routes/test_transaction_auth.py has test_inline_create_with_other_users_category (line 257) for the INLINE route, test_create_with_other_users_period (line 273) and test_create_with_other_users_scenario_id (line 290) for the bare route -- but NO test_create_with_other_users_category for the bare /transactions route. The only category test for the bare route is test_create_with_nonexistent_category_id (line 392) which asserts 400 (FK fails -> IntegrityError -> 400). A cross-tenant category behaves differently: the row exists, so no IntegrityError, so it persists. I ran both baseline tests: PASSED (2 passed in 1.67s) -- confirming the nonexistent path is 400 and the inline cross-user path is 404, the two distinct behaviors that prove the gap.

Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable, not a quality-pass ACCEPT. Violates C-29/F-029 route-boundary FK ownership rule and the 404-for-both security rule. Suggested fix is correct: add (Category, data["category_id"], "Category not found") to the spec list in create_transaction (mirroring create_inline) and import Category (already imported at create.py:20). Sole inaccuracy in the finding is the schema file path; substance and line numbers are correct, so the finding stands.


## MED severity

### 7. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] update_tax_config silently no-ops (no config created, no error flash) when flat_rate is omitted and no config exists yet
- **Location:** `app/routes/salary/tax_config.py` :: 55-93
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** StateTaxConfigSchema declares flat_rate as NOT required and strips empty strings in @pre_load (validation.py:968-978), so a POST with state_code + tax_year but no/empty flat_rate validates. In update_tax_config, flat_rate resolves to None (line 56). When no StateTaxConfig row exists, the else branch's inner guard 'if flat_rate is not None' (line 74) is False, so NO row is created and NO flash is emitted, yet the handler still calls db.session.commit(), _regenerate_all_salary_transactions(), commits again, and redirects to the tax settings page (lines 86-93). The user sees a normal redirect with no success or error message and no config saved.
- **Why it matters:** The user believes they configured their state tax rate, but projections silently continue with no state tax applied -- mis-stating projected net pay across every period. A skipped write should never be reported as success; per CLAUDE.md rule 4 (never ignore a problem) it must surface a clear error.
- **Suggested fix:** When flat_rate is None and no existing config is found, flash a 'State tax rate is required' danger message and redirect without committing/regenerating (or make flat_rate required in the schema).
- **Verifier evidence:** Every cited detail verified against committed code.

SCHEMA (app/schemas/validation.py): StateTaxConfigSchema.flat_rate (lines 975-978) is declared `fields.Decimal(places=2, as_string=True, validate=Range(min=0,max=100))` with NO `required=True`. The `@pre_load strip_empty_strings` (lines 968-970) drops keys whose value == "". So a POST with state_code + tax_year but empty/omitted flat_rate passes `.validate()` and loads with flat_rate absent. (By contrast, FicaConfigSchema marks every rate `required=True` at lines 943-962, so the same hole does not exist there -- confirms the state-tax path is uniquely affected.)

HANDLER (app/routes/salary/tax_config.py:42-93): line 55-56 `flat_rate = None; if data.get("flat_rate") is not None:` -> stays None when omitted. Line 61-65 looks up existing StateTaxConfig. Line 72 `else:` (no existing row) -> line 73 computes flat_type_id, line 74 `if flat_rate is not None:` is False -> NO StateTaxConfig is created and NO flash is set anywhere in this branch (the only success flashes are line 71 update-branch and line 84 inside the create guard). Line 86 `db.session.commit()`, line 89 `_regenerate_all_salary_transactions()`, line 90 commit, line 93 redirect to settings.show?section=tax all run unconditionally. Net: clean redirect, no row saved, no success or error message. Claim is accurate in full.

MODEL (app/models/tax_config.py:165 + CHECK 130-133): flat_rate column is nullable and the CHECK explicitly permits `flat_rate IS NULL`, so a NULL-flat_rate row is a legal state (a no-income-tax state). This is why the fix is a judgment call, not mechanical.

NOT SAFE-BY-CONSTRUCTION: the only form posting here (app/templates/settings/_tax_config_sections.html:60-61) adds the HTML `required` attribute, but that is client-side only and trivially bypassed by curl/HTMX/scripted POST; the server-side schema is the mandated safeguard and it accepts the input by design.

NOT TEST-COVERED: tests/test_routes/test_salary.py TestTaxConfig (lines 1381-1456) covers create-with-flat_rate (1393), fica (1414), invalid-state-code (1436, still sends flat_rate), and fica-missing-field (1448). No test exercises empty/omitted flat_rate with no existing config.

NOT ALREADY-KNOWN: docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/{plan,quality-pass}.md reference tax_config only for mechanical pylint work (line-length, import hoisting, the salary.py module split, UserScopedMixin extraction) -- no ACCEPT row for this behavior. Not P-1 (loan escrow) and not P-3 (negative deduction).

NEEDS-DECISION rationale: the schema's deliberate optionality of flat_rate (plausibly to support no-tax states or standard_deduction-only edits) means the correct remedy is a financial/design choice -- (a) flash danger + skip commit/regenerate, (b) make flat_rate required, or (c) intentionally create a NULL-flat_rate row for no-tax states -- each with different modeling semantics. settings.show (app/routes/settings.py:95,173,231) only lists existing configs and adds no no-config warning, so nothing mitigates the silent outcome.

Severity MED held (lower end): realistic UI triggering is blocked by client-side `required`, requiring a scripted POST or a future template change, but the consequence when triggered (state tax silently omitted from every projected paycheck, reported via a success-style redirect) is a real-money correctness concern and violates CLAUDE.md rule 4 (never silently report a skipped write as success).

### 8. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] Anchor true-up clears entries across ALL of the user's accounts and scenarios, not just the trued-up account/scenario
- **Location:** `app/services/entry_service.py (invoked by app/services/anchor_service.py:234)` :: 681-700 (filter); anchor_service.py:232-235
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** balance-grid
- **Claim:** clear_entries_for_anchor_true_up(owner_id) filters only by PayPeriod.user_id == owner_id, Transaction.is_deleted == False, and is_projected_clause(Transaction) (entry_service.py:689-693). It has NO account_id and NO scenario_id predicate. apply_anchor_true_up (anchor_service.py:222-235) is called to true up ONE specific checking account, but the entry-clear it triggers flips is_cleared=TRUE on every past-dated uncleared entry on every Projected transaction the owner has -- including transactions on a second checking account and transactions in other scenarios. accounts have no per-type uniqueness (only uq_accounts_user_name, account.py:44), so multiple checking accounts are allowed, and transactions/entries are scenario-scoped.
- **Why it matters:** Once an entry is is_cleared=TRUE, _entry_checking_impact subtracts it from the reservation (balance_calculator.py:281-284), treating it as 'already in the anchor.' But the OTHER account's / OTHER scenario's anchor was never updated, so that account's projected balance silently rises by the cleared amounts -- a wrong checking balance for a budgeting app. The leak across scenarios is unconditional (any user with >1 scenario), and across accounts for any user with a second checking/envelope-bearing account.
- **Suggested fix:** Add account_id == account.id (and the operating scenario_id) to the subquery filter in clear_entries_for_anchor_true_up and thread both from apply_anchor_true_up; join Transaction.account_id == account.id.
- **Verifier evidence:** FILTER: clear_entries_for_anchor_true_up (app/services/entry_service.py:681-695) filters ONLY on TransactionEntry.is_cleared.is_(False), entry_date <= today, and a Transaction subquery joined to PayPeriod with PayPeriod.user_id == owner_id, Transaction.is_deleted.is_(False), is_projected_clause(Transaction). Confirmed: NO account_id predicate and NO scenario_id predicate. CALLER: apply_anchor_true_up (anchor_service.py:222-235) gates on account.account_type_id == checking_type_id for ONE account but passes only user_id (line 234). Same pattern in routes/accounts/crud.py:354-359 (update_account) and routes/accounts/anchor.py wiring.

MULTI-ACCOUNT (REAL, PRESENT): accounts have only uq_accounts_user_name (account.py:44) -- no per-type uniqueness; create_account (routes/accounts/crud.py:132+) accepts any visible account_type_id with no single-checking enforcement, so a user can hold two checking accounts. Each account's grid loads its OWN account-scoped txns+entries (routes/accounts/detail.py:114-124: Transaction.account_id == account.id, scenario_id == scenario.id, selectinload(entries)). A true-up on checking A flips is_cleared=TRUE on checking B's past-dated projected debit entries; B's grid then runs _entry_checking_impact (balance_calculator.py:281-284) = max(estimated - cleared_debit - sum_credit, uncleared_debit), which lowers B's reservation (debit moves uncleared->cleared) while B's anchor was never raised -> B's projected balance silently inflates. Mechanism and downstream subtraction confirmed against the actual code, not docstrings.

CROSS-SCENARIO (OVERSTATED / NOT PRESENTLY REACHABLE): every txn-creating path uses get_baseline_scenario; the only scenario-creation route is grid.py:565-590 create_baseline (is_baseline=True). scenario.py:4-5 docstring: Phase 1 is baseline-only; clone/what-if is Phase 3. So no user can currently have >1 scenario with transactions -- the finding's claim that the leak is 'unconditional (any user with >1 scenario)' is not currently true; it is a latent Phase-3 concern, not a present defect.

TESTS: tests/test_services/test_anchor_service.py covers single-account checking-clears (lines 225-288) and savings-skip (155-223) only; NO test creates a second checking account, so the cross-account leak is uncovered, not test-protected.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: grep of docs/audits (financial_calculations, security-2026-04-15, pylint-cleanup) shows no entry for this cross-account/cross-scenario entry-clear; not P-1, not P-3, not a documented disable, not a quality-pass ACCEPT row.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION: the multi-account defect is genuine and accurately described, but the correct remedy is a developer design call -- (a) scope the clear by account_id (and thread it from apply_anchor_true_up), vs (b) enforce one checking account per user at creation (which would make the contract's stated single-checking assumption real). Severity reduced HIGH->MED: the leak requires a non-default setup (a second checking account); the cross-scenario amplifier the finding leans on is not currently reachable.

### 9. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] Dashboard re-projects the current period from its already-complete end balance (double counts current-period growth + contribution)
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py` :: 531-539, 209-211, 149-172
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `_resolve_current_balance` returns `balances.get(current_period.id, anchor_balance)`, which `balance_resolver.balances_for` documents as the projected END balance of that period (balance_resolver.py:261,415,760 'projected end balance'). `_project_dashboard_balances` then builds `future_periods = [p for p in all_periods if p.period_index >= current_period.period_index]` (line 532-535), which INCLUDES the current period, and feeds them to `_run_growth_projection` starting from that end-of-current-period balance. The growth engine `_project_one_period` applies growth on the opening balance plus a fresh contribution for the current period (growth_engine.py:340-379), so the current period's growth and contribution are applied a second time on top of a balance that already contains them.
- **Why it matters:** The first projection row (and therefore the entire forward chart and the dashboard 'projected balance' figures) overstates the balance by roughly one period's contribution + growth. On a real account this is a visible, recurring over-projection of retirement money that compounds across the horizon.
- **Suggested fix:** Project from the prior period's end balance, or exclude the current period from `future_periods` (use `period_index > current_period.period_index`) so the loop starts after the period whose end balance was used as the seed.
- **Verifier evidence:** Could not REFUTE; the finding's mechanics are accurate and a real over-projection exists for transfer-funded accounts, but the suggested one-line fix is wrong for deduction-funded accounts, so the correct remedy is a developer financial judgment (NEEDS-DECISION).

FACTUAL CHAIN (all verified against committed code):
- app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:172 `_resolve_current_balance` returns `balances.get(current_period.id, anchor_balance)`. balance_resolver.py:260-267 (BalanceResult.balances) and :415 (balances_for docstring) state this is the "projected END balance for that period." So the seed = END balance of the current period.
- investment_dashboard_service.py:532-535 `future_periods = [p for p in all_periods if p.period_index >= current_period.period_index]` INCLUDES the current period (period_index is monotonic, pay_period.py:27; the current period sorts first).
- :256 `_run_growth_projection` seeds `current_balance=ctx.current_balance`. growth_engine.py:340 `start_balance = state.current_balance`; :343-345 growth on start_balance; :350-356 contribution looked up by `period.start_date`; :376-377 `end_balance = start + growth + contribution + employer`. So the FIRST row (the current period) applies growth + contribution on top of a balance that already represents the current period's end state. _build_chart_series (:288-296) plots `pb.end_balance`, so the over-projection is user-visible on the chart's first point and the whole forward curve.

REAL ISSUE, but funding-path dependent (the finding overstates by treating it as universal):
- build_contribution_timeline (investment_projection.py:340-379) has TWO paths. Path 1 deductions (:305-307): "there is no per-period transaction record for deductions" -> deduction contributions are NOT in budget.transactions, so balances_for's current-period end balance does NOT include them; re-projecting the current period's deduction is CORRECT and necessary. Path 2 transfers (:357-379): shadow income Transactions with a pay_period_id that calculate_balances DOES count for projected income (balance_calculator.py:475-493, is_projected) -> these ARE in the seed AND re-added by the growth engine -> genuine double-count (one period's transfer contribution + growth-on-contribution) for transfer-funded accounts.
- Even for deduction accounts, seeding from the END of the current period while the engine treats it as the START applies a full extra period of growth (order/off-by-one), distinct from the contribution double-count.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN / NOT TEST-COVERED:
- Distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction). The pylint-cleanup of this file (plan.md commit e3dbea7, 2026-06-05) is explicitly "no logic change, behavior bit-identical"; the quality-pass register only renamed/typed helpers (quality-pass.md:396-397) and never analyzed this seed/period correctness -- so a pre-existing semantic defect.
- Cross-surface inconsistency corroborates it: compute_growth_chart_data (:666-670) seeds the SAME current_balance but projects synthetic periods from date.today() (generate_projection_periods, growth_engine.py:584-595, ids 1..N) whose start_dates never match real period start_dates, so the chart always uses periodic_contribution fallback and never re-adds a current-period transfer shadow -- the two surfaces disagree on the current period.
- Tests do not catch it: test_routes/test_investment.py test_dashboard_with_deduction (:601-624) only asserts substring `b"500.00" in resp.data`; test_growth_chart_with_deduction (:626-652) only asserts the chart renders. No test seeds a transfer-funded account with a current-period shadow contribution and pins the first projection row's start_balance/end_balance vs the seed.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION not CONFIRMED: the suggested fix (period_index > current_period.period_index) is correct for transfer-funded accounts but would WRONGLY DROP the current period's deduction contribution for deduction-funded accounts (whose seed lacks it). The correct fix differs by funding path and is a financial/design judgment. Severity corrected HIGH->MED: it bites only the transfer-funded current period (a one-period offset that does not compound period-over-period beyond the first row; the rest of the chain is internally consistent), and many investment accounts here are deduction-funded.

### 10. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] YTD seed double-counts the current period against the annual contribution limit
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_projection.py` :: 224-238, 282-290
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `_ytd_contributions` sums contributions for periods with `p.start_date <= current_period.start_date` (line 228-232), i.e. it INCLUDES the current period. The dashboard then passes this as `ytd_contributions_start` (investment_dashboard_service.py:263) while also projecting the current period via the `contributions` timeline (F1). In `_project_one_period`, the engine adds the current period's contribution to `state.ytd_contributions` and subtracts it from `remaining_limit` (growth_engine.py:382-385) on top of a seed that already counted it.
- **Why it matters:** When the annual contribution limit binds, the current period's contribution is charged against the limit twice, so the engine caps later contributions ~one period early and under-projects total contributions and the employer match. Real-money projection error in the limit-binding case.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute the YTD seed over periods strictly before the projection's first period (`p.start_date < current_period.start_date`), or once F1/F2 stop re-projecting the current period, ensure the YTD window and the projected window do not overlap.
- **Verifier evidence:** VERDICT: NEEDS-DECISION (the finding is factually accurate and a real defect; the correct fix is a financial/design judgment for the developer). Could not refute it.

FACTS VERIFIED BY READING THE CODE:
1) app/services/investment_projection.py:228-232 -- _ytd_contributions builds ytd_period_ids with `p.start_date <= current_period.start_date`, i.e. it INCLUDES the current period. The matching contribution sum runs over those ids (234-237). CONFIRMED, and tests lock this in: test_investment_projection.py:198-200 (current=periods[3], YTD=1500 includes period 4) and :388-393 ("YTD only includes current_period=periods[0], which has the $200 contribution"). So the seed deliberately includes the current period.
2) app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:262 passes ytd_contributions_start=ctx.inputs.ytd_contributions. CONFIRMED.
3) app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:531-536 builds future_periods with `p.period_index >= current_period.period_index` -- INCLUDES the current period -- and feeds it to _run_growth_projection. CONFIRMED.
4) app/services/growth_engine.py:458-466 seeds state.ytd_contributions=ytd_start and remaining_limit=max(limit-ytd_start,0). Every period in the list runs _project_one_period (475-478) with no skip. Line 363-367 caps the period's contribution via cap_contribution_at_limit using the RUNNING state.ytd_contributions; lines 382-385 then add that contribution to state.ytd_contributions and subtract from remaining_limit. So the current period's contribution is charged against the limit TWICE (once in the seed, once on re-projection). CONFIRMED -- exactly the mechanism claimed. When the limit binds, later contributions cap ~one period early -> under-projected contributions and employer match.

BROADER THAN THE FINDING STATES (related, larger): _resolve_current_balance (investment_dashboard_service.py:149-172) returns balances.get(current_period.id) -- the END-of-current-period balance. balance_resolver.py:287 documents the invariant balances[p]-balances[p-1]==period_subtotal(p).net, and shadow-income contributions are budget.transactions counted in that subtotal, so current_balance ALREADY includes the current period's contribution. Re-projecting the current period (step 4, growth_engine.py:376-379) adds the contribution to the balance AGAIN. This over-projects the balance on EVERY load with a current-period contribution, not only when the limit binds.

DUPLICATED ACROSS DASHBOARDS: retirement_dashboard_service.py:861-865 uses the identical `period_index >= ctx.current_period.period_index` fallback window with ytd_contributions_start=inputs.ytd_contributions (891) and balance from bals.get(ctx.current_period.id) (821) -- same defect (its primary path uses synthetic_periods, but the no-synthetic fallback hits the same overlap).

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: Not P-1 (loan escrow) nor P-3 (negative deduction). The quality-pass rows for investment_projection.py/growth_engine.py (quality-pass.md:138,342,363) only verified the lint refactor was BEHAVIOR-EQUIVALENT to the pre-refactor monolith -- they did not assess whether the original YTD-window/projection-window overlap was financially correct, so the bug predates and survived the cleanup unchanged. No documented disable covers it.

NO TEST COVERS IT: test_investment.py limit tests (701-967) assert UI prompts only; no test hand-computes projected contribution/limit_remaining/end_balance for a current-period contribution overlapping the YTD seed.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION: the fix is a design call -- (a) compute the YTD seed strictly-before (`< current_period.start_date`) so it does not overlap the projected window, OR (b) start the projection at `period_index > current_period.period_index` (since current_balance already bakes in the current period), OR (c) re-anchor to a start-of-current-period balance. Each has different effects on the displayed first-period row and the balance side, so the developer must choose; whichever is chosen should be applied consistently to both the investment and retirement dashboards. Severity MED upheld (read-only projection, no money moved; per-load error is one period's contribution + its growth), with the note that the balance over-projection is broader than the limit-only framing in the finding.

### 11. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] Same shadow-income transactions are summed via estimated_amount in one path and effective_amount in another
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_projection.py` :: 166-167, 234-237, 368-372
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `_average_transfer_contribution` (line 166-167) and `_ytd_contributions` (line 234-237) sum `t.estimated_amount`, but `build_contribution_timeline` sums `txn.effective_amount` (line 368) for the SAME shadow-income transactions. `effective_amount` returns `actual_amount` when populated, else `estimated_amount` (transaction.py:241-248). Both outputs feed the same projection: the timeline supplies per-period dated amounts and YTD seeds the limit, while the average is the periodic fallback.
- **Why it matters:** For any settled contribution whose actual differs from estimated, the per-period dated amount (effective) and the YTD/limit seed and periodic fallback (estimated) disagree on the same dollars, so the limit accounting and the fallback for un-dated periods are computed off a different number than the engine actually applies. Inconsistent contribution accounting in the limit/fallback math.
- **Suggested fix:** Use one amount accessor for contribution math throughout -- prefer `effective_amount` everywhere (it is the documented single source of truth for balance contribution) so the average, YTD seed, and per-period timeline agree.
- **Verifier evidence:** All three legs of F4 independently confirmed from committed code.

(1) FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- yes.
- _average_transfer_contribution sums Decimal(str(t.estimated_amount)) at app/services/investment_projection.py:166-167.
- _ytd_contributions sums Decimal(str(t.estimated_amount)) at app/services/investment_projection.py:234-237.
- build_contribution_timeline uses amount = txn.effective_amount at app/services/investment_projection.py:368.
- effective_amount returns actual_amount when populated, else estimated_amount, at app/models/transaction.py:241-248 (and is documented there, lines 234-239, as "the single source of truth for what amount a transaction contributes to balance projections").
- Both outputs feed the SAME project_balance call on the SAME acct_contributions list: app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:219-230 passes the one acct_contributions list into BOTH build_investment_projection_inputs (-> estimated avg + estimated YTD) AND build_contribution_timeline (-> effective timeline); _run_growth_projection (lines 255-264) then passes periodic_contribution=inputs.periodic_contribution, ytd_contributions_start=inputs.ytd_contributions, AND contributions=ctx.contributions into one growth_engine.project_balance. Same dual-feed in app/services/year_end_summary_service/_savings.py:205-235.

(2) REAL ISSUE -- yes; the divergent state is reachable and matters, and is untested.
- Reachability: app/services/transfer_service.py:542-571 (_apply_actual_amount) mirrors a settled actual_amount onto both shadow transactions, so a shadow income txn can have actual_amount != estimated_amount. Not an impossible scenario (not rule-13).
- Effect: in growth_engine._project_one_period (app/services/growth_engine.py:350-385), a period WITH a dated record uses the timeline amount (effective) for the applied contribution AND the annual-limit cap, while ytd_contributions_start (estimated YTD seed, lines 458-466) seeds state.ytd_contributions/remaining_limit and periodic_contribution (estimated avg) is the fallback for un-dated periods (line 356). When actual differs from estimated, the limit/remaining-limit accounting seed and the un-dated fallback are computed off a different dollar figure than the engine actually applies for the same contributions.
- Untested: the two functions are tested with disjoint fakes -- FakeContribution exposes ONLY estimated_amount (tests/test_services/test_investment_projection.py:43-47) and FakeContribTransaction exposes ONLY effective_amount (lines 434-439). No test sends one transaction with actual_amount != estimated_amount through both paths into one projection. growth_engine YTD tests (tests/test_services/test_growth_engine.py:1076-1123) use ytd_contributions_start=ZERO, so they never exercise the estimated-seed vs effective-timeline mismatch.

(3) ALREADY KNOWN -- no. Not P-1 (loan escrow) nor P-3 (negative deduction). quality-pass.md row #20 (line 138) and rows at lines 363-368 verified only refactor behavior-equivalence of investment_projection.py vs the prior monolith (which already used estimated_amount in both helpers); no register row addresses estimated-vs-effective consistency BETWEEN _average_transfer_contribution/_ytd_contributions and build_contribution_timeline. No documented disable covers it.

Why NEEDS-DECISION not CONFIRMED: accurate + real, but the correct fix (align on effective_amount for the average and YTD seed too, vs intentionally keeping estimated for the fallback/seed) is a financial-design judgment the developer must ratify; the suggested fix direction (effective_amount everywhere, matching transaction.py:234-239's single-source-of-truth claim) is sound but should be a deliberate decision, and any change must hand-compute the limit/cap interaction.

### 12. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] _apply_raises does not implement the documented 'flat before percentage' ordering, making same-date raise compounding order-dependent
- **Location:** `app/services/paycheck_calculator.py` :: 572-624
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** paycheck-tax
- **Claim:** The docstring (lines 575-577) states 'Raises are sorted by (effective_year, effective_month) before application so that flat raises apply before percentage raises within the same effective date ... This ensures deterministic results regardless of database query order (M-01).' But the sort key at line 594 is only `(r.effective_year or 0, r.effective_month or 0)` with NO tertiary key for flat-vs-percentage; the relationship order_by (app/models/salary_profile.py:116) is also only year,month. The unique constraint uq_salary_raises_profile_type_year_month keys on raise_type_id too, so two DIFFERENT raise types (e.g. a merit % and a COLA flat) CAN coexist at the same year+month.
- **Why it matters:** Raise application is non-commutative: (salary*1.03)+5000 != (salary+5000)*1.03 (a ~$150 annual-salary difference at $100k). For two same-date raises of different types the compounded result depends on stable-sort input/DB order, contradicting the documented deterministic contract; a re-query in a different order silently changes projected gross/net pay. No test pins the claimed flat-before-percentage behavior (grep for 'before'/'M-01' in test_paycheck_calculator.py returns nothing).
- **Suggested fix:** Add a tertiary sort key that orders flat raises before percentage within the same (year, month), e.g. key=lambda r: (r.effective_year or 0, r.effective_month or 0, 0 if r.flat_amount else 1), and add a test asserting the documented order.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every factual claim in F2 checks out against the committed code.

DOCSTRING vs IMPLEMENTATION mismatch (the core defect):
- app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:575-578 -- docstring states raises are sorted "so that flat raises apply before percentage raises within the same effective date" and "This ensures deterministic results regardless of database query order (M-01)."
- app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:592-595 -- the actual sort key is `lambda r: (r.effective_year or 0, r.effective_month or 0)`. There is NO tertiary key for flat-vs-percentage. Python's sorted() is stable, so two same-(year,month) raises retain their input (relationship) order; the docstring's flat-before-percentage promise is NOT enforced.
- app/models/salary_profile.py:116 -- the relationship order_by is also only `effective_year, effective_month`, with no method/id tie-break, so the DB returns same-date ties in plan-dependent (non-deterministic) order.

The mixed-type same-date scenario is real and supported:
- app/models/salary_raise.py:76-81 -- uq_salary_raises_profile_type_year_month keys on raise_type_id (with NULLS NOT DISTINCT). Two DIFFERENT raise types CAN coexist at the same (year, month).
- app/models/salary_raise.py:52-56 (ck_salary_raises_one_method) -- each raise is exactly one method (percentage XOR flat_amount); method is independent of raise_type_id. So a COLA flat raise and a Merit percentage raise both effective Jan 2026 is a valid, creatable combination.
- app/routes/salary/items.py:75-109 -- the create route accepts any raise_type_id with either method; the only block (line 109) is the same-type-same-date duplicate. A different-type same-date pair is permitted.

Non-commutativity / financial impact is real and pre-documented:
- app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:627-634 (_apply_single_raise) -- percentage does salary*(1+pct); flat does salary+flat. Order-dependent.
- docs/adversarial_audit.md:369-372 -- the original M-01 finding gives the exact example: flat-first $100K+$5K then *1.03 = $108,150 vs pct-first *1.03 then +$5K = $108,000, a $150/yr divergence that compounds. docs/implementation_plan_audit_remediation.md:1100 states the fix's GOAL was flat-before-percentage, but the suggested key (line 1093-1096) was `(effective_year, effective_month)` -- which does not achieve the stated goal. The implementation copied the inadequate key, not the goal.

No test pins the behavior:
- tests/test_services/test_paycheck_calculator.py -- of 16 FakeRaise uses, only one (line 324) uses flat_amount, and it is a single recurring flat raise. The two multi-element raise fixtures (lines 3059, 3287) each contain a single percentage raise. grep for "before"/"M-01"/flat+percentage-at-same-date yields nothing. The documented contract is untested.

Not already known:
- docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:328-334 reviewed paycheck_calculator.py in depth (_PaycheckContext, _bracket_federal, DeductionBreakdown, _residue_cents, net-pay determinism) but has NO row touching _apply_raises ordering or the flat-before-percentage gap.
- Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). Not a documented inline disable.

Severity: MED is appropriate. Requires a user to create two different-type same-date raises with different methods (real but uncommon); divergence is bounded (~$150/yr at $100k per the audit example) but compounds across projection years and silently changes projected gross/net on re-query. The code fails to honor its own documented deterministic contract. The suggested tertiary key (0 if flat else 1) directly matches the documented intent, so this is a defect fix; the only judgment item is whether "flat before percentage" is itself the financially-correct convention (the docstring already asserts it is).

### 13. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] _get_raise_event labels a recurring raise in calendar years BEFORE its effective_year, disagreeing with the salary actually applied
- **Location:** `app/services/paycheck_calculator.py` :: 646-664
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** paycheck-tax
- **Claim:** _get_raise_event matches a recurring raise purely on `raise_obj.is_recurring and period_month == eff_month` (line 651), ignoring eff_year entirely. By contrast _apply_raises only applies a recurring raise when `period_year >= eff_year` (line 609). So a recurring raise with effective_year=2027, effective_month=3 produces a 'MERIT +X%' event label on the March-2026 paycheck (line 651 true) while _apply_raises applies nothing that year.
- **Why it matters:** The projection table (salary/projection.html via PeriodInfo.raise_event) shows a raise event in a period whose gross did not change, contradicting the displayed gross/net. It misleads the user about when their raise takes effect. Display-only, but it is wrong financial information in the salary forecast UI.
- **Suggested fix:** Gate the recurring branch on the effective year as _apply_raises does: `if raise_obj.is_recurring and period_month == eff_month and (eff_year is None or period_year >= eff_year):`.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/services/paycheck_calculator.py. _get_raise_event line 651: `if raise_obj.is_recurring and period_month == eff_month: is_match = True` -- matches purely on month, eff_year is read into a local (line 648) but NEVER used in the recurring branch. The non-recurring branch (line 653 `elif eff_year == period_year and eff_month == period_month`) DOES gate on year. By contrast _apply_raises (lines 601-614): for a recurring raise with an eff_year, salary only changes when `period_year >= eff_year` (line 609); the local var test test_recurring_raise_not_yet_effective (tests/test_services/test_paycheck_calculator.py:237-246) confirms a recurring raise (eff_month=3, eff_year=2026) applies nothing on a 2026-02 period. So for a recurring raise with effective_year=2027, effective_month=3, a 2026-03 period: _get_raise_event returns a "MERIT +X%" label (651 true: 3==3) while _apply_raises returns the unraised salary (609 false: 2026>=2027 is false). Label disagrees with the applied gross.
