Consumer: line 269 feeds _get_raise_event into PeriodInfo.raise_event (dataclass field default at line 140), which is rendered in app/templates/salary/projection.html line 43 (table-warning row highlight) and lines 52-53 (green "MERIT +X%" badge), and salary/breakdown.html line 53. So the wrong label is user-visible in the salary forecast for every pre-effective-year March -- showing a raise in a period whose gross/net did not change.

Test coverage: the ONLY _get_raise_event test, test_raise_event_appears_in_correct_period (line 1055-1073), uses is_recurring=False (line 1060), exercising the year-gated elif branch (653), not the buggy recurring branch (651). No test covers a recurring raise in a calendar year before its effective_year for the label. Not test-covered.

Not already known: distinct from P-1 (loan escrow threshold) and P-3 (negative deduction); not a documented disable or quality-pass ACCEPT. The suggested fix (gate the recurring branch on `(eff_year is None or period_year >= eff_year)`, mirroring _apply_raises) is mechanical and correct -- hence CONFIRMED, not NEEDS-DECISION. Severity MED: display-only (computed money is correct) but it is wrong financial information misrepresenting when a raise takes effect.

### 14. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] Retirement projection has the same current-period double-count in its no-horizon fallback path
- **Location:** `app/services/retirement_dashboard_service.py` :: 856-865, 884-894, 787-826
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (MED confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `_resolve_current_balances` stores `bals.get(ctx.current_period.id, anchor)` per account (line 820-822) -- the end-of-current-period balance. When there is no `planned_retirement_date`, `synthetic_periods` is empty so `_project_one_account` falls back to `projection_periods = [p for p in ctx.all_periods if p.period_index >= ctx.current_period.period_index]` (line 861-865) and runs `project_balance` from `balance` (line 884-894). As in F1, the current period is re-projected on top of a balance that already includes it.
- **Why it matters:** `projected_balance` (used by `_sum_projected_balances` -> `gap_result.projected_total_savings` -> required-savings/surplus and the gap chart) is overstated by one current-period contribution + growth per account whenever a user has no planned retirement date set. This directly distorts the surplus/shortfall the retirement dashboard reports.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the F1 fix: start the fallback projection from the period after the current one (`period_index > current_period.period_index`), keeping `balance` as the current-period end balance.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- verified line-for-line:
- app/services/retirement_dashboard_service.py:820-822: balance_map[acct.id] = bals.get(ctx.current_period.id, anchor). balances_for (app/services/balance_resolver.py:408-507, delegating to balance_calculator.calculate_balances at balance_calculator.py:57-124) returns the END-of-period balance, which for the current period already includes that period's contributing transactions (anchor period uses _sum_remaining; post-anchor uses _sum_all). Shadow-income contributions into the account (transfer_id IS NOT NULL, INCOME) are captured by _load_balance_transactions (balance_resolver.py:358-368, account_id == account.id + balance_contributing_clause), so a transfer-funded current-period contribution IS in this balance.
- retirement_dashboard_service.py:856 balance = batch.balance_map.get(...); :860-865 fallback projection_periods = [p for p in ctx.all_periods if p.period_index >= ctx.current_period.period_index] -- INCLUDES the current period; :884-894 project_balance(current_balance=balance, periods=projection_periods,...).
- growth_engine.py:_project_one_period (306-397) applies growth (Step 1) AND a fresh periodic_contribution (Step 2, contribution_lookup is None here so the periodic fallback is used) for EVERY period, including the first/current one. No skip-first mechanism. So the current period is re-projected on top of a balance that already reflects it.

REAL ISSUE -- impact path confirmed: projected_balance (retirement_dashboard_service.py:899) -> retirement_gap_calculator._sum_projected_balances (50-62) -> projected_total_savings (162) -> savings_surplus_or_shortfall (165) and the SWR retirement-income figure (retirement_dashboard_service.py:682). For transfer-funded accounts this double-counts ~one current-period contribution; for all funding it applies an extra current-period growth on an already-period-end balance, overstating the dashboard's surplus/shortfall.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not P-1/P-3, no documented disable. quality-pass.md rows 4 (retirement) and 5 (investment) are "REVIEWED ... test-gap", behavior-EQUIVALENCE only -- they verify the refactor computes what the original did, not whether the original is correct; the overlap is nowhere accepted.

NOT TEST-COVERED: the no-InvestmentParams tests (test_retirement_dashboard_service.py:605-668) skip the growth math; test_returns_current_net_when_no_retirement_horizon (199-217) tests _compute_gap_net_biweekly, NOT projected_balance; the C8 test (449-525) pins only current_balance, never projected_balance.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION (not clean CONFIRMED): the identical overlap exists in (a) the with-horizon synthetic path -- generate_projection_periods starts at date.today() (growth_engine.py:570-596) which is INSIDE the current period (get_current_period, pay_period_service.py:98-119), starting from the same end-of-current-period balance -- and (b) the shared investment_dashboard_service pattern (_resolve_current_balance:172 + _project_dashboard_balances:531-535, same period_index >= current). The suggested fix only patches the no-horizon fallback, leaving the synthetic path and the sibling service inconsistent. The correct fix turns on a semantic decision (does the resolved current balance mean start-of-period or end-of-period, and should projection begin mid-current-period, at next period, or carry a partial-period growth) that the developer must make and apply uniformly across all three sites.

### 15. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] restore_transfer does not re-sync shadow due_date drift, violating the extended Transfer Invariant 3
- **Location:** `app/services/transfer_service.py` :: 894-927
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** transfer-txn
- **Claim:** The drift-correction loop in restore_transfer corrects only estimated_amount (899-906), status_id (909-916), and pay_period_id (919-926), but never due_date -- even though update_transfer (671-675) and _build_shadow (322) mirror due_date to both shadows, and the Transfer model docstring (transfer.py:160-169) states the parent due_date is canonical and mirrored to shadows per 'Transfer Invariant 3'. A shadow whose due_date drifted while the transfer was soft-deleted is restored with the stale due_date.
- **Why it matters:** After restore, the two shadows can carry a due_date different from the parent transfer. Consumers that read the shadow Transaction.due_date (calendar, dashboard 'paid on time', year-end) would show a wrong due date and mis-compute days_paid_before_due, while the parent shows the correct one -- a silent invariant break the restore path is supposed to repair.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a fourth drift check in the loop: if shadow.due_date != xfer.due_date, log and set shadow.due_date = xfer.due_date (mirroring the amount/status/period blocks).
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- verified every cited line. restore_transfer's drift-correction loop (app/services/transfer_service.py:894-927) corrects exactly three fields: estimated_amount (899-906), status_id (909-916), pay_period_id (919-926). It never touches shadow.due_date. Meanwhile due_date IS a mirrored field: _build_shadow sets due_date=xfer.due_date (322) and update_transfer mirrors it to both shadows (671-675: xfer.due_date / expense_shadow.due_date / income_shadow.due_date). The Transfer model docstring (app/models/transfer.py:160-169) explicitly states the parent due_date is canonical and "the transfer service mirrors it to both shadow transactions so the two stay equal (Transfer Invariant 3)," and lists the consumers that read the SHADOW due_date: "calendar, dashboard, year-end, spending-trend."

IS A REAL ISSUE -- not gold-plating an impossible scenario. The loop's own docstring (776-802) defines its purpose as restoring shadows and "verifies and corrects shadow invariants (amount, status, period) that may have drifted while the transfer was soft-deleted." The two drift tests (tests/test_services/test_transfer_service.py:1142, 1173) simulate drift by directly mutating a shadow (bypassing the transfer service) -- establishing that defensive drift-repair from ANY direct mutation is the intended contract here, not a hypothetical. due_date is in the exact same class of mirrored invariant fields as the three already repaired, so its omission is a genuine asymmetry. Real consumers compute date-sensitive output from the shadow's due_date: dashboard_service.py:231 computes days_until = (txn.due_date - today).days; dashboard_service.py:161/398/437/461-462 and budget_variance_service.py:309 attribute/filter by Transaction.due_date. So a shadow restored with a stale due_date silently shows a wrong due date and mis-computes days-until/days-paid-before-due while the parent shows the correct one -- exactly the invariant break the restore path is meant to repair. Confirmed there is NO due_date drift test in TestRestoreTransfer (class at line 1059; grep for due_date+restore/drift inside it returns nothing).

NOT ALREADY KNOWN -- the quality-pass register (docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:401-403) touches transfer_service.py only for TransferSpec (R0902), _build_shadow (DRY), and the update_transfer decomposition -- NOT the restore_transfer drift loop. Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). No documented disable involved.

Severity MED is correct: balance integrity is unaffected (the model docstring 165 and Transfer Invariant 5 confirm the balance/loan engines never read due_date), but post-restore the two shadows can carry a due_date differing from the parent, producing wrong calendar/dashboard/variance/year-end display and days-until-due math -- a silent display/attribution invariant break, not a money-corrupting one. Fix is mechanical and matches the existing blocks (the canonical-source question is already resolved by the model docstring: parent is canonical), so this is CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION.

### 16. [DECIMAL/DEFECT] Suggested recurring-transfer amount is rounded with implicit ROUND_HALF_EVEN, then persisted as a template default
- **Location:** `app/routes/investment.py` :: 200
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** transfer_amount = (limit / _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR).quantize(TWO_PLACES) at line 200 omits rounding=, defaulting to ROUND_HALF_EVEN. transfer_amount is passed as default_amount into build_recurring_transfer_template (line 218-224) and persisted -- a stored, recurring money value that drives shadow transactions and balance projections, not a display-only number.
- **Why it matters:** A persisted recurring contribution amount that lands on a half-cent (e.g. an annual limit divisible to a .xx5 per-period value) rounds opposite to the documented ROUND_HALF_UP convention, so the persisted transfer can be a cent off from what every other path would compute. money.py exists specifically to prevent this implicit-mode leak at persistence boundaries.
- **Suggested fix:** Use round_money(limit / PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR) (importing both from app.utils.money) so the persisted amount follows the project rounding mode.
- **Verifier evidence:** app/routes/investment.py:200 reads `transfer_amount = (limit / _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` with no rounding= arg; TWO_PLACES=Decimal("0.01") (line 51), _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR=26 (line 53). Python Decimal default = ROUND_HALF_EVEN. transfer_amount -> default_amount at investment.py:218-224 -> persisted to TransferTemplate.default_amount (Numeric(12,2)) in _transfer_creation_helpers.py:177 -> seeded into transfers AND their shadow transactions via transfer_recurrence.py:102 (amount=template.default_amount through transfer_service.create_transfer). So it is a persisted, recurring, shadow-driving money value, NOT display-only -- the finding's persistence claim is exact.

The project's own app/utils/money.py module docstring states ROUND_HALF_UP "is the only default... ROUND_HALF_EVEN... must never be reached implicitly through a bare .quantize(Decimal('0.01'))." round_money() (ROUND_HALF_UP) and PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR=Decimal("26") both live there; investment.py imports neither and uses a local TWO_PLACES + bare-26.

Realizability verified by computation: annual_contribution_limit is Numeric(12,2) (app/models/investment_params.py:108), so limit/26 always terminates; ~1.92% of 2dp limits in [0,30000] land on a .xx5 half-cent where HALF_EVEN vs HALF_UP diverge by one cent (e.g. $0.13 -> 0.005 -> HE 0.00 vs HU 0.01; $0.65 -> 0.025 -> HE 0.02 vs HU 0.03). Round-dollar IRS limits ($7000,$23000) happen not to diverge, but arbitrary user limits do.

Not test-covered: the transfer-creation route tests (tests/test_routes/test_investment.py:836,852,880,977,1015-1044) all post an explicit amount ("269.23"/"1000.00"), hitting the user-override branch (investment.py:172), never the suggested-default branch at line 200. The _compute_suggested_contribution unit tests (lines 193-219) only cover zero-cap/None-cap (both yield 0.00, where rounding mode is irrelevant). No half-cent boundary is asserted anywhere.

Semantic sibling with the SAME defect: app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:386-388 computes the dashboard suggested_amount via `(remaining_limit / max(remaining_periods,1)).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` -- also bare implicit ROUND_HALF_EVEN, local TWO_PLACES (line 68), money.py not imported.

Not already-known: not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). quality-pass.md row 5 (investment_dashboard_service, e3dbea7) reviewed type-precision/bundle-caveat/test-gap and was "behavior bit-identical" -- it preserved the bare quantize, did not audit the rounding mode; routes/investment.py is not in the register at all. No documented disable covers this.

Verdict CONFIRMED, severity MED: a persisted recurring contribution can be one cent off the project's ROUND_HALF_UP convention at half-cent boundaries; deterministic, low blast radius (one cent on the seed default, and only when the user accepts the suggestion). Fix per suggestion: round_money(limit / PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR) from app.utils.money, and apply the same to the dashboard sibling at investment_dashboard_service.py:388.

### 17. [DECIMAL/DEFECT] Per-component escrow rounding does not equal the aggregate -- displayed rows and the monthly-escrow total diverge by a cent
- **Location:** `app/services/escrow_calculator.py` :: 44-82, 85-128
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** build_escrow_display rounds EACH component's monthly to cents at line 67 ((annual/12).quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP)), while calculate_monthly_escrow sums full-precision monthlies and rounds ONCE at line 128. These produce different totals: two $100/year components yield displayed rows summing to $16.66 but an aggregate monthly_escrow of $16.67 (verified: python shows template=16.66 aggregate=16.67). _escrow_list.html renders both side-by-side -- the per-row Monthly column (line 37) and the OOB monthly_escrow badge (line 16) computed by calculate_monthly_escrow -- so the user sees rows that do not add up to the badge.
- **Why it matters:** The build_escrow_display docstring (lines 49-51) explicitly claims 'every row's monthly value matches the rule the aggregate calculate_monthly_escrow uses.' It does not: round-each-then-sum != sum-then-round. A mortgage escrow display where the line items do not total the stated monthly escrow undermines trust and is a real money-display inconsistency on the same screen.
- **Suggested fix:** Have the template (or build_escrow_display) derive the displayed total by summing the same full-precision monthlies and rounding once, OR document that per-row values are individually-rounded approximations whose sum may differ by a cent -- not 'match'.
- **Verifier evidence:** Could NOT refute -- the finding is accurate and real. Verified against committed code (no working-tree changes).

(1) FACTUALLY ACCURATE. app/services/escrow_calculator.py:67 rounds EACH component's monthly: `monthly = (annual / MONTHS_PER_YEAR).quantize(TWO_PLACES, rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)` (round-each-then-sum, since the caller/template sums the rows). escrow_calculator.py:125-128 sums full-precision monthlies and rounds ONCE: `monthly = annual / MONTHS_PER_YEAR; total += monthly` then `return total.quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP)` (sum-then-round). The two methods diverge. Reproduced: python3 with two $100/yr components -> round-each-then-sum = Decimal('16.66'), sum-then-round = Decimal('16.67'), diverge = True. The docstring at escrow_calculator.py:49-51 ("so every row's monthly value matches the rule the aggregate calculate_monthly_escrow uses") is materially false: round-each != sum-then-round.

(2) REAL ISSUE, rendered side-by-side. Per-row monthly: app/templates/loan/_escrow_list.html:37 renders `comp.monthly_amount` (from build_escrow_display). Aggregate badge: _escrow_list.html:16 renders `monthly_escrow` (from calculate_monthly_escrow). dashboard.html:284 renders the same `monthly_escrow` badge and dashboard.html:288 includes _escrow_list.html -- both on screen together. Both data sources are produced by the SAME route render: app/routes/loan/escrow_rates.py:164+170 and :211+217 pass monthly_escrow=calculate_monthly_escrow(...) and escrow_components=build_escrow_display(...); app/routes/loan/dashboard.py:419 (build_escrow_display) + :608 monthly_escrow=ctx.loan.monthly_escrow, which traces to loan_payment_service.py:124 calculate_monthly_escrow(...). $100/yr components (small HOA / supplemental insurance) are realistic -- any component whose annual/12 third decimal is >=5 contributes drift -- so this is NOT a rule-13 impossible scenario.

NOT test-covered. tests/test_services/test_escrow_calculator.py TestBuildEscrowDisplay only uses 4800/2400/1000/500 (none produce sub-cent drift vs the aggregate). No test asserts sum(build_escrow_display rows) == calculate_monthly_escrow. The test_inactive_excluded docstring (lines 284-286) even CLAIMS "the per-row display and the badge total can never disagree" but the test body only verifies active/inactive filtering, not rounding equality -- a test-quality gap reinforcing the false invariant.

(3) NOT already known. quality-pass.md row 34 concerns NOT extracting escrow Step 1 for DRY in loan_payment_service.py -- unrelated to this rounding divergence. Not P-1 (escrow threshold baseline) and not P-3 (negative deduction). grep of docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/ for build_escrow/round-each/sum-then-round = no match. No documented disable.

VERDICT NEEDS-DECISION (not CONFIRMED) because the correct fix is a developer financial/display judgment: (a) sum full-precision monthlies and round once for the displayed total, (b) add a displayed Total row that sums the rounded rows so badge == visible total, or (c) relax the docstring to call per-row values individually-rounded approximations. Severity MED: max 1-cent visual mismatch, display-only (no balance/payment/PITI math is affected -- those use calculate_monthly_escrow/calculate_total_payment which round once), but it is a visible line-items-do-not-total-the-badge inconsistency on a money screen and a false docstring invariant.

### 18. [DECIMAL/DEFECT] Percentage-of-salary contribution rounds banker's in investment path but HALF_UP in paycheck path (same business rule, two answers)
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_projection.py` :: 98-102
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** _compute_deduction_per_period computes the percentage-of-salary contribution as `gross = (salary / pay_per_year).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` (line 98) and `amt = (gross * amt).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` (line 101), both bare quantize with NO rounding argument, so Decimal's default ROUND_HALF_EVEN (banker's) applies. The identical computation in the canonical paycheck path, app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:738, does `amount = (ctx.gross_biweekly * amount).quantize(TWO_PLACES, rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)`. For gross=1000.50 and pct=5%, raw=50.0250 -> investment path yields 50.02 while the paycheck deduction yields 50.03 (verified by direct Decimal evaluation).
- **Why it matters:** app/utils/money.py:8-11 names exactly this `.quantize(Decimal("0.01"))` pattern as a silent source of one-cent drift that 'must never be reached implicitly.' The investment dashboard's projected per-period contribution can disagree by a cent with the actual paycheck deduction for the same 401k/percentage line, so the projection and the real deduction silently diverge.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP` to the quantize calls at lines 98, 101 (and 173), or route them through app.utils.money.round_money.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE (verified):
- app/services/investment_projection.py:28 TWO_PLACES = Decimal("0.01").
- Lines 98 `gross = (salary / pay_per_year).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, 101 `amt = (gross * amt).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, and 173 `(total_contrib / num_periods_with_contrib).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` are ALL bare quantize -> implicit ROUND_HALF_EVEN (banker's). grep confirms the module contains NO `rounding=`/ROUND_HALF_UP anywhere.
- Canonical paycheck path app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:738-740 uses `.quantize(TWO_PLACES, rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)`.
- app/utils/money.py:8-11 explicitly names `.quantize(Decimal("0.01"))` bare as a forbidden silent one-cent-drift source; ROUND_HALF_UP is the only sanctioned default.
- Math reproduced by direct Decimal eval: salary 26013/26 = gross 1000.50, *5% = raw 50.0250 -> banker's 50.02, half-up 50.03. Divergence confirmed.

REAL ISSUE (verified same business rule): build_contribution_timeline docstring (investment_projection.py:305-306) and comment (351-355) state Path 1 reproduces the dollar amount "taken from the paycheck" -- so the investment projection is modelling the SAME percentage-of-salary deduction the paycheck calculator computes, and the project mandates one rounding convention. The bare quantize violates that standard.

NOT covered by tests: test_investment_projection.py:116-117 (`gross = (Decimal("100000")/26).quantize(Decimal("0.01")); expected = (gross*Decimal("0.07")).quantize(Decimal("0.01"))`) is TAUTOLOGICAL -- it recomputes the production expression (same bare quantize) rather than a hand-computed literal, so it ratifies whatever rounding the code uses and cannot catch the mode mismatch. This contradicts quality-pass row 367's claim that these are "hand-computed Decimals."

WHY NEEDS-DECISION not CONFIRMED-as-clean-fix: the paycheck path's per-period gross is NOT (salary/26).quantize() -- _gross_biweekly_for_period (paycheck_calculator.py:447-538) distributes a floor+residue so per-period grosses vary (e.g. 1923.07 vs 1923.08) and percentages are taken against THAT. The investment path uses one flat (salary/26).quantize() for every period, so it already diverges structurally from the actual paycheck deduction and was never cent-exact. The rounding-mode inconsistency is a real, additional violation of the explicit money standard, but whether the right fix is "add ROUND_HALF_UP" (closes the half-cent gap but the flat-gross approximation remains) or a broader reconciliation is a financial/design judgment.

ALREADY KNOWN = false: quality-pass rows 363-368 reviewed only refactor behavior-equivalence vs the pre-refactor monolith and flagged only the negative-deduction P-3 comment. Cross-path rounding-mode consistency between investment and paycheck was never assessed. Distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction).

### 19. [DECIMAL/DEFECT] Money values quantized with implicit ROUND_HALF_EVEN (banker's rounding) instead of round_money
- **Location:** `app/services/retirement_dashboard_service.py; app/routes/investment.py; app/services/investment_projection.py; app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py` :: retirement_dashboard_service.py:629,632,682; routes/investment.py:200; investment_projection.py:98,101,173; investment_dashboard_service.py:292,295,388
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** app/utils/money.py:8-11 mandates ROUND_HALF_UP and explicitly forbids a bare '.quantize(Decimal("0.01"))' as 'a silent source of one-cent drift ... must never be reached implicitly'. Yet retirement_dashboard_service.py:629 ('final_gross_biweekly = (final_salary / (...)).quantize(Decimal("0.01"))'), :632, :682, routes/investment.py:200 ('transfer_amount = (limit / _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR).quantize(TWO_PLACES)'), and investment_projection.py:98 all quantize monetary Decimals with NO rounding= argument, so they use Python's default ROUND_HALF_EVEN. routes/investment.py:200 is the amount of a recurring transfer that gets persisted; retirement_dashboard_service.py:629/632 feed further computation (final_gross_biweekly * effective_take_home_rate).
- **Why it matters:** At a half-cent boundary banker's rounding and ROUND_HALF_UP disagree by a cent, so the same dollar value computed here vs through round_money elsewhere can differ by $0.01. For a persisted transfer amount (routes/investment.py:200) that cent drift compounds across every pay period of a projection and contradicts the project-wide hand-computed-test rounding convention.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace each bare '.quantize(Decimal("0.01"))'/'.quantize(TWO_PLACES)' on a monetary value with 'round_money(...)' from app.utils.money (which forces ROUND_HALF_UP).
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE (verified line-for-line): every cited monetary quantize is BARE (no rounding= arg -> Python default ROUND_HALF_EVEN). retirement_dashboard_service.py:629 `(final_salary / (profile.pay_periods_per_year or 26)).quantize(Decimal("0.01"))`, :632 `(final_gross_biweekly * effective_take_home_rate).quantize(Decimal("0.01"))`, :682 (chart). routes/investment.py:200 `(limit / _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` with TWO_PLACES=Decimal("0.01") (line 51). investment_projection.py:98 `(salary / pay_per_year).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, :101 `(gross * amt).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, :173. investment_dashboard_service.py:292/295/388 (TWO_PLACES local at :68). money.py:8-11 docstring explicitly: ROUND_HALF_EVEN "is a silent source of one-cent drift ... and must never be reached implicitly through a bare `.quantize(Decimal(\"0.01\"))`"; round_money (money.py:45-72) forces ROUND_HALF_UP. grep confirms the project-wide convention is explicit ROUND_HALF_UP: pension_calculator, paycheck_calculator, calibration_service, savings_goal_service, spending_trend_service, budget_variance_service all pass rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP; round_money is the established helper used across loan/balance/savings/year-end. The investment files are the outliers (none import round_money).

REAL ISSUE: divergence reachable with realistic inputs -- $95,000 salary -> gross (95000/26).quantize=3653.85; 3653.85*Decimal("0.10")=365.385 -> HALF_EVEN 365.38 (current code) vs HALF_UP 365.39 (project convention). Load-bearing, not display-only, at 3 sites: routes/investment.py:200 -> template default_amount (line 223) -> generate_transfers_for_all_periods (line 233) -> db.session.commit (line 235): a PERSISTED recurring transfer amount. retirement_dashboard_service.py:629/632: return of _compute_gap_net_biweekly -> gap_net_biweekly (:278) -> net_biweekly_pay (:292) into the retirement gap calculator (computed, not display). investment_projection.py:98/101/173: per-period gross/contribution feeding the growth projection. (investment_dashboard_service.py:292/295 wrap str(...) for chart data attrs and :388 is a UI pre-fill suggestion -- weaker, display-boundary; finding over-broad there but core sites stand.)

TEST GAP (confirms uncovered): tests assert expected with the SAME bare quantize as the code under test -- test_investment_projection.py:116-117 `gross=(Decimal("100000")/26).quantize(Decimal("0.01")); expected=(gross*Decimal("0.07")).quantize(Decimal("0.01"))`, also :154, :272, :337-338, :542-543, :671-672. These tautologically mirror production rounding and cannot detect a HALF_EVEN/HALF_UP divergence; they would lock in the wrong mode.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: quality-pass.md rows 4/5/18/20 reviewed these files for refactor behavior-equivalence and rounding ORDER (whole-expression quantize, lines 352/363) but never dispositioned the rounding-MODE inconsistency. Not P-1 (loan escrow) nor P-3 (negative deduction; that # BUG at test:340/345 is a distinct issue). No pylint disable on any cited quantize line (grep confirmed: disables present are only duplicate-code at investment.py:154 and too-many-args at investment_projection.py:241).

Severity corrected HIGH->MED: divergence is exactly $0.01 and requires an input landing on an exact half-cent boundary; the most damaging site (persisted transfer) is a UX-suggested default the user can override and a $0.01/period drift, real but bounded. The fix (swap bare quantize for round_money at the computed/persisted sites; decide whether display-str sites also convert) is the recommended remediation aligned with the mandated convention.

### 20. [DRY/DEFECT] Savings-goal percent-funded computed by two divergent rules (truncate+no-lower-clamp vs canonical percent_complete)
- **Location:** `app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_goals.py` :: 119-124
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** _build_goal_datum computes progress_pct = min(100, int(acct_balance / resolved_target * 100)) -- int() TRUNCATES toward zero and there is no lower clamp -- while the budget dashboard's equivalent savings-goal card computes the same 'percent funded' via app.utils.money.percent_complete (dashboard_service.py:553), which ROUND_HALF_UPs and clamps to [0,100] returning a Decimal. money.py:106-133's docstring explicitly claims percent_complete is 'the single numeric contract behind every percent funded / progress-bar surface', yet this site bypasses it. progress_pct is rendered as both the progress-bar width and the '% complete' label (savings/dashboard.html:374,380).
- **Why it matters:** Two screens show different numbers for the same goal: a goal 99.6% funded shows '99% complete' on the savings dashboard but '99.60%' (rounded) on the budget dashboard. A negative projected balance yields a negative progress_pct here (no lower clamp), rendering a negative-width/negative-label bar, whereas percent_complete clamps to 0. This is exactly the one-sided-drift risk the centralization exists to prevent.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the inline min/int expression with progress_pct = percent_complete(acct_balance, resolved_target) so both savings surfaces share the canonical clamped, HALF_UP rule.
- **Verifier evidence:** CONFIRMED -- semantic duplication of the "percent funded" rule with a divergent shape (R0801-invisible).

factually_accurate: app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_goals.py:119-124 computes `progress_pct = min(100, int(acct_balance / resolved_target * 100))` -- `int()` truncates toward zero, there is NO lower clamp, and it returns a plain int. The budget dashboard's equivalent card at app/services/dashboard_service.py:553 uses `percent_complete(current, target)` which (app/utils/money.py:126-133) divides, `.quantize(CENTS, ROUND_HALF_UP)`, and clamps to [0,100], returning a Decimal. money.py:109-110 docstring explicitly calls percent_complete "the single numeric contract behind every 'percent funded' / progress-bar surface." progress_pct is rendered as both the bar width (app/templates/savings/dashboard.html:374-375) and the "% complete" label (line 380). All cited facts check out.

is_real_issue: YES. (1) Truncation-vs-round divergence is always present, not edge-only: a goal 99.6% funded yields 99 here (int(99.6)) but percent_complete returns Decimal("99.60") on the budget dashboard, where _savings_goals.html:20 `{:.0f}.format` renders it "100%". Same goal, two screens, "99% complete" vs "100%", and the bar width differs 99 vs 99.60. (2) Missing lower clamp: I traced acct_balance to _goal_account_balance -> account_data current_balance -> _projections.py:_compute_base_balances:107-110 (`balances.get(current_period.id)` from balance_calculator/balance_resolver), which can be negative (overdrawn/projected-negative savings), producing a negative progress_pct and a negative-width/negative-label bar, whereas percent_complete clamps to 0. plan.md:2239 confirms percent_complete was created specifically to dedupe dashboard `_safe_pct_complete` + entry_service `pct_complete`; this third site was missed -- the exact one-sided-drift the centralization exists to prevent. NOT gold-plating (rule 13) -- the negative case is reachable, and the round-vs-truncate gap is unconditional.

already_known: NO. quality-pass.md row 6 (savings_dashboard_service pkg) records only "M2: untyped params bag, built-then-patched" -- it does not mention progress_pct, int()-truncation, the missing lower clamp, or the percent_complete divergence. Not a documented disable; not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction).

Note for the fix: replacing the inline expr with `percent_complete(acct_balance, resolved_target)` flips the return type int->Decimal, so the tests asserting int values (tests/test_services/test_savings_dashboard_service.py:169 `== 50`, :313/:419 `== 0`, :389 `> 0`) and the template `gd.progress_pct >= 100` / `< 100` comparisons (savings/dashboard.html:372, 405) must be updated to the Decimal contract. That ripple is a legitimate behavior-clarification (rule 5), not a reason to keep the divergent rule. Severity MED upheld: display-percentage only (no stored/transacted money), but a genuine cross-surface inconsistency plus a reachable negative-render.

### 21. [SECURITY/DEFECT] Cross-user start_period_id persisted unchecked for all non-EVERY_N recurring patterns (recurrence-rule IDOR)
- **Location:** `app/routes/_recurrence_form_helpers.py` :: 234-250
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-idor
- **Claim:** In build_recurrence_rule_from_form, the ownership check on start_period_id (lines 236-238: db.session.get(PayPeriod, start_period_id) then start_period.user_id != user_id) runs ONLY inside the `if int(pattern_id_str) == every_n_id and start_period_id and interval_n:` branch (line 234). For every other recurring pattern (MONTHLY, QUARTERLY, SEMI_ANNUAL, ANNUAL, EVERY_PERIOD) the submitted start_period_id is written verbatim into rule_kwargs['start_period_id'] (line 250) with no owner check. recurrence_engine.py then dereferences rule.start_period.start_date (lines 117-118 and 260-261) to derive effective_from, so a victim's pay-period start date drives the attacker's generation window. Both create routes feed user-controlled start_period_id straight into this helper: app/routes/templates.py:282-301 (create_template) and app/routes/transfers/templates.py:174-194 (create_transfer_template).
- **Why it matters:** Violates the project ownership-scoping rule and the 404-for-not-yours contract: an authenticated owner can store a RecurrenceRule that references another user's PayPeriod and have the recurrence engine read that victim row's start_date, leaking pay-period structure and silently coupling the attacker's recurring rule to a foreign period. The read-only preview path (templates.py:766-773) already guards this for all patterns, so the persist path is inconsistent with the path that is supposed to mirror it.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the start_period ownership probe out of the EVERY_N-only branch so any non-None start_period_id is verified (db.session.get + user_id == user_id, 404/redirect on failure) before it is written to rule_kwargs, for every pattern.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUAL ACCURACY -- every cited code claim verified by reading the committed files:
- app/routes/_recurrence_form_helpers.py:234-241: the start_period ownership probe (db.session.get(PayPeriod, start_period_id) then start_period.user_id != user_id, flash + redirect) lives ONLY inside `if (int(pattern_id_str) == every_n_id and start_period_id and interval_n):`. Verified.
- Line 250: rule_kwargs["start_period_id"] = start_period_id is written verbatim for every pattern, after the EVERY_N-only block. Verified.
- app/services/recurrence_engine.py:117-118 (_resolve_generation_plan) and 260-261 (can_generate_in_period) both do `effective_from = rule.start_period.start_date` when effective_from is None and start_period_id is set. Verified. match_periods (line 467) uses effective_from as the candidate cutoff: `candidates = [p for p in periods if p.end_date >= effective_from]`.
- Both create routes feed user-controlled start_period_id straight in: app/routes/templates.py:282-301 (start_period_id = data.pop(...); build_recurrence_rule_from_form(..., start_period_id=start_period_id)) and app/routes/transfers/templates.py:174-194. Verified.
- Preview path app/routes/templates.py:766-773 guards ownership for ALL patterns (comment cites "audit finding H3"), confirming the persist path is inconsistent with the read path. Verified.

REAL ISSUE -- not intended/safe/test-covered:
- Schema accepts it unchecked: app/schemas/validation.py:348 and :1017 declare `start_period_id = fields.Integer()` with no ownership validator; a raw POST can carry any id under any pattern (the form's d-none JS gating does not bind a crafted request).
- NOT test-covered: tests/test_routes/test_recurrence_form_helpers.py C2-3 (line 137) and C2-4 (line 188) exercise start_period ownership ONLY for EVERY_N_PERIODS, and C2-4 uses a NONEXISTENT id (99_999_999), never a cross-user id under a non-EVERY_N pattern. grep of tests/ found no cross-user start_period_id coverage.
- Real downstream effect: create_template (templates.py:321-323) and the transfers `elif rule:` branch (transfers/templates.py:662-664 -> generate_transfers_for_all_periods -> transfer_recurrence.generate_for_template:65-68 -> _resolve_generation_plan) both call the engine WITHOUT explicit effective_from, so a foreign rule.start_period.start_date drives the attacker's generation boundary against the attacker's OWN periods (templates.py:320 get_all_periods(current_user.id)). The transfers docstring at transfers/templates.py:142-152 explicitly claims "a malicious start_period_id cannot leak into the transfer service," but proves it only for the ONCE re-fetch branch (_materialize_initial_transfers:624-632); the recurring non-ONCE non-EVERY_N path bypasses that re-check -- the exact gap.

ALREADY KNOWN -- no:
- H3 (docs/audits/security-2026-04-15/reports/02a-routes.md:739) covered only the preview/READ path; the persist path gap is not in that fix.
- Not in the quality-pass register (quality-pass.md:336 ACCEPTs _build_preview_rule, a different concern), not a documented disable, not P-1/P-3. The F-24 remediation plan (remediation_follow_up_F24_F25_F26_plan.md:566-574) carried the EVERY_N-only check forward "to preserve pre-extraction behaviour exactly" -- the gap was inherited, not consciously accepted.

SEVERITY -- corrected HIGH->MED: this is an IDOR-shaped stored cross-user FK plus an inferential boundary leak (the attacker stores a foreign PayPeriod reference and the engine reads its start_date as a date threshold over the attacker's own periods), not a direct disclosure of the victim's row. Same class as the already-fixed H3, which the team treated as worth fixing -- so the persist path inconsistency is a genuine standing defect, but the impact is inference/coupling rather than data exfiltration.

NEEDS-DECISION rationale: the developer's own committed docstring (transfers/templates.py:142-152) asserts the current behaviour is safe, so confirming this requires the developer to overturn that stated assumption; the fix location (hoist the probe out of the EVERY_N branch vs. add it at the route boundary like the other FKs) and whether an inferential boundary leak warrants a fix are design judgments to make explicitly.

### 22. [TEST-QUALITY/DEFECT] Route-layer envelope-on-income fallback (_is_tracking_on_non_expense) has no covering route test
- **Location:** `app/routes/templates.py` :: 102-170
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** The schema test test_update_schema_partial_payload_skips_check_when_type_absent (tests/test_routes/test_template_flags.py:773-786) deliberately loads {"is_envelope":"on"} with NO transaction_type_id and asserts the schema validator returns early, documenting that the route is responsible for enforcement via _is_tracking_on_non_expense. But every route-level rejection test (test_template_flags.py:320-352, test_templates.py:1759-1803) ALWAYS includes transaction_type_id in the POST body, so the schema validator (not the route fallback) does the rejection. No route test POSTs is_envelope='on' without transaction_type_id against a stored income template, so the live getattr(template,'transaction_type_id') branch of _is_tracking_on_non_expense (templates.py:125-129) is never exercised.
- **Why it matters:** This is the explicit defense-in-depth path the schema defers to. If the route fallback regressed (e.g. the getattr default flipped, or the check were dropped), the suite would stay green while a user could silently attach envelope/carry-forward semantics to an income template via a partial update, corrupting carry-forward rollover math on income flows.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a route test that POSTs to /templates/<id> of a stored income template with is_envelope='on' and NO transaction_type_id field, asserting the 'expense templates' rejection and unchanged is_envelope.
- **Verifier evidence:** Attempted to refute; could not. The finding is accurate on every point.

ROUTE FALLBACK EXISTS AND IS THE SOLE ENFORCER ON THE PARTIAL-TYPE-ABSENT PATH:
- app/routes/templates.py:102-129 `_is_tracking_on_non_expense`: when `transaction_type_id` is absent from the payload it reads `getattr(template, "transaction_type_id", None)` (line 125-128) and rejects if `type_id != EXPENSE` (line 129). This is the exact branch the finding cites.
- app/schemas/validation.py:189-195 `_reject_envelope_on_income`: returns early when `txn_type_id is None` (line 192-193). So a payload with is_envelope on and NO transaction_type_id passes the schema; only the route fallback can catch it.
- Route order confirms reachability: app/routes/templates.py:376-379 runs `_update_schema.validate(request.form)` and early-returns on errors; only if the schema passes does line 451 call `_validate_template_form(..., template=template)`, which invokes `_is_tracking_on_non_expense` (line 167). When `transaction_type_id` IS present with income type, the schema rejects first and the fallback never runs.

EVERY EXISTING ROUTE REJECTION TEST INCLUDES transaction_type_id (so they hit the schema, not the fallback):
- tests/test_routes/test_template_flags.py:296-318 and 320-352 build the POST via `_base_form_data(...)`, which always sets `transaction_type_id` (helper at lines 57-79, the field is set at line 75).
- tests/test_routes/test_templates.py:1756-1803 posts an explicit dict that includes `"transaction_type_id": income_type.id` (line 1790).

THE ONLY ABSENT-TYPE TEST IS SCHEMA-LEVEL, NOT A ROUTE TEST:
- tests/test_routes/test_template_flags.py:773-786 `test_update_schema_partial_payload_skips_check_when_type_absent` calls `schema.load({"is_envelope":"on"})` directly and asserts the validator returns early; it never goes through `auth_client.post` and never asserts rejection. Its own docstring (lines 776-786) says "the route layer is responsible for the existing-template fallback."
- grep for `_is_tracking_on_non_expense` across tests/ finds it only in that test's docstring/comment (lines 778, 786) -- never in a route POST.

So the live `getattr(template,"transaction_type_id")` rejection branch (templates.py:127-129) has zero route coverage. A regression there (default flip, or dropping the check) would keep the full suite green while letting a partial update attach envelope/carry-forward semantics to a stored income template, corrupting expense-only carry-forward rollover on an income flow. The fix (a route POST of is_envelope='on' with no transaction_type_id against a stored income template, asserting the 'expense templates' flash and unchanged is_envelope) is non-controversial, so this is a straightforward test-quality gap, not a NEEDS-DECISION judgment call. Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable, not in the quality-pass ACCEPT rows. Severity MED stands: schema covers the normal full-form path, so live exposure needs a narrower partial-update vector, but the consequence is financial.

### 23. [TEST-QUALITY/DEFECT] No test covers cross-user category_id on POST /transactions (the F1 IDOR path)
- **Location:** `tests/test_routes/test_transaction_auth.py` :: 257-271 (inline test) vs 273-315 (POST /transactions tests)
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** The suite has `test_inline_create_with_other_users_category` for POST /transactions/inline (test_transaction_auth.py:257) and cross-user tests for POST /transactions covering pay_period_id (273) and scenario_id (290), plus `test_create_with_nonexistent_category_id` returning 400 (392) -- but there is NO test asserting POST /transactions with ANOTHER USER's (valid) category_id returns 404. The nonexistent-category test passes via IntegrityError, which masks the IDOR because a real foreign category never triggers IntegrityError. This missing case is exactly why F1 shipped undetected.
- **Why it matters:** The category IDOR on the ad-hoc create route is the one cross-user FK with no regression test, so the gate that protects every other create FK does not protect this one. A solo-maintained app with no human reviewer relies on these tests as the only safeguard.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `test_create_with_other_users_category` mirroring `test_create_with_other_users_period` but submitting `other["category"].id`, asserting 404 and that no transaction was created.
- **Verifier evidence:** I tried to refute this and could not -- every claim verifies against the committed code.

FACTUAL ACCURACY (all cited lines confirmed):
- tests/test_routes/test_transaction_auth.py:257-271 = test_inline_create_with_other_users_category, POSTs other["category"].id to /transactions/inline and asserts 404. Exists as claimed.
- POST /transactions cross-user tests cover pay_period_id (test_create_with_other_users_period, line 273) and scenario_id (test_create_with_other_users_scenario_id, line 290). Confirmed.
- test_create_with_nonexistent_category_id (line 392) POSTs category_id=999999 (nonexistent) to /transactions and asserts status_code == 400 (line 410). Confirmed -- it passes via IntegrityError, NOT a 404 ownership probe.
- Grepped the entire tests/ tree: no test POSTs another user's VALID category_id to POST /transactions. The c27 cross-user category tests (test_c27_input_validation_sweep.py:459/497/621/702) all target /transfers/* routes, not POST /transactions. So no regression test exists for the ad-hoc-create category IDOR.

THE GAP REFLECTS A REAL UNDERLYING DEFECT (the "F1" IDOR):
- app/routes/transactions/create.py:121-125 (create_transaction) calls _resolve_owned_fks with ONLY Account, PayPeriod, Scenario -- it omits Category, with the comment (lines 119-120) "this route carries no category." That comment is FALSE: app/schemas/validation.py:250 declares category_id = fields.Integer(required=True) on TransactionCreateSchema, and create.py:133 does Transaction(**data), so category_id IS loaded and written.
- By contrast create_inline (create.py:75-83) DOES include (Category, ..., "Category not found") in its probe. The two sibling create routes are asymmetric -- only the inline one ownership-checks the category.
- app/models/transaction.py:162-164: category_id is a nullable FK with ondelete="SET NULL" and there is no cross-user CHECK constraint. So an existing-but-foreign category_id satisfies the FK (row exists) and is persisted with NO IntegrityError. This exactly confirms the finding's mechanism: the nonexistent-id test (400 via IntegrityError) cannot catch a real foreign category, which would silently succeed as a 201. The IDOR is genuine and untested on this route.

ALREADY-KNOWN CHECK: Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). Not in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md -- the "F1" strings there are rubric-dimension labels ("F1. Would a plausible next feature slot in"), unrelated. No documented disable involved. This is a new finding.

VERDICT: CONFIRMED. The missing test is real and high-value because it would have caught a live cross-user FK write. MED severity is correct: the test gap is the surface, but it sits on top of an actual IDOR in create_transaction (omitted Category probe + wrong "carries no category" comment), so fixing it should be paired with adding Category to _resolve_owned_fks in create.py. Suggested fix (add test_create_with_other_users_category mirroring the period test, asserting 404 + no transaction created) is correct.

### 24. [TEST-QUALITY/DEFECT] start_period_id IDOR tests cover only the safe paths (ONCE and the Every-Period preview), giving false confidence the persist path is guarded
- **Location:** `tests/test_routes/test_transfers.py` :: 1796-1827
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-idor
- **Claim:** test_one_time_transfer_idor_period (test_transfers.py:1796-1819) exercises the cross-user start_period_id case ONLY for the ONCE pattern (the pattern fetched at lines 1803-1805), which is the one path actually re-checked in _materialize_initial_transfers (transfers/templates.py:624-632). No test posts a cross-user start_period_id with a recurring pattern (monthly/quarterly/annual/every-period), i.e. the unguarded persist path from F1. On the templates side, test_preview_rejects_other_users_start_period (test_templates.py:825-860) asserts only against /templates/preview-recurrence with the Every-Period pattern, whose preview branch never dereferences start_period, and asserts byte-equality with the baseline -- so it passes regardless of whether the create/persist path checks ownership. The docstring's claim that 'the ownership check caused the foreign period to be ignored' is not what the asserted code path proves.
- **Why it matters:** The existing tests make the start_period IDOR look closed across all patterns while the create-time persist path (F1) is actually open for every non-EVERY_N recurring pattern. A reviewer relying on these tests would wrongly conclude the boundary is enforced.
- **Suggested fix:** Add create-route tests that POST a recurring (e.g. monthly) template AND transfer template with another user's start_period_id and assert the rule is rejected (or start_period_id not persisted) rather than only testing ONCE and the Every-Period preview.
- **Verifier evidence:** All material claims verified by reading the actual code (note: the finding's path "app/services/transfers/templates.py" is a typo -- the real file is app/routes/transfers/templates.py; the function and line numbers match exactly).

COVERAGE GAP (the finding's core, all confirmed):
- tests/test_routes/test_transfers.py:1796-1827 (test_one_time_transfer_idor_period): fetches the ONCE pattern (line 1803-1805 filter_by(name="Once")) and posts recurrence_pattern=once.id (line 1813) with seed_second_periods[0].id as start_period_id (line 1815). Asserts b"Invalid pay period" (1819) and xfer_count==0 (1827). Exercises ONLY the ONCE branch.
- The ONCE re-check is _materialize_initial_transfers (app/routes/transfers/templates.py:624-632): `if is_one_time and start_period_id:` re-fetches the period (628) and rejects when period.user_id != current_user.id (629-632). This is the path the test covers.
- tests/test_routes/test_templates.py:825-860 (test_preview_rejects_other_users_start_period): hits ONLY GET /templates/preview-recurrence with the Every-Period pattern (838-840) and asserts resp.data == baseline_resp.data (860). Byte-equality with a no-start_period baseline cannot prove anything about the create/persist path.
- Exhaustive grep of the whole suite for seed_second_periods + start_period_id confirms NO test posts a cross-user start_period_id with a recurring (monthly/quarterly/annual/EVERY_N) pattern through a create route. test_create_template_with_recurrence (test_templates.py:215-241) sends no start_period_id at all. test_c29_cross_user_fk.py covers update_transaction PATCH (pay_period_id), a different route/mechanism.

UNDERLYING HOLE IS REAL (makes the gap meaningful):
- app/routes/_recurrence_form_helpers.py:250 persists start_period_id onto the RecurrenceRule UNCONDITIONALLY for every pattern.
- The ownership check (lines 234-241) is gated on `int(pattern_id_str) == every_n_id` -- so for monthly/quarterly/annual recurring patterns a foreign start_period_id is persisted with NO ownership verification (schema validation.py:1017 is a bare fields.Integer(), no ownership check, correctly).
- app/services/recurrence_engine.py:117-118 and 260-261 then dereference rule.start_period.start_date as the effective_from generation boundary -- so a foreign period both joins another user's PayPeriod row and shifts generation timing.

MINOR IMPRECISION (does not undermine the finding): the finding says the preview branch "never dereferences start_period," but preview_recurrence (app/routes/templates.py:768) does db.session.get(PayPeriod, ...) then ownership-gates its use at line 772. The net behavior the finding relies on (foreign period ignored -> baseline-equal output) is still correct.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: quality-pass.md line 336 accepts _build_preview_rule for code-quality (relocation), not this test gap; not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction).

### 25. [TEST-QUALITY/DEFECT] No test asserts schedule rows equal the recorded recast in a future ARM period, leaving F1 uncovered
- **Location:** `tests/test_services/test_loan_resolver.py` :: 805-854 (test_arm_second_period_uses_recorded_recast_held_constant)
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** loan-amort
- **Claim:** test_arm_second_period_uses_recorded_recast_held_constant constructs exactly the recorded-recast future-period scenario (monthly_pi=$2500.00) but only asserts state_early.monthly_payment == Decimal('2500.00') (line 847) -- the loan-card scalar. It never asserts that any row in state.schedule whose payment_date falls in [2031-01-01, ...) carries payment==$2500.00. Because LoanState.schedule is assembled from project_forward (which ignores monthly_pi, see F1), the schedule rows are actually $2582.13, but the test passes anyway.
- **Why it matters:** The test's name and docstring claim it exercises 'the recorded-recast path end to end through resolve_loan', giving false confidence that the schedule honors the recorded recast. The one assertion that would catch the F1 divergence is absent, so the bug ships green. This is the assertion gap that lets a chart/summary divergence -- the precise failure mode the architecture was built to prevent -- go undetected.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an assertion that the first projected schedule row in the second period has payment == Decimal('2500.00') (and interest_rate == 0.07), which will fail until F1 is fixed.
- **Verifier evidence:** CONFIRMED. Every claim in F2 verified against the actual code, and the underlying divergence reproduced empirically.

1) The test (tests/test_services/test_loan_resolver.py:805-854) constructs exactly the recorded-recast future-period scenario: 5/5 ARM $400k/6%/360mo, rate change 2031-01-01 -> 7% with monthly_pi=Decimal("2500.00") (lines 831-836), as_of dates 2032-06-01 / 2035-06-01 inside the second period. Its ONLY assertions are: state_early.monthly_payment == Decimal("2500.00") (line 847), the cross-as_of equality (848), and state_p0.monthly_payment == Decimal("2398.20") (854). Confirmed by reading: NO assertion touches state.schedule. grep of the whole file (\.schedule / 2582 / 2500) shows the only .schedule assertions in this module are the is_confirmed-flag tests at 924/966 (fixed-rate loan, no ARM, no rate change) -- F1 is uncovered.

2) Root cause is real. LoanState.schedule = history_rows + committed_forward from compute_payoff_scenarios (_state.py:218-225). The forward slice is project_forward (_payoff.py:432-436). project_forward recasts at a rate change via _recast_for_rate_change (amortization_engine.py:486-518), which calls calculate_monthly_payment(state.balance, period_rate, months_left) -- it RE-AMORTIZES and never reads RateChangeRecord.monthly_pi. The recorded $2500 recast is honored ONLY by build_rate_periods -> RatePeriod.period_pi (rate_period_engine.py:478-484), which drives the scalar state.monthly_payment (_state.py:242), not the schedule rows.

3) Reproduced the exact divergence by running the test's scenario: state_early.monthly_payment = 2500.00 (the asserted scalar), but the second-period schedule rows carry payment=2582.13 (interest_rate=0.07), e.g. first second-period row 2031-01-01 payment=2582.13; rows 2030-11/12 are 2500.00 then 2031-01 jumps to 2582.13. distinct second-period payments = {2582.13, 2582.81(final residue)}. So the loan card ($2500) and the schedule ($2582.13) diverge -- precisely the chart/summary divergence the architecture (PayoffScenarios docstring _payoff.py:49-53) was built to prevent. The suggested assertion (first second-period row payment == 2500.00, rate 0.07) would fail today.

4) Confirmed the test currently PASSES green (./scripts/test.sh ... ::test_arm_second_period_uses_recorded_recast_held_constant -> 1 passed), so the bug ships undetected, matching why_it_matters.

5) already_known = NO. Not P-1 (escrow threshold docstring) nor P-3 (negative deduction). Not a documented disable nor a quality-pass ACCEPT row (quality-pass.md only covers _replay_from_anchor DRY @195/346 and the project_forward DECOMPOSITION @plan.md:2248 asserting "behavior bit-identical" -- neither touches recorded-recast forward rows). The "scalar-vs-schedule rate divergence (ARM)" in 04_source_of_truth.md:834 is a DISTINCT, pre-rate-period-engine issue: a RATE mirror mismatch (interest_rate vs RateHistory via _find_applicable_rate); F1/F2 is a PAYMENT-AMOUNT mismatch at the SAME rate (0.07 on both sides). remediation_follow_up.md F-8 is fixed-rate trueups, not this.

Verdict CONFIRMED (test gap is real and unique). Severity kept MED: it is a test-quality finding, but it is the assertion gap masking a genuine financial-correctness divergence. Note: whether the correct fix is making project_forward honor the recorded recast P&I in forward rows, or making the scalar match the re-amortized schedule, is the F1 design call for the developer; the F2 test assertion itself is mechanical once that is decided.

### 26. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Amount/category/period edits allowed on a settled (paid) transaction or transfer with no immutability guard
- **Location:** `app/routes/transactions/mutations.py` :: 169-247 (_apply_regular_update); parity in transfers/mutations.py:382-415
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** In `_apply_regular_update` the status-transition guard (`_resolve_status_change`) runs ONLY when `status_id` is present in the payload (mutations.py:137-138). A PATCH that changes `estimated_amount`/`actual_amount`/`category_id`/`pay_period_id` WITHOUT a status_id goes straight to the unguarded `setattr` loop (mutations.py:217-218) and commits, even when the row is already Settled/Received/Done/Cancelled. The transfer service mirrors this: `_apply_status_change` only calls `verify_transition` when status_id changes (transfer_service.py:524-525), so amount-only edits on a settled transfer are likewise unguarded. There is no `is_immutable`/`is_settled` precondition on either edit path (grep of transaction.py shows no immutability property used by the route).
- **Why it matters:** A user (or replayed/stale form) can silently rewrite the dollar amount of an already-paid transaction or transfer, retroactively shifting the projected balance and the audit trail of a settled money movement -- the kind of after-the-fact mutation the settled status is meant to lock. Needs domain confirmation: if post-settlement corrections are intended, the behavior should at least be explicit and tested.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide the policy: if settled rows are immutable, add a guard (reject estimated/category/period edits when `txn.status.is_settled`) in both `_apply_regular_update` and the transfer update path; otherwise document the intentional editability and add a test pinning it.
- **Verifier evidence:** Could not refute -- the code confirms the claim on every cited point.

FACTUALLY ACCURATE:
- app/routes/transactions/mutations.py:137-138: `_resolve_status_change` returns `(False, None)` immediately when `"status_id" not in data`. So a PATCH with only estimated_amount/actual_amount/category_id/pay_period_id skips `verify_transition` entirely.
- mutations.py:216-218: unguarded `for field, value in data.items(): setattr(txn, field, value)`, then commit (229). No is_immutable/is_settled precondition anywhere in `_apply_regular_update`. The only `is_immutable` mention in the file is a comment at line 489 inside `_mark_done_regular`, not a guard on the edit path.
- Transfer mirror: transfer_service.py:617-622 applies an amount change with no transition check; `verify_transition` lives only in `_apply_status_change` (transfer_service.py:525), which `update_transfer` calls only when `"status_id" in kwargs` (transfer_service.py:628). Amount/period/category-only transfer edits are likewise unguarded. (Finding cited lines 524-525/382-415; actual lines 525/617-622 -- substance is correct.)
- TransactionUpdateSchema (app/schemas/validation.py:220-224) and TransferUpdateSchema accept estimated_amount/actual_amount/category_id/pay_period_id independently of status_id, so an amount-only PATCH validates and reaches the setattr loop.

REAL ISSUE + DESIGN-INTENT CONFLICT:
- The state machine documents settled rows as terminal/immutable: state_machine.py:17 ("settled -> settled (terminal -- archived rows cannot be mutated)") and 115-118 ("Terminal: a Settled row must not be mutated"). After mark_done an expense is "Paid" which seeds is_settled=True AND is_immutable=True (app/ref_seeds.py:94-98).
- The amount edit shifts the balance: Transaction.effective_amount (app/models/transaction.py:243-248) returns actual_amount or estimated_amount for all non-excluded statuses including settled, so rewriting either field on a settled row retroactively changes the projected checking balance and the audit record of a completed movement.
- Reachable through the normal UI, not just a crafted request: app/templates/grid/_transaction_quick_edit.html:8-18 PATCHes estimated_amount with no settled-row gating, and _transaction_full_edit.html:16-50 renders the amount input + a free status dropdown unconditionally.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION (not CONFIRMED bug):
- is_immutable's documented contract is narrow: "the recurrence engine must not overwrite this transaction" (app/models/ref.py:197-199), not "the user may not edit it." C-21 (state_machine.py:48-53) deliberately scoped enforcement to status TRANSITIONS and called the broader rollout out of scope.
- An existing test incidentally pins the current allow-edit behavior: tests/test_routes/test_grid.py:4513-4534 (test_paid_at_preserved_on_non_status_update) marks a row done, then PATCHes estimated_amount=200.00 and asserts 200 OK. Its stated purpose is paid_at preservation, not "settled rows are editable," so it is not an explicit accepted policy -- but it does mean the behavior is partially tested rather than wholly unexpected.
- No documented policy resolves whether post-settlement field corrections are intended (the roadmap "course correction" text at project_roadmap_v4-5.md.md:1197 concerns seasonal-forecast actual capture, not arbitrary settled-row editing).

ALREADY KNOWN: no -- not a documented disable, not a quality-pass ACCEPT row, and distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction). Ownership/IDOR is enforced (mutations.py:316 _verify_owned_fks_in_update; transfer route loop at 119-122), so this is an owner mutating their own settled data, not a cross-user issue. The correct fix (settled rows field-immutable vs. an intentional, documented, and explicitly-tested post-settlement correction path) is a financial/design judgment for the developer.

### 27. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] authenticate() runs bcrypt only for existing accounts, leaking account existence via response-time side channel despite the constant-message design
- **Location:** `app/services/auth_service.py` :: 646-657
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** auth-sec
- **Claim:** When `db.session.query(User).filter_by(email=email).first()` returns None (line 646-648) the function raises AuthError immediately WITHOUT calling verify_password, so no bcrypt work occurs. When the email exists but the password is wrong (line 657) verify_password runs a full bcrypt.checkpw. The wrong-password path is therefore measurably slower (tens of ms of bcrypt) than the unknown-email path. The docstring (lines 599-601) and module design only neutralize the message-content enumeration oracle ('same generic message'), not this timing oracle. No dummy/throwaway bcrypt hash is computed on the no-user branch to equalize timing.
- **Why it matters:** An attacker can probe which emails have accounts by timing /login responses, which is exactly the enumeration vector the generic-message design claims to close. The per-account lockout caps but does not eliminate this (a handful of timed samples per email suffice before any lockout). For a solo-operated money app the enumerated email set is a phishing/credential-stuffing target.
- **Suggested fix:** On the user-is-None branch, run verify_password(password, <a fixed valid bcrypt dummy hash>) and discard the result so both branches pay the bcrypt cost before raising the identical AuthError.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/services/auth_service.py:646-697 and verify_password at 574-591. The claim is factually exact: line 646-648 does `user = db.session.query(User).filter_by(email=email).first(); if user is None: raise AuthError("Invalid email or password.")` and returns BEFORE any bcrypt work. The wrong-password path at line 657 calls `verify_password`, which at line 579 runs `bcrypt.checkpw(...)` -- tens of ms of cost. No dummy/throwaway bcrypt hash is computed on the no-user branch (grep for "dummy" in the module returns nothing). The function docstring (599-601) neutralizes only the CONTENT oracle ("via response content"), not timing.

Timing-awareness is provably present yet selectively applied: the locked-account branch (652-655) deliberately skips bcrypt and the docstring (604-607) states this is precisely "so an attacker observing response timing cannot ... use a lockout window as a side-channel oracle." The same authors did NOT equalize the no-user branch, leaving the enumeration-via-timing oracle open -- the exact vector the generic-message design claims to close.

Not test-covered: tests/test_services/test_auth_service.py:69-83 (wrong_email / wrong_password) and 586-605 (None email/password) assert only `pytest.raises(AuthError, match="Invalid email or password")`; no test exercises or pins response timing or constant-time behavior. The route caller app/routes/auth.py:372-386 likewise reasons only about response WORDING (lines 376-379), not timing.

Not already known: no quality-pass ACCEPT row exists for `auth_service.py`/`authenticate` (grep of docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md returns none); no documented inline disable on this code; not P-1 (loan escrow) nor P-3 (negative deduction); not in deep-quality-hunt.md. Not rule-13 gold-plating of an impossible scenario: the project's own docs/security-audit-workflow.md:457-458 rates an analogous timing side-channel (backup-code `==` compare) as a Medium finding, and the codebase already invests in timing equalization for the lockout branch, so the no-user-branch equalization is consistent with established security posture, not speculative. Lockout (LOCKOUT_THRESHOLD default 10, _get_lockout_threshold at 60-81) caps but does not eliminate the oracle -- a few timed samples per email suffice before lockout, and a successful-existence probe needs no correct password. Corrected severity MED matches both the finding and the project's own rating of the analogous side-channel.

### 28. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] reverse_project_balance ignores the annual contribution limit while the forward path it claims to invert applies it
- **Location:** `app/services/growth_engine.py` :: 482-541, 523, 361-391
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `reverse_project_balance` computes `contribution = max(periodic_contribution, ZERO)` (line 523) with no annual-limit capping and accepts no limit argument. The year-end caller pairs it with `_forward_project_periods`, which DOES pass `annual_contribution_limit` and `ytd_contributions_start` to `project_balance` (year_end_summary_service/_balances.py:382-390) while `_reverse_project_periods` passes neither (line 424-430). The docstring claims reverse is 'the exact inverse of the forward growth formula' (line 492-497), but when the limit binds the forward per-period contribution is capped (cap_contribution_at_limit, line 363-367) and the reverse uses the uncapped `periodic_contribution`.
- **Why it matters:** For a contributor whose periodic contribution exceeds the remaining annual limit in pre-anchor periods, the inferred Jan-1 (pre-anchor) balance is computed by subtracting more contribution per period than was actually allowed, mis-deriving the historical balance the year-end summary displays. The roundtrip tests never set a limit (test_growth_engine.py:1177-1259), so this asymmetry is unguarded.
- **Suggested fix:** Either pass the annual limit (and a reverse-walking YTD) into `reverse_project_balance` so it caps symmetrically, or correct the docstring to state the inverse holds only for the no-limit / non-binding case and document why the year-end usage is safe.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- verified every cited line:
- growth_engine.py:482-488: reverse_project_balance's signature accepts (anchor_balance, assumed_annual_return, periods, periodic_contribution=ZERO, employer_params=None) -- NO annual_contribution_limit and NO ytd argument.
- growth_engine.py:523: contribution = max(periodic_contribution, ZERO) -- a single uncapped value reused for EVERY reversed period (line 539 subtracts it each iteration). No cap_contribution_at_limit call.
- growth_engine.py:492-497, 502-503: docstring claims "the exact inverse of the forward growth formula" and explicitly rationalizes the omission: "Annual contribution limits are NOT tracked in reverse because the anchor balance already reflects historical limit enforcement."
- Forward asymmetry confirmed: growth_engine.py:363-367 caps the per-period contribution via cap_contribution_at_limit, and 334-338/382-385 reset YTD+remaining_limit at the year boundary. So when the limit binds the forward per-period contribution is < periodic_contribution.
- _balances.py:382-390 (_forward_project_periods) passes annual_contribution_limit AND ytd_contributions_start to project_balance; _balances.py:424-430 (_reverse_project_periods) passes NEITHER. Exactly the pairing the finding describes.

REAL ISSUE (not safe-by-construction, not test-covered):
- InvestmentInputs.annual_contribution_limit IS populated (investment_projection.py:287-288) and periodic_contribution IS populated (282-285), so the limit data exists at both call sites but is dropped on the reverse side.
- The reverse-derived value is actually DISPLAYED: _merge_balance_sources (_balances.py:459-467) uses rev_by_pid for pre-anchor periods (they are absent from proj_by_pid and from base_balances -- balance_resolver has no pre-anchor data, confirmed by _periods.py:132 "calculate_balances skips them"). In the savings path _derive_investment_jan1 (_savings.py:290-297) returns reversed_proj[0].start_balance directly as the Jan-1 balance.
- Worked example: IRA limit $7,000, periodic $1,000, anchor mid-year. Actual contributions cap at $7,000 total (periods 1-7 = $1,000, period 8+ = $0); the anchor balance reflects only that. Reverse subtracts $1,000 EVERY period including the post-cap ones, over-subtracting and deriving a Jan-1 balance that is too LOW -- so the docstring's "anchor already reflects enforcement" justification is mathematically wrong precisely when the limit binds. In _savings.py this is internally self-inconsistent: the same pre-anchor periods are re-walked forward at lines 226-235 WITH the cap right after being walked backward WITHOUT it.
- The trigger (anchor after Jan 1) is the documented purpose of the reverse path, and a per-period contribution exceeding the remaining IRA/limit room early in the year is plausible (front-loading, $7,000 IRA), so this is NOT rule-13 gold-plating of an impossible scenario.
- Tests: TestReverseProjectBalance (test_growth_engine.py:1177-1259) roundtrips NEVER set a limit, so the asymmetry is unguarded.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: open problems are P-1 (loan escrow payments arg, plan.md:2155), P-2 (account dropdown, fixed), P-3 (negative deduction, plan.md:2199) -- none is this. quality-pass.md row 16/lines 340-344 reviewed growth_engine.py but only for refactor behavior-equivalence and the _period_return_rate DRY ("reverse INVERTS the forward formula" -- true ONLY of the rate, not the contribution cap); it never examined the pre-existing reverse/limit capping asymmetry. No documented disable covers it.

NOTE: severity MED is correct -- bites only when anchor is mid-year AND the contribution exceeds remaining limit in pre-anchor periods. The correct fix (thread the limit + a reverse-walking YTD into reverse_project_balance vs. document a non-binding precondition) is a financial/design judgment, so this borders NEEDS-DECISION; the defect itself is confirmed real.

### 29. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Emergency-fund avg-monthly-expenses compares figures computed over different account scopes
- **Location:** `app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py` :: 134-150, 170-201, 204-216
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** _compute_avg_monthly_expenses returns max(historical, floor). historical (_recent_settled_expenses_monthly) sums settled expenses with NO account filter -- across every account (checking, savings, loan, etc.) -- while floor (_committed_expense_floor) is explicitly scoped to checking accounts only (checking_ids, lines 170-174). The two operands of the max() therefore measure different universes of spending.
- **Why it matters:** An expense recorded on a non-checking account (e.g. a loan-account payment row or an HSA spend) inflates the historical operand but never the floor, so emergency-fund 'months covered' coverage can be driven by spending the floor deliberately excludes, making the headline emergency-fund metric inconsistent with its own committed baseline.
- **Suggested fix:** Scope _recent_settled_expenses_monthly to the same checking-account set the floor uses (or document and align both to the intended account scope) so the max() compares like with like.
- **Verifier evidence:** I attempted to refute but the code independently confirms the finding.

FACTUAL ACCURACY (confirmed): app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:
- _recent_settled_expenses_monthly (lines 134-150) queries Transaction filtered ONLY on pay_period_id.in_(recent_period_ids), scenario_id == scenario.id, and is_deleted.is_(False) (lines 136-140). There is NO account_id / account-type filter. The per-txn loop (lines 145-147) sums Decimal(str(txn.effective_amount)) for every txn where txn.is_expense and txn.status.is_settled, regardless of which account the row lives on.
- _committed_expense_floor (lines 170-201) builds checking_ids = [acct.id for acct in accounts if acct.account_type_id == checking_type_id] (lines 170-174) and constrains BOTH the expense-template query (.account_id.in_(checking_ids), line 183) and the transfer-template query (.from_account_id.in_(checking_ids), line 193) to checking only.
- _compute_avg_monthly_expenses (lines 212-216) returns max(historical, floor). The two operands are computed over different account universes exactly as claimed.

REACHABILITY (confirmed -- not safe-by-construction, not rule-13): Expense rows can legitimately exist on non-checking accounts. app/routes/transactions/create.py:75-92 and 121-133 build a Transaction from data["account_id"] after only an ownership probe (_resolve_owned_fks) -- no checking-account restriction. Transfer expense shadows live on from_account: app/services/transfer_service.py:456 (_build_shadow with spec.from_account_id, expense_type_id) and _build_shadow at line 282-323 sets account_id=from_account; a transfer FROM a savings/HSA account TO checking therefore writes a settled is_expense shadow ON the non-checking source account. Such rows inflate the historical operand but are excluded from the floor.

TEST COVERAGE (confirmed gap): tests/test_services/test_savings_dashboard_service.py TestEmergencyFundMetrics (line 583) contains a single test, test_total_savings_sums_savings_accounts, covering only total_savings. The orchestrator key-presence/empty-default tests (lines 35, 51) assert avg_monthly_expenses == 0 on an empty user. No test exercises the historical-vs-floor account-scope mismatch.

ALREADY-KNOWN (confirmed not): quality-pass register docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md row 6 (line 124) marks the savings_dashboard_service package REVIEWED with note "M2: untyped params bag, built-then-patched" -- unrelated. plan.md:1154 references this function only for too-many-locals (mechanical). Financial-audit F-006 (docs/audits/financial_calculations/03_consistency.md:530-576) discusses "different account universes" but for the savings-BALANCE aggregators across /savings vs retirement-gap vs year-end, NOT this avg-monthly-EXPENSES computation. Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction).

VERDICT NUANCE: The defect (two max() operands over different account universes) is real and accurate. But whether to fix by scoping historical to checking_ids, aligning the floor's scope, or accepting the max() as a deliberately-conservative "cover all observed spending" metric is a financial/design judgment the developer must make -- hence NEEDS-DECISION rather than CONFIRMED.

### 30. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Multi-year salary projection applies a single (current) tax year's brackets, FICA wage base and SS cap to all future-year periods
- **Location:** `app/services/tax_config_service.py` :: 16-69
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** paycheck-tax
