- **Claim:** load_tax_configs defaults tax_year to date.today().year (lines 36-37) and returns ONE bracket_set/state_config/fica_config. Every caller of project_salary (app/routes/salary/views.py:90-94, app/services/income_service.py:124-129 and 222-229) loads tax_configs ONCE and runs project_salary over the full ~2-year get_all_periods set, so periods dated 2027/2028 are withheld using 2026 brackets and 2026 FicaConfig.ss_wage_base (default 176100, lines 207-210 of app/models/tax_config.py). _get_cumulative_wages (paycheck_calculator.py:778-808) resets per calendar year, so each future year's SS cap-crossing period is computed against the current year's wage base, not that year's.
- **Why it matters:** The SS wage base and brackets rise roughly yearly; for a high earner the cap-crossing period and the post-cap zero-SS periods in 2027/2028 are computed against the wrong base, mis-stating projected net pay and the FICA portion of forward projections. Needs domain confirmation on whether future-year tax configs are expected to exist and be used per-period.
- **Suggested fix:** In project_salary (or calculate_paycheck) resolve tax_configs per period.start_date.year (falling back to the latest available year), rather than passing a single current-year config for the whole 2-year horizon.
- **Verifier evidence:** Finding is factually accurate at every cited line. app/services/tax_config_service.py:36-37 defaults tax_year to date.today().year and returns ONE bracket_set/state_config/fica_config (65-69). app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:project_salary (289-294) passes that same single tax_configs dict to calculate_paycheck for EVERY period; calculate_paycheck (184-257) reads bracket_set/state_config/fica_config from the dict with no regard for period.start_date.year. _get_cumulative_wages (778-808) resets cumulative by period_year but the SS cap uses the single passed fica_config (ss_wage_base default 176100, app/models/tax_config.py:207-210). Callers app/routes/salary/views.py:90, app/services/income_service.py:125 (live_projected_gross) and 225 (live_projected_net) all call load_tax_configs(user_id, profile) with no tax_year, applying current-year configs across the full ~2-year get_all_periods horizon.

It is a REAL issue, not gold-plating of an impossible scenario: multi-year tax configs are an explicit designed capability -- migration 7abcbf372fff docstring lines 60-61 ("intent ... is to let a user configure different tax brackets per tax_year"), load_tax_configs accepts a tax_year arg, and tests/test_services/test_tax_config_service.py:116/167 (test_explicit_tax_year_selects_correct_configs) verifies per-year selection. The codebase itself established the per-year-with-current-year-fallback pattern in TWO places that the project_salary callers do NOT follow: app/services/recurrence_engine.py:749-765 (_get_transaction_amount, tax_year=period.start_date.year, fallback only when the future year has NO configs at all) and app/services/year_end_summary_service/_income_tax.py:99-101. recurrence_engine's own docstring (725-729) acknowledges the divergence: "This matches the salary profile page's behavior (which always uses the current year)." Consequence: the recurrence engine generates and persists future-year net pay using future-year configs, while income_service.live_projected_net -- whose stated purpose (docstring 137-151) is that the stored estimated_amount "cannot silently disagree" with the live recompute -- uses current-year configs; live_projected_net feeds balance_resolver.py:399 and balance_calculator.py (consumers confirmed via grep), so for any user who creates 2027/2028 configs the forward balance projection silently disagrees with the generated grid amount, the exact reconciliation the code claims to uphold. Not test-covered: tests/test_routes/test_salary.py:41-45 deliberately freezes "today" inside the seeded 2026 range so the horizon never escapes existing configs; no test exercises the salary-page/income_service path against future-year configs. In the COMMON seeded case it is benign -- the default seed (app/services/auth_service.py:_seed_tax_data_for_user, DEFAULT_FEDERAL_BRACKETS at 285 keys 2025/2026 only) gives no 2027/2028 configs, so the recurrence-engine fallback collapses to current-year and the two paths agree -- which is why severity is MED, not HIGH.

NEEDS-DECISION rather than CONFIRMED because the correct fix is a financial/design judgment the developer must make: (a) push per-period tax_year resolution + the current-year fallback into project_salary/calculate_paycheck so every consumer (salary page, income_service, dashboards) matches the recurrence engine, vs (b) fix each caller, and (c) whether _get_cumulative_wages should also vary the SS wage base by each period's year. Distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction); not a documented disable or quality-pass ACCEPT row.

### 31. [SECURITY/CORRECTNESS-RISK] CSV exports write user-controlled strings without formula-injection neutralization
- **Location:** `app/services/csv_export_service.py` :: 72-83, 98-110, 134-163, 330-377
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** _safe/_write_csv emit transaction names, category names, account names, and deduction names verbatim into CSV cells via csv.writer. csv.writer only quotes/escapes for CSV parsing correctness; it does NOT neutralize spreadsheet formula injection. A cell beginning with =, +, -, @, TAB or CR (e.g. a transaction named `=HYPERLINK("http://evil","x")` or `=cmd|...`) is executed by Excel/Google Sheets on open. The routes serve these as `text/csv` attachments (app/routes/analytics.py:455). grep found no startswith/sanitize/neutralize guard anywhere in the CSV path.
- **Why it matters:** A field a user (or a companion in a shared scenario) types becomes an active formula in the downloaded spreadsheet, enabling data exfiltration or local command execution against whoever opens the export.
- **Suggested fix:** Prefix any cell whose string value starts with one of = + - @ TAB CR with a single quote (or a leading space) in a shared _safe helper before writing.
- **Verifier evidence:** VERIFIED ACCURATE. _safe (app/services/csv_export_service.py:72-83) only does `str(value)` with None->"" -- no formula-prefix neutralization. _write_csv (lines 98-110) uses bare csv.writer, which handles RFC-4180 quoting/escaping (commas, quotes, newlines) for parser correctness but does NOT neutralize spreadsheet formula injection (a cell starting with = + - @ TAB CR is executed by Excel/Sheets on open). User-controlled name strings flow verbatim into cells: transaction names via _safe (lines 153 entry.name, 364 txn.name), category group/item names (259-261, 351-363, 411-412 -- emitted raw, not even through _safe), account names (270 destination_account, 292 d.account_name, 306 s.account_name), and deduction names (237/241 ded["name"]). These are user-input free-text columns: transaction.name String(200) (app/models/transaction.py:161), category.group_name/item_name String(100) (app/models/category.py:31-32), account.name String(100) (app/models/account.py:66). Routes serve them as a text/csv attachment download (app/routes/analytics.py:454-457 in _csv_response; export calls at 154,161,203,259,306). MITIGATION ABSENT: grep over app/ and tests/ found no startswith/sanitize/neutralize guard in the CSV path. NOT TEST-COVERED for this: test_csv_export_service.py covers comma quoting (line 332 test_export_commas_in_names) and quote escaping (342 test_export_quotes_in_names) for CSV parseability only -- zero formula-injection test; XSS-prevention suite does not touch CSV. NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not P-1, not P-3, not a documented pylint disable, and the quality-pass register is design-quality (A-G rubric), not security. This is CWE-1236 CSV/formula injection. Severity MED is correct: exploitation needs the victim to open the export and (in modern Excel/Sheets) bypass a warning, and in the single-user case attacker==victim, but the shared-scenario companion vector (companion-supplied names landing in another user's export) makes it a real cross-user risk. CONFIRMED (not NEEDS-DECISION) because the fix is the standard, non-judgment mitigation: prefix any cell whose string starts with = + - @ TAB CR with a single quote in a shared _safe helper.

### 32. [DRY/JUDGMENT] savings.update_goal inlines the pre-flush stale-form conflict instead of the shared handle_stale_form_conflict helper
- **Location:** `app/routes/savings.py` :: 200-213
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** The block at 200-213 (log `"Stale-form conflict on update_goal id=%d (submitted=%d, current=%d)"`, flash a warning, redirect to the edit form) is the exact behavior of `_recurrence_form_helpers.handle_stale_form_conflict(StaleConflictContext(...), submitted=..., current=...)` (helper at lines 389-431, identical log template at line 426-429). savings.py already imports `StaleConflictContext` and `commit_or_handle_stale` from `_commit_helpers` and uses the commit-time helper at 236-245, yet reimplements the form-side mirror inline. templates.py:405 and transfers/templates.py:284 use the helper for the same case.
- **Why it matters:** This is semantic duplication R0801's near-textual matcher misses (different variable names/log label across ~8 inlined copies: savings, entries, anchor x2, salary x2, transfers/mutations, transactions/mutations vs only 2 helper users). The wording/log-format of the stale-conflict UX can now drift per route, defeating the point of the F-26 extraction. savings is the in-scope instance and is one import line from using the shared helper.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace lines 200-213 with `return handle_stale_form_conflict(StaleConflictContext(logger=logger, log_label="update_goal", log_id=goal_id, flash_message=..., redirect=RedirectTarget("savings.edit_goal", {"goal_id": goal_id})), submitted=submitted_version, current=goal.version_id)`.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every load-bearing claim verified against committed code.

FACTUALLY ACCURATE: app/routes/savings.py:200-213 inlines the pre-flush stale-form conflict: log template "Stale-form conflict on update_goal id=%d (submitted=%d, current=%d)" (lines 204-206), flash(..., "warning") (208-212), redirect to savings.edit_goal (213). This is behaviorally identical to handle_stale_form_conflict (app/routes/_recurrence_form_helpers.py:389-431): identical log template at 425-428 ("Stale-form conflict on %s id=%d (submitted=%d, current=%d)"), identical "warning" flash (430), redirect via RedirectTarget.to_response() (431). savings.py already imports StaleConflictContext + commit_or_handle_stale (lines 22-25) and RedirectTarget (line 26), and uses the commit-time half commit_or_handle_stale at 236-245, but does NOT import handle_stale_form_conflict. Confirmed the two existing helper users at templates.py:405 and transfers/templates.py:284.

REAL ISSUE (semantic DRY, invisible to R0801): grep shows the same inline pre-flush block in 8 routes (transfers/mutations.py:99, salary/profiles.py:292, entries.py:315, accounts/anchor.py:79 & 252, salary/items.py:230 & 501, savings.py:202, transactions/mutations.py:325) vs only 2 helper users -- the finding's "~8 inlined vs 2 helper" count is exact. plan.md:2264 (commit 8e01099) confirms the F-26 extraction routed the commit-time half to ~30 sites across savings/salary/accounts/etc. but the form-side mirror handle_stale_form_conflict reached only 3 sites (8->3), and that R0801 misses these because "log_labels / flash strings / endpoints differ." So the asymmetry is structural, not coincidental. The helper depends only on StaleConflictContext/flash/RedirectTarget (nothing recurrence-specific), and the commit-time sibling was already deliberately relocated OUT of the recurrence module to _commit_helpers.py "once the salary / savings / account CRUD routes needed them" (_recurrence_form_helpers.py:42-45) -- the form-side mirror simply was not similarly generalized. Refactor is safe: test_optimistic_locking_c18.py:930 (TestSavingsGoalStaleFormPrevention) covers the savings stale-form branch (asserts b"changed by another action" and no write), and STALE_EDITING_MESSAGE (_recurrence_form_helpers.py:82-85) reproduces savings' exact wording.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not P-1 (loan escrow) and not P-3 (negative deduction). No quality-pass ACCEPT row covers app/routes/savings.py's update_goal stale-form block (the savings rows in quality-pass.md are services/savings_dashboard_service and services/savings_goal_service only; grep for routes/savings|update_goal|stale-form|form-side|pre-flush in quality-pass.md returned nothing). No documented disable on the inline block.

SCOPE NUANCE (does not change verdict): the finding's narrow "fix savings alone, one import line" is accurate and actionable, but the genuine problem is the fleet-wide 8-vs-2 split; the fully-correct remediation (relocate the helper to _commit_helpers.py alongside its commit-time sibling and migrate all 8 inline sites) is a coordinated cross-file refactor. MED is correct: this is a DRY/maintainability/UX-drift issue, not a financial-correctness bug -- the behavior is currently identical at all 8 sites, but each can drift independently.

### 33. [DRY/JUDGMENT] _sum_remaining and _sum_all are now byte-identical after the is_projected extraction
- **Location:** `app/services/balance_calculator.py` :: 457-489 vs 492-523
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** After routing both through is_projected (D6-09), _sum_remaining (anchor period) and _sum_all (post-anchor) have identical bodies: init income/expenses to Decimal('0.00'), loop, 'if not is_projected(txn): continue', then 'if txn.is_income: income += _income_amount(...) elif txn.is_expense: expenses += _expense_amount(...)'. The only difference is docstring/comment prose ('remaining' vs 'all'). Their historical distinction (anchor period summed only remaining, post-anchor summed all projected) collapsed when both became Projected-only. R0801 misses it: both are in one file with differing docstrings.
- **Why it matters:** A future change to the projected-period summing rule must be made in two places that are supposed to mean different things but no longer do; editing one and not the other silently desynchronizes the anchor-period and post-anchor balance math.
- **Suggested fix:** Collapse to one function (e.g. _sum_projected(transactions, amount_overrides)) called from both balance branches in calculate_balances, or document why two names with identical bodies must persist.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE: Read app/services/balance_calculator.py:457-523. _sum_remaining (def 457, body 471-489) and _sum_all (def 492, body 506-523) have byte-identical executable bodies. Stripped comments and diffed both bodies -> "IDENTICAL". Both init income/expenses=Decimal("0.00"), loop, `if not is_projected(txn): continue` (lines 481 / 515), then `if txn.is_income: income += _income_amount(...) elif txn.is_expense: expenses += _expense_amount(...)`, return tuple. Only difference is docstring/comment prose. Both route through the SAME imported is_projected (line 28) and the same _income_amount/_expense_amount helpers, so no hidden divergence. Callers confirmed: calculate_balances uses _sum_remaining for the anchor period (line 103) and _sum_all for post-anchor (line 108). HISTORICAL DISTINCTION CONFIRMED: git show of the initial build (f9b35ec) proves _sum_remaining excluded credit+SETTLED_STATUSES and used estimated_amount (projected-remaining only), while _sum_all excluded only credit and used effective_amount (included done/received in post-anchor periods) -- genuinely different rules that collapsed when both became Projected-only (the is_projected/D6-09/MED-02 routing, git -S diff confirms the `status_id != projected_id` -> `not is_projected(txn)` change in both).

REAL ISSUE: Latent DRY/SOLID drift substrate. tests/test_services/test_balance_calculator.py:1445-1479 (test_balance_excludes_settled_from_projection) exercises only the anchor path (periods[0]) and its docstring notes both functions "filter by status_id == projected_id" but asserts no sync invariant; grep of tests/ found no test that pins the two bodies as equivalent. A one-sided edit (e.g. adding a credit guard to _sum_all only) would silently split anchor vs post-anchor balance math with no test failing -- exactly the why_it_matters claim.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN (per task scope): This is NOT an inline documented disable, NOT a quality-pass ACCEPT row (quality-pass.md row #2 line 558 covers the DIFFERENT _entry_checking_impact 3-bucket extraction; _sum_projected_balances refs are an unrelated retirement_gap_calculator helper), and NOT P-1/P-3. It IS independently recorded as D6-06 -> CRIT-01 in the SEPARATE financial-calculations audit (docs/audits/financial_calculations/06_dry_solid.md:485-549; 08_findings.md:2429), where it is explicitly "report only / Phase-6 DRY observation, structural substrate" and remains UNRESOLVED -- git log of all branches shows no commit collapsing _sum_remaining/_sum_all (grep -c still finds 2 separate defs). The pylint-cleanup do-not-re-report list does not include financial-calculations-audit open findings.

VERDICT CONFIRMED (not NEEDS-DECISION): the remediation is a plain DRY collapse to one parameter-free helper (already prescribed by D6-06 since the anchor-vs-roll-forward semantics live solely in calculate_balances at lines 104/109), not a financial-judgment fork. Severity MED: the two cannot disagree today (same code -> no current numeric drift), so the risk is latent-only.

### 34. [DRY/JUDGMENT] 'Whole months between two dates' formula inlined in 5 places; rate_period_engine even has a named helper others ignore
- **Location:** `app/services/rate_period_engine.py` :: 177-184; also escrow_calculator.py:116-117, amortization_engine.py:157-158, amortization_engine.py:953-954, savings_goal_service.py:410-411
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** The expression (end.year - start.year) * 12 + (end.month - start.month) -- whole calendar months, day ignored -- is reproduced at rate_period_engine._months_between (184), escrow_calculator.py:116-117, amortization_engine.calculate_remaining_months (157-158), amortization_engine.py:953-954, and savings_goal_service._compute_required_monthly (410-411). rate_period_engine._months_between's own docstring (180-181) cross-references amortization_engine.calculate_remaining_months's convention -- proof both authors knew they shared the rule -- yet neither extracted it. The natural home app/utils/dates.py owns add_months but not this.
- **Why it matters:** A month-counting convention scattered across escrow inflation, loan amortization, debt-payoff, and savings-contribution math is a single rule whose definition can drift per-site (e.g. one site adding a day-of-month adjustment). Centralizing also makes the sign/clamp contract testable once.
- **Suggested fix:** Add months_between(start, end) to app/utils/dates.py next to add_months and route all five sites (delete rate_period_engine._months_between) through it.
- **Verifier evidence:** All five cited sites verified by reading the actual code:

1. app/services/rate_period_engine.py:184 -- `return (end.year - start.year) * 12 + (end.month - start.month)`. This is `_months_between`, a named private helper used 5x internally (lines 209, 476, 497, 572, 694) but exported/used nowhere else (grep: only rate_period_engine references it). Its docstring (180-181) DOES cross-reference `amortization_engine.calculate_remaining_months`'s convention -- claim verified verbatim.
2. app/services/escrow_calculator.py:116-117 -- `(as_of_date.year - created.year) * 12 + (as_of_date.month - created.month)`. Identical base formula (day ignored); clamp applied separately at 119-121.
3. app/services/amortization_engine.py:157-158 (calculate_remaining_months) -- `(as_of.year - origination_date.year) * 12 + (as_of.month - origination_date.month)`. Identical; clamp at 160 (`max(0, term_months - months_elapsed)`).
4. app/services/amortization_engine.py:953-955 -- `(request.target_date.year - start_year) * 12 + (request.target_date.month - start_month) + 1`. SAME base formula but with a deliberate `+ 1` ("inclusive", "legacy convention" per the 944-948 comment) -- a genuine semantic variant, not the bare rule.
5. app/services/savings_goal_service.py:410-411 -- `(target_date.year - today.year) * 12 + (target_date.month - today.month)`. Identical; clamp at 414.

A targeted grep `year)\s*\*\s*12` over app/ returns exactly these 5 occurrences -- no more, no fewer, so the inventory is complete and accurate.

app/utils/dates.py read in full: it has only `add_months` (13) and no `months_between` -- the claim's "natural home owns add_months but not this" is correct, and add_months is the proven precedent for centralizing day-clamped month arithmetic.

NOT already known: searched docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md -- the "F3" rows there are the rubric dimension F3 (public surface), NOT this finding's id. The DRY register entries (cluster 3a-3e at line 559, the horizon dedup at 395, ref_cache at 379) do not cover the months-between formula. No documented disable or ACCEPT row touches it. Not P-1 (loan escrow threshold) or P-3 (negative deduction).

Why NEEDS-DECISION rather than CONFIRMED: the finding is accurate and real, but the right fix is a developer judgment because the five sites are not perfectly uniform. Four sites use "whole calendar months, day ignored, no clamp" identically, but site 4 (amortization_engine.py:953) deliberately adds `+ 1` for an inclusive legacy gate, and the clamping differs per site (some clamp the months, escrow clamps years-elapsed). Routing all five through a single `months_between(start, end)` is sound (the `+1` becomes `months_between(...) + 1` at the call site, clamps stay caller-local exactly as today), but the developer should ratify the contract (signed, unclamped) and decide whether the inclusive site is worth the extra call-site `+1` versus staying inline. This is currently a maintainability/drift-risk finding (the four base-rule sites agree today), not a live correctness defect -- so MED severity is appropriate, not HIGH.

### 35. [DRY/JUDGMENT] 3/6/12-month horizon offset table duplicated inline while the canonical helper is imported in the same module
- **Location:** `app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_projections.py; app/utils/period_projections.py` :: _projections.py:289-294 vs :374; period_projections.py:13-17,48-53
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** period_projections.HORIZON_OFFSETS (=[('3 months',6),('6 months',13),('1 year',26)]) plus project_balance_horizons() is the shared producer for the 3/6/12-month balance horizons, and _projections.py imports project_balance_horizons (line 31) and uses it at line 374. Yet _projections.py:_investment_horizons (lines 289-294) re-declares the identical literal offset table '[("3 months", 6), ("6 months", 13), ("1 year", 26)]' and re-implements the 'current_period.period_index + offset -> balance map' lookup inline. Same concept, two definitions of the offset constant, in one package.
- **Why it matters:** If the horizon set or the period-offset approximation changes (e.g. a 2-year horizon, or a non-26-period cadence), the investment branch silently keeps the old horizons while the plain-account branch updates, so the same dashboard shows inconsistent horizons.
- **Suggested fix:** Refactor _investment_horizons to build the {period_id: end_balance} map from the projection and then call project_balance_horizons / iterate HORIZON_OFFSETS, deleting the inline offset literal.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUAL (all confirmed by reading committed code): period_projections.py:13-17 defines HORIZON_OFFSETS = (("3 months",6),("6 months",13),("1 year",26)); project_balance_horizons (period_projections.py:20-54) is the shared producer doing the "current_period.period_index + offset -> balance_map[period.id]" scan. _projections.py:31 imports project_balance_horizons and uses it at line 374 (the plain-account else branch). _investment_horizons (_projections.py:270-295) re-declares the byte-identical literal [("3 months", 6), ("6 months", 13), ("1 year", 26)] at lines 289-291 and re-implements the same period_index+offset lookup at lines 288-294 (it first builds proj_by_idx keyed by period_index via a nested loop over projection x all_periods at 282-287). Minor imprecision in the finding: the literal is at 289-291, not 289-294, and HORIZON_OFFSETS is a tuple not a list -- immaterial, values identical.

REAL ISSUE: Genuine R0801-invisible semantic duplication -- same business rule, different shape (module-level tuple + period_id-keyed map vs inline list literal + period_index-keyed map built by a nested loop). Both branches feed the same ad["projected"] dict rendered uniformly by app/templates/savings/dashboard.html:206-209 ({% for label, bal in ad.projected.items() %}), so a change to HORIZON_OFFSETS (e.g. adding a 2-year/52 horizon or a non-26 cadence) updates plain-account tiles but silently NOT investment tiles -- a real cross-tile horizon inconsistency on a money-displaying dashboard. Suggested fix is clean and behavior-preserving: growth_engine.ProjectionRecord has period_id directly (growth_engine.py:38, end_balance at :43), so {pb.period_id: pb.end_balance for pb in projection} then project_balance_horizons(current_period, all_periods, map) reproduces the result AND removes the unnecessary O(projection x periods) re-keying loop. The loan path (_loan_projected_horizons, _projections.py:143-153) uses MONTH offsets [3,6,12] + date-containment -- a genuinely different rule, correctly NOT in scope. NOT test-covered: tests/test_services/test_savings_dashboard_service.py has 55 tests, zero exercise the investment branch (only ref is a comment at line 1634); the parametric TestLoanProjectedBalanceDispatcher (2172+) is loan-only. So the inline table is unpinned and the refactor needs no test edits (rule 5 not implicated).

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: quality-pass.md:394-395 examined project_balance_horizons and enumerated its consumers as interest_detail + checking_detail + _projections.py:374 (plain-account branch) -- it explicitly did NOT mention _investment_horizons as a fourth inline-duplicate site. deep-quality-hunt.md row 12 (line 309-326) on this file concerns a DIFFERENT issue (current-period double-count projection semantics), not the offset-table DRY. Not a documented disable, not P-1 (loan escrow), not P-3 (negative deduction).

### 36. [LAZY/JUDGMENT] Grid subtotals are an N+1 query: period_subtotal re-queries transactions once per visible period despite balances_for already loading them all
- **Location:** `app/services/balance_resolver.py (consumed by app/routes/grid.py)` :: balance_resolver.py:558-560; grid.py:260-273 / 530-533
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** balance-grid
- **Claim:** period_subtotal calls _load_balance_transactions(account, scenario_id, [period.id]) on every invocation (balance_resolver.py:558). grid._build_grid_subtotals loops `for period in periods` and calls period_subtotal once per period (grid.py:261-269). On the same render, balances_for already issued one query loading every transaction across ALL periods (balance_resolver.py:479), and grid._load_grid_transactions loaded them a third time. So a wide grid (ctx.periods up to ~26 in compact mode, grid.py:542-546) issues ~N extra per-period transaction SELECTs plus N live_amount_overrides recomputations.
- **Why it matters:** The database rule explicitly calls out preventing N+1 on the grid route 'especially.' The transaction set for all periods is already in memory twice; re-querying per period scales the grid's DB round-trips with the visible-period count for no correctness benefit.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an optional pre-loaded `transactions` parameter to period_subtotal (or a batch period_subtotals(periods) that groups the single loaded set by period_id) and have the grid pass the already-loaded set instead of re-querying per period.
- **Verifier evidence:** Core claim verified against committed code. period_subtotal unconditionally re-queries per period: balance_resolver.py:558-560 calls `_load_balance_transactions(account, scenario_id, [period.id])` (def at :313-368, one SELECT with selectinload(entries)). grid.py:260-273 `_build_grid_subtotals` loops `for period in periods` and calls period_subtotal once per period (grid.py:269). On the same full-grid render, balances_for already issued one all-periods load (balance_resolver.py:479 `_load_balance_transactions(account, scenario_id, period_ids)`) AND `_load_grid_transactions` (grid.py:474, def :161-195) issued a second all-periods load -- so the per-period subtotal queries are a third in-memory re-fetch of the same data. num_periods is uncapped: it comes straight from request args / settings.grid_default_periods (grid.py:128-133) with only a `grid_default_periods > 0` check constraint (app/models/user.py:193, :251); col_size logic (grid.py:542-546) confirms num_periods can exceed 13 ("compact"), so a wide grid genuinely issues ~N extra per-period SELECTs. No query-count / assert_num_queries guard exists in tests/test_routes/test_grid.py, tests/test_services/test_balance_resolver.py, or tests/test_integration/test_cross_page_balance_equality.py (grep found none), so this is uncovered. The .claude/rules/database.md rule (lines 19-20) explicitly calls out preventing N+1 "on the grid route and balance calculator especially."

ONE sub-claim is FALSE (does not change verdict): "plus N live_amount_overrides recomputations." All three real callers of _build_grid_subtotals that loop multiple periods THREAD amount_overrides in (grid.py:437 plan view, grid.py:530-532 main render), so inside period_subtotal the `if amount_overrides is None` branch at balance_resolver.py:565 never fires per-period -- live_amount_overrides is NOT recomputed per period on the grid path. The only caller that omits overrides (grid.py:708, _mobile_tp_summary HTMX) passes a single `[period]`, so it is one query, not an N+1. The finding overcounts the cost but the underlying per-period transaction-SELECT N+1 is real.

Not already known: not P-1 (loan escrow threshold) or P-3 (negative deduction). quality-pass/plan.md only records balance_resolver KEEP rows for the protected-access disables (:565/:706) and the dated entry-bucketing duplicate-code disable (commit 6475429) -- none addresses period_subtotal's query count.

NEEDS-DECISION rather than CONFIRMED: the two proposed fixes (optional pre-loaded `transactions` param vs. a batch `period_subtotals(periods)` grouping the single loaded set by period_id) are a design choice, and any fix touches the financial core -- it must preserve the `balances[p] - balances[p-1] == period_subtotal(p).net` invariant that tests/test_integration/test_cross_page_balance_equality.py:465-516 enforces, so the developer should decide the shape.

### 37. [SECURITY/JUDGMENT] companion_reactivate lacks @fresh_login_required while every other companion lifecycle mutation requires it
- **Location:** `app/routes/settings.py` :: 539-565
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** companion_create (settings.py:388), companion_edit (450), and companion_deactivate (509) are all decorated @fresh_login_required(), but companion_reactivate (544) is not. Reactivation re-grants login access to a previously disabled companion account (settings.py:558 sets is_active=True) -- a credential-lifecycle operation at least as sensitive as deactivation. No test asserts a fresh-login requirement on reactivate (tests/test_routes/test_settings_companion.py:609-672 covers behavior but not re-auth).
- **Why it matters:** A hijacked but stale owner session could silently restore access to a companion the real owner deliberately disabled, bypassing the re-auth wall that protects the symmetric deactivate action. Inconsistent re-auth on inverse operations is a real access-control gap.
- **Suggested fix:** Add @fresh_login_required() to companion_reactivate (matching the other three companion routes) and add a test asserting an un-fresh session is redirected to /reauth.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/routes/settings.py directly. Decorator stacks confirmed exactly as claimed: companion_create has @login_required/@require_owner/@fresh_login_required() (lines 386-388); companion_edit has all three (448-450); companion_deactivate has all three (507-509); companion_reactivate has ONLY @login_required + @require_owner (542-543) and is MISSING @fresh_login_required() (def at 544). Line 558 confirms reactivation sets companion.is_active = True, re-granting login access -- the credential-lifecycle inverse of deactivate's is_active=False at line 524. fresh_login_required (app/utils/auth_helpers.py:364-435) is the step-up re-auth wall added in commit 2509357 ("security(session): C-10 ... step-up auth"); it redirects to /reauth when the owner's last password verification is stale, defending exactly against a hijacked-but-stale owner session performing a sensitive mutation. The asymmetry is a real access-control gap: the symmetric deactivate is protected, its inverse is not. NOT safe-by-construction -- @require_owner + @login_required give role + authentication but NOT the recency guarantee fresh_login_required provides. NOT intended: git blame shows the missing decorator dates to the route's original creation (34f091e5), and the later refactor (1d52d3f) never touched the decorator stack; no documented rationale anywhere says reactivate should skip fresh-login. The reactivate docstring (settings.py:545-551) explains only why session_invalidated_at is preserved (the COMPANION's old sessions stay dead) -- a different concern from the OWNER's re-auth recency. NOT test-covered: tests/test_routes/test_settings_companion.py TestReactivateCompanion (608-676) asserts is_active flip, login-after-reactivate, session_invalidated_at preservation, and idempotency, but no test asserts a fresh-login/redirect-to-reauth requirement (grep for fresh_login_required/reauth in that file returns nothing). NOT already-known: the quality-pass settings.py rows (quality-pass.md register #25 and rows at 386-389) all concern the show/update decomposition's behavior-equivalence and the icon-list tuple -- none mention the decorator asymmetry; not a documented disable; not P-1 or P-3. Fix is a mechanical security-consistency change (add @fresh_login_required() at line 544 to match the other three routes, plus a test asserting an un-fresh session is redirected to /reauth), not a design/financial judgment fork -- hence CONFIRMED, not NEEDS-DECISION. Severity MED is correct: real gap but gated on an already-compromised stale owner session as precondition.

### 38. [SOLID/JUDGMENT] employer_contribution_type and compounding_frequency are denormalized free-string enums driving financial branch logic via Python string-literal comparison
- **Location:** `app/models/investment_params.py` :: 39-41, 110-113
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** models-schema
- **Claim:** InvestmentParams.employer_contribution_type is a String(20) with a SQL CHECK IN ('none','flat_percentage','match') (investment_params.py:38-41,110-113) and InterestParams.compounding_frequency is a String(10) with CHECK IN ('daily','monthly','quarterly') (interest_params.py:22-25,78-80). These are domain enums that drive money math, yet they are stored as bare strings (not ref-table FKs, not in app/enums.py) and compared against string literals in service code: growth_engine.py:176 `if emp_type == 'flat_percentage'` / :180 `if emp_type == 'match'`; interest_projection.py:137/141/147 `if compounding_frequency == 'daily'/'monthly'/'quarterly'`. The same literals are triplicated across the model CHECK, the Marshmallow OneOf (validation.py:1534-1537, 1892-1895), and the service comparisons.
- **Why it matters:** The project mandate is full normalization and 'IDs for logic, strings for display only'; every other logic-bearing enum (statuses, calc_methods, tax_types, goal_modes) is a ref table resolved via ref_cache. The shekel-refname-compare gate only catches `.name` comparisons on ref relationships, so these free-string logic enums evade it. A typo or rename in any of the three copies silently mis-branches employer-match or interest-compounding math, and there is no single source of truth.
- **Suggested fix:** Promote both to ref tables (or at minimum module-level named constants shared by model CHECK, schema, and services) and branch on IDs/enum members via ref_cache, eliminating the literal-string triplication.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every cited location verified against committed code. MODEL: app/models/investment_params.py:38-41 `CheckConstraint("employer_contribution_type IN ('none','flat_percentage','match')")` and :110-113 `db.String(20), default="none", server_default=text("'none'")`; app/models/interest_params.py:22-25 `CheckConstraint("compounding_frequency IN ('daily','monthly','quarterly')")` and :78-80 `db.String(10), server_default="daily"`. SCHEMA: app/schemas/validation.py:1534-1537 `compounding_frequency ... OneOf(["daily","monthly","quarterly"])` and :1892-1895 `employer_contribution_type ... OneOf(["none","flat_percentage","match"])`. SERVICE branch logic: app/services/growth_engine.py:176 `if emp_type == "flat_percentage":`, :180 `if emp_type == "match":`; app/services/interest_projection.py:137/141/147 `if compounding_frequency == "daily"/elif "monthly"/elif "quarterly":` with :151 `else: return ZERO`. The investment literal `"none"` is ALSO compared in app/services/investment_projection.py:191-195 (`_employer_params`: `emp_type == "none"` then `{"type": emp_type, ...}` feeding growth_engine) -- so the literals are quadruplicated for investment (model default+CHECK, schema load_default+OneOf, two service modules), strengthening the finding beyond what the claim states.

ESTABLISHED PATTERN confirms outlier status: app/enums.py defines 13 logic-bearing enums all mirrored to ref tables + ref_cache, INCLUDING identically-shaped short-string enums -- CalcMethodEnum (`FLAT="flat"`, `PERCENTAGE="percentage"`, :100-101), DeductionTimingEnum (`PRE_TAX="pre_tax"`, `POST_TAX="post_tax"`, :90-91), TaxTypeEnum, GoalModeEnum. Neither compounding_frequency nor employer_contribution_type appears in app/enums.py, app/ref_cache.py, or app/models/ref.py (grep returned only an unrelated docstring mention).

GATE GAP confirmed: tools/pylint/shekel_checkers.py:171-216 (ShekelRefNameChecker) only flags an outermost `.name` attribute read compared to a string literal; `emp_type == "flat_percentage"` (plain str var) and `compounding_frequency == "daily"` are provably NOT flagged.

NOT TEST-COVERED as a defect: tests reference these strings per-layer (test_hysa.py:243 checks the OneOf, test_models/test_c25_column_invariants.py etc.) but no test asserts consistency BETWEEN the model CHECK, schema OneOf, and service comparisons; a rename in one copy that diverges from another would silently mis-branch (interest -> `else: return ZERO`; investment -> employer match falls through to `return ZERO`/`return None`), not crash.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/{plan,quality-pass,deep-quality-hunt}.md mention these models only for unrelated concerns (R0801 FK-block dedup, HALF_UP rounding on limit/26, projection-context decomposition); no ACCEPT row or disable addresses the free-string-enum / literal-triplication concern, and it is not P-1 or P-3.

Verdict NEEDS-DECISION (not flat CONFIRMED) only because the corrective action is a design fork the developer must choose -- full ref-table promotion (matches the normalization mandate but is invasive: migration + enum + ref_cache wiring) vs. the lighter shared module-level named constants referenced by model CHECK, schema, and services. Both are valid; the developer should pick. Severity MED stands: latent SSOT/maintainability + silent-mis-branch risk on rename, not a currently-firing money bug (model CHECK + schema OneOf bound today's inputs).

### 39. [TEST-QUALITY/JUDGMENT] generate_pay_periods has no test (and a behavioral gap) for partial overlap creating index gaps / cadence misalignment
- **Location:** `app/services/pay_period_service.py (tests: tests/test_services/test_pay_period_service.py)` :: service 65-95; tests 69-122
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** balance-grid
- **Claim:** The duplicate-skip loop (pay_period_service.py:68-84) consumes one of `num_periods` iterations per skipped duplicate (`continue` without decrement) and only matches EXACT existing start_dates via the set captured at line 58-63. The tests cover only full overlap (all dups -> 0 created, test l.69-96) and a clean cadence-aligned append (test l.98-122). There is no test for a PARTIAL overlap where the requested grid is offset from the existing one (so no start_date matches and periods are created starting at next_index but at start_dates that interleave existing ones), nor for the requested-count shortfall when some start_dates collide. The behavior in those cases (interleaved start_dates with monotonically-increasing indices, i.e. period_index no longer ordered by start_date) is undocumented and unverified.
- **Why it matters:** balance_as_of_date and _project_to_period_before assume period_index ordering tracks start_date ordering (balance_resolver.py:828-837 selects target by start_date but the anchor guard and prefix span use period_index, lines 836-884). If generate_pay_periods can produce a period whose higher index has an earlier start_date, those date-vs-index assumptions silently break. The generator's partial-overlap behavior should be pinned by a test before downstream code relies on the ordering invariant.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a test that generates an offset/partial-overlap batch and asserts the resulting (period_index, start_date) pairs stay co-monotonic; if they cannot be guaranteed, document and enforce cadence alignment in generate_pay_periods.
- **Verifier evidence:** All load-bearing claims independently verified against committed code.

FACTUAL ACCURACY -- CONFIRMED:
- pay_period_service.py:65-95: the duplicate-skip loop is `for _ in range(num_periods)`; on a duplicate (line 70, `if current_start in existing_starts`) it does `current_start += timedelta(days=cadence_days); continue` (lines 71-72) with NO decrement, so a duplicate consumes one of the num_periods iterations. CORRECT.
- existing_starts (lines 58-63) is a set of EXACT start_date values; line 70 is an exact-match membership test. So an OFFSET batch (start_date not aligned to existing paydays) matches nothing and creates all num_periods periods with assigned_index from next_index (= max existing index + 1, line 55) while their start_dates interleave the existing ones. CORRECT.
- Tests (test_pay_period_service.py): test_duplicate_start_date_silently_skipped (69-96) covers full overlap (3 dups -> 0 created); test_appending_to_existing_periods (98-122) covers a cadence-aligned append (Jan 2 + 42 days = Feb 13). There is NO test for an offset/partial-overlap batch anywhere in TestGeneratePayPeriods (23-167) or TestNegativeAndBoundaryPaths (346-478). CORRECT.
- Downstream assumption (why_it_matters): balance_resolver.py:828-833 selects target_period by iterating index-ordered periods (order_by period_index, line 817) and BREAKS on the first start_date > as_of (line 833) -- this assumes start_date is monotonic with period_index. Lines 836-838 (anchor guard) and 882-885 (_project_to_period_before prefix span) use period_index ordering. If a higher-index period had an earlier start_date, the break stops early and selects the wrong target. CORRECT.

REAL ISSUE -- YES, not safe-by-construction, not gold-plating:
- The offset/partial-overlap scenario is REACHABLE through the production form: pay_periods.py:45-49 passes user-submitted start_date/num_periods/cadence_days straight through; PayPeriodGenerateSchema (validation.py:433-442) validates only field types and Range(min/max) in isolation -- it does NOT validate start_date against existing periods or enforce cadence alignment.
- No guard prevents it: the service (lines 44-47) checks only isinstance(date) and cadence_days >= 1; the DB enforces only uq_pay_periods_user_start (unique start_date) and period_index >= 0 (pay_period.py:16-22, migration e5f6a7b8c9d0:71) -- nothing enforces index/date co-monotonicity. So a non-co-monotonic period set is permitted and the downstream break-assumption can silently break.

ALREADY KNOWN -- NO:
- Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). Not a documented inline disable. Not a quality-pass ACCEPT row. The only prior mention is deep-quality-hunt.md:139, which ASSERTS "assigning period_index monotonically in chronological order ... so order-by period_index == chronological" as a supporting PREMISE for Finding #4 (trend window) -- it never examines or pins the partial-overlap edge case; that premise holds only for a single batch or cadence-aligned appends, exactly the gap F6 raises.

VERDICT -- NEEDS-DECISION: accurate and a real latent gap, but the correct fix is a developer design judgment: either (a) treat offset batches as valid and add a test pinning co-monotonicity expectations -- which would expose the balance_resolver break (line 833) as the actual defect, or (b) enforce cadence alignment in generate_pay_periods so co-monotonicity is an invariant. Severity MED: latent, requires a user to generate an offset second batch (plausible via the UI but not the common contiguous-extend path).

### 40. [TEST-QUALITY/JUDGMENT] No test covers the cross-account/cross-scenario scope of the true-up entry clear (the leak in F1 is invisible to the suite)
- **Location:** `tests/test_routes/test_accounts.py` :: 645-657 (class scope doc); test methods 718-~860
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** balance-grid
- **Claim:** TestTrueUpClearsEntries asserts past-dated/projected entries get cleared, future-dated do not, non-projected parents are untouched, and a NON-checking true-up clears nothing (test names enumerated at the class). Every entry in these tests is created on seed_user['account'] in seed_user['scenario'] (_make_grocery_txn_with_entries, l.691-700). There is NO test that creates a second checking account (or a second scenario) and asserts that trueing up account A leaves account B's / scenario B's entries' is_cleared unchanged.
- **Why it matters:** Because every test confines entries to a single account+scenario, the missing predicate identified in F1 produces correct-looking results in all current tests; the cross-account/scenario over-clear ships undetected. The financial-assertion contract requires edge-case tests to assert the specific edge behavior.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a test with two checking accounts (and/or two scenarios) for one user, entries on both, true up account A, and assert account B's / scenario B's entries remain is_cleared=False.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- verified every cited line. TestTrueUpClearsEntries (tests/test_routes/test_accounts.py:645) has exactly the 5 enumerated methods: test_past_dated_projected_entries_get_cleared (l.718), test_future_dated_entries_not_cleared (l.749), test_entries_on_non_projected_parent_not_cleared (l.777), test_non_checking_true_up_does_not_clear (l.814), test_already_cleared_entries_unchanged (l.863). Every entry/txn in these tests is created via _make_grocery_txn_with_entries (l.659) which hardcodes account_id=seed_user["account"].id (l.681,695) and scenario_id=seed_user["scenario"].id (l.694). The savings-true-up service test (test_anchor_service.py:160-223) also keeps the unrelated entry on the single seed_user checking account. There is NO test in either file that creates a second CHECKING account or a second SCENARIO, trues up account A, and asserts account B's / scenario B's entries' is_cleared stays False.

REAL ISSUE -- the masked leak (F1) is genuine. clear_entries_for_anchor_true_up (app/services/entry_service.py:637) filters the bulk UPDATE only by PayPeriod.user_id == owner_id (l.690) plus is_deleted (l.691) and is_projected_clause (l.692); it has NO account_id and NO scenario_id predicate. Its only caller, anchor_service.apply_anchor_true_up (l.234), passes solely user_id -- the account being trued up is not forwarded into the scope. So trueing up checking account A flips is_cleared=TRUE on the owner's past-dated projected entries across ALL their checking accounts and ALL scenarios. The balance calculator is per-account/per-scenario sensitive to is_cleared: _entry_aware_amount (balance_calculator.py:287-302) subtracts cleared debits from the reservation, and the existing test_accounts_multi_account_each_correct (test_accounts.py:2758) proves the projection responds per-account to is_cleared. That very test, however, never calls /true-up and never asserts is_cleared preservation -- it creates already-cleared entries and only checks projection. So the over-clear genuinely ships undetected by the suite: a regression in the missing account_id/scenario_id predicate would leave all current tests green.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN -- not P-1 (loan escrow) nor P-3 (negative deduction). Not a documented disable. The quality-pass register (docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md) and plan.md have anchor.py rows, but the only anchor watch-item is a DIFFERENT test (test_double_submit_creates_one_history_row body assertion); nothing covers the clear-true-up cross-account/cross-scenario scope.

Verdict CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION: F7's own remedy (add a two-checking-account and/or two-scenario test asserting account B / scenario B entries stay is_cleared=False) is unambiguous test-quality work. The judgment call belongs to the bound defect F1 (whether the clear should scope by account_id, scenario_id, or both), not to writing the protecting test. Severity held at MED: it is a missing edge-case test, but it shields a HIGH-impact financial over-clear.


## LOW severity

### 41. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] HTMX category-create group_names dropdown includes archived groups; settings GET excludes them
- **Location:** `app/routes/categories.py` :: 98-103
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** The HTMX branch builds `group_names` from `db.session.query(Category.group_name).filter_by(user_id=current_user.id).distinct()` with NO `is_active` filter (lines 98-103), whereas the full-page settings render derives it from active categories only: `sorted(set(cat.group_name for cat in active_categories))` (settings.py:207, where active_categories is filtered on `c.is_active`). Both feed the same `group_names` dropdown (settings/_categories.html and categories/_category_row.html iterate it).
- **Why it matters:** After creating a category via HTMX, the returned row's group-assignment dropdown can list group names that exist only on archived categories, which the user does not see when they reload the settings page. The two render paths present a different set of selectable groups for the same UI control, an inconsistency in account/category dropdown contents (the special-mandate dropdown-ordering/consistency item).
- **Suggested fix:** Add `.filter_by(user_id=current_user.id, is_active=True)` (or reuse the settings helper) so the HTMX group list matches the GET path's active-only set.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read both code paths and confirmed the claim. categories.py:96-108 (HTMX branch of create_category) builds group_names from db.session.query(Category.group_name).filter_by(user_id=current_user.id).distinct() at lines 98-103 -- NO is_active filter. The full-page GET path in settings.py _load_categories_context (lines 195-209) derives active_categories = [c for c in all_categories if c.is_active] (line 201) and then "group_names": sorted(set(cat.group_name for cat in active_categories)) (line 207) -- active-only. Both feed the same UI control: _category_row.html:44 ({% for g in group_names %} in the HTMX-appended row's group select) and settings/_categories.html:54,156 (the GET-rendered add/edit dropdowns). So the two render paths present a different set of selectable groups for the same control; after an HTMX create, the returned row's group dropdown can list groups that exist only on archived categories, which the user does not see on a settings reload. The discrepancy only manifests when every category of some group has been archived (otherwise the group still appears on an active category), making this a narrow real edge case -- LOW severity, not HIGH. Confirmed NOT test-covered: test_create_category_htmx (test_categories.py:105-115) only asserts b"Netflix" in resp.data, never the group_names contents; the archive tests (test_categories.py:1429-1646) cover settings/grid/template dropdowns but never the HTMX _category_row group list. Not P-1 (loan escrow), not P-3 (negative deduction), not a documented disable. Fix is mechanical (add is_active=True to the filter_by, or reuse the settings helper), so it is a defect to fix rather than a design judgment -- CONFIRMED, not NEEDS-DECISION.

### 42. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] _apply_shadow_update omits db.session.rollback() on NotFoundError/ValidationError, unlike every sibling shadow handler
- **Location:** `app/routes/transactions/mutations.py` :: 98-104
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** In _apply_shadow_update the except (NotFoundError, ValidationError) branch (lines 103-104) returns 'str(exc), 400' WITHOUT calling db.session.rollback(). transfer_service.update_transfer mutates xfer.amount and both shadow.estimated_amount in-memory (transfer_service.py:618-622) BEFORE _apply_status_change runs verify_transition (transfer_service.py:629 -> :525), which raises ValidationError for an illegal transition. A PATCH carrying both estimated_amount and an illegal status_id therefore leaves dirty amount/category mutations staged in the session when the route returns. Every parallel handler does roll back: _mark_done_shadow (mutations.py:432-434), _cancel_shadow (mutations.py:702-703), and the regular path _apply_regular_update (mutations.py:235-237).
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistent with the documented invariant-4 enforcement and with all sibling handlers. Flask-SQLAlchemy's per-request teardown calls db.session.remove() so the dirty state is discarded at request end rather than persisted, which is why this is not data-loss HIGH; but the asymmetry is a latent bug -- any future code that performs additional DB work after this branch in the same request, or any change to teardown behavior, would flush the half-applied transfer mutation and silently corrupt the transfer + both shadows (transfer invariant 3).
- **Suggested fix:** Add db.session.rollback() as the first line of the except (NotFoundError, ValidationError) block in _apply_shadow_update, matching _cancel_shadow and _mark_done_shadow.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE - every cited fact verified against committed code:
- app/routes/transactions/mutations.py:103-104: the `except (NotFoundError, ValidationError) as exc:` branch in `_apply_shadow_update` returns `str(exc), 400` with NO `db.session.rollback()`. Confirmed by reading lines 93-104.
- app/services/transfer_service.py:618-622: `update_transfer` mutates `xfer.amount`, `expense_shadow.estimated_amount`, `income_shadow.estimated_amount` when "amount" in kwargs.
- transfer_service.py:628-629 then 524-525: the status block runs AFTER the amount block and `_apply_status_change` calls `verify_transition(xfer.status_id, new_status_id, context="transfer")` at line 525, which raises ValidationError on an illegal transition. So a PATCH carrying both estimated_amount and an illegal status_id stages dirty amount mutations on xfer + both shadows, then raises before status propagation. No rollback exists anywhere in update_transfer (grep of rollback in transfer_service.py shows none inside lines 574-690).
- Sibling asymmetry confirmed: _mark_done_shadow rolls back at mutations.py:433-434, _cancel_shadow at 702-703, and _apply_regular_update's IntegrityError branch at 235-237.

REAL but ZERO CURRENT DATA IMPACT:
- Caller flow: update_transaction route at mutations.py:335 returns _apply_shadow_update(...) directly; the except returns at line 104 -> route returns the tuple. NO further DB work occurs in this request after the except branch.
- No custom teardown override in app/__init__.py (only the 500 errorhandler rollback at :591 and the seed rollback at :882). Flask-SQLAlchemy==3.1.1 (requirements.txt) registers the default teardown_appcontext calling db.session.remove() at request end, so the uncommitted dirty state is discarded -- no corruption persists. The finding itself acknowledges "not data-loss HIGH" and calls it "latent."

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not P-1 (loan escrow) nor P-3 (negative deduction). The closest register entry is deep-quality-hunt.md #21 (no settled-row immutability guard on edits, NEEDS-DECISION) which is a DISTINCT issue. grep for "rollback" in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/deep-quality-hunt.md returns nothing, and quality-pass.md has no row for transactions/mutations.py. So the rollback-omission asymmetry is novel.

VERDICT NEEDS-DECISION / LOW: The asymmetry is genuine and matches a real defensive pattern used by all three sibling handlers in the same file, but it produces no current data corruption (teardown discards the session). Whether to add db.session.rollback() for consistency/future-proofing vs. accept reliance on per-request teardown is a developer judgment, and severity is LOW not MED given zero present impact. The suggested one-line fix (add db.session.rollback() as the first line of the except block) is correct, cheap, and consistent with _cancel_shadow/_mark_done_shadow if the developer chooses to harden it.

### 43. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] _check_pwned_password ignores the HIBP breach count, contradicting its own docstring and inline comment
- **Location:** `app/services/auth_service.py` :: 238-256 (matcher); 176-181 and 239-243 (docstrings/comment)
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** auth-sec
- **Claim:** The behaviour-matrix docstring (lines 176-178) states a match is rejected only 'with a count > 0', and the inline comment (lines 239-243) claims a 'non-integer count' line is skipped as a protocol violation. The actual loop never reads or parses parts[1] (the count): it only checks `len(parts) != 2` then compares `parts[0].strip().upper() == suffix` and raises unconditionally on a suffix match. A line with a malformed/non-integer count whose suffix matches is NOT skipped, and a count of 0 still raises. The test _hibp_response_for docstring even concedes 'zero counts ... the suffix still raises if it matches', confirming the code, not the docstring.
- **Why it matters:** Practically harmless (HIBP padding suffixes are random 35-hex, so a count-0 collision with a real suffix is ~2^-140), but the documentation actively misstates the security contract a future maintainer will rely on. Rule 2/3 (read before write, no guessing) means the next editor could 'fix' the count gating to match the docstring and change behavior, or assume malformed lines are filtered when they are not.
- **Suggested fix:** Either delete the count-gating language from the docstring/comment to match the unconditional suffix-match behavior, or add the documented `int(parts[1]) > 0` check (wrapped to skip non-integer counts) so code and docs agree.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/services/auth_service.py:238-256. The matcher loop does exactly what the finding states: line 244 `parts = line.split(":", 1)`; lines 245-246 `if len(parts) != 2: continue`; line 247 `record_suffix = parts[0].strip().upper()`; line 248 `if record_suffix == suffix:` -> raise ValidationError (253-256). parts[1] (the count) is NEVER read or parsed anywhere in the function. So: (a) a count of 0 with a matching suffix still raises (no `> 0` gate), and (b) a malformed/non-integer count with a matching suffix (e.g. "<suffix>:abc", len(parts)==2) is NOT skipped -- it raises.

Docstring/comment contradictions confirmed: lines 176-178 state a match raises only "with a count > 0" -- not implemented. Lines 239-243 claim an invalid line including "non-integer count" is skipped as a protocol violation -- false; only the no-colon case (len(parts)!=2) is skipped. Line 221 separately says padded zero-count lines are "ignored" by the loop, which is true only because their suffixes differ, not because of count gating.

The test helper at tests/test_services/test_auth_service.py:986-988 explicitly concedes the code's actual behavior: "zero counts are HIBP padding noise and the service treats them like normal lines (the suffix still raises if it matches)" -- corroborating the code over the main docstring. Test coverage: test_breached_password_raises_validation_error (1045) uses count=42; test_malformed_response_line_skipped (1185-1201) only covers the no-colon line; there is NO test for a non-integer count with a matching suffix and NO test asserting count-0 gating, so the documented contract is both contradicted and untested.

Not already known: the only auth_service entries in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/plan.md (lines 810, 843, 2097, 2229) concern an unrelated import-outside-toplevel hoist at line 804; no quality-pass ACCEPT row, documented disable, or P-1/P-3 covers _check_pwned_password or HIBP count gating.

Severity LOW is correct: practical impact is negligible (HIBP padding suffixes are random 35-hex; a count-0 collision with the real suffix is astronomically improbable, and genuine breach records carry count>=1). This is a documentation-vs-code discrepancy / maintenance hazard under rules 2-3, not a money or live-security defect. The fix direction (delete the count-gating language vs. add an `int(parts[1]) > 0` check) is a developer judgment, but the discrepancy itself is unambiguous and independently confirmed from the code.

### 44. [CORRECTNESS/DEFECT] Dashboard cash-runway expense query omits the scenario_id filter (cross-scenario aggregation)
- **Location:** `app/services/dashboard_service.py` :: 454-467
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** _compute_cash_runway filters settled expenses by account_id, is_deleted, status_id, transaction_type_id, and due_date window, but NOT by scenario_id -- unlike every other expense query in this service (_get_upcoming_bills line 149, _sum_settled_expenses line 664) which all filter `Transaction.scenario_id == scenario_id`. The caller already resolved a baseline scenario but does not pass it here.
- **Why it matters:** For a user with more than one scenario on the same account, recent settled expenses from non-baseline scenarios are summed into the daily-average spend, overstating spending and understating the cash-runway days shown on the dashboard.
- **Suggested fix:** Thread scenario_id into _compute_cash_runway and add `Transaction.scenario_id == scenario_id` to the filter, matching the other dashboard expense queries.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE (verified): app/services/dashboard_service.py:454-467 -- _compute_cash_runway's settled-expense query filters Transaction.account_id, is_deleted.is_(False), status_id.in_(settled_ids = DONE/RECEIVED/SETTLED), transaction_type_id == EXPENSE, and the due_date window (>= thirty_days_ago, <= today), but NOT scenario_id. The two sibling expense queries in the same file DO filter scenario: _get_upcoming_bills at line 149 (Transaction.scenario_id == scenario_id) and _sum_settled_expenses at line 664 (same). Caller chain confirmed: compute_dashboard_data (line 44) resolves scenario = get_baseline_scenario(user_id) at line 65, but _get_balance_info(account, current_period, balance_results) at lines 88-90 is NOT passed scenario, and it calls _compute_cash_runway(account.id, current_balance) at line 419 with no scenario_id. So the filter is genuinely absent and the scenario was never threaded down.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable. The quality-pass register (docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md) touches dashboard_service only for R0801/DRY clusters. Its 3e note (lines 536-537: "dashboard correctly needs none") concerns the _get_upcoming_bills query at dashboard_service[145:151] (the scenario-filtered one), NOT the cash-runway query at 454-467. So this specific omission was never reviewed/accepted.

IS IT A REAL ISSUE -- but no LIVE impact today: Transaction.scenario_id is nullable=False (app/models/transaction.py:152-156), so every txn belongs to exactly one scenario. Decisively, NO production code path creates a non-baseline scenario: every Scenario(...) construction across app/, scripts/, and migrations/ is is_baseline=True -- app/services/auth_service.py:818, app/routes/grid.py:577 (create_baseline, idempotent), scripts/seed_user.py:178, scripts/benchmark_triggers.py:80. Multi-scenario clone/compare is explicitly Phase 3 future work (app/models/scenario.py:4-5: "Phase 1 uses only the baseline scenario; Phase 3 adds clone, compare, and diff features"). get_baseline_scenario filters is_baseline=True and the partial unique index uq_scenarios_one_baseline guarantees one baseline per user. Therefore the "user with >1 scenario on the same account" precondition in why_it_matters cannot be reached by any shipping code; the result set is byte-identical with or without the filter today, so the overstated-spending/understated-runway harm does not currently occur (Rule 13 territory for the LIVE claim). No test covers a cross-scenario cash-runway case (tests/test_services/test_dashboard_service.py:678-704 use a single seeded scenario only). HOWEVER this is a genuine latent consistency defect, not impossible-by-construction gold-plating: it diverges from the two sibling queries in the same file and becomes a live cross-scenario data leak the instant Phase 3 ships -- a class (scenario spill) the scenario_resolver docstring explicitly guards ("queries that must NOT spill into what-if scenarios"). Whether to add the one-line filter prophylactically now (cheap, matches siblings) or defer it to Phase 3 with the rest of the multi-scenario plumbing is a developer judgment, hence NEEDS-DECISION. Severity corrected MED->LOW because there is zero impact under any currently-shippable state.

### 45. [DECIMAL/DEFECT] FicaConfig Python column defaults are float literals on Numeric money columns (same class of bug C24-5 fixed for investment_params, left unfixed here)
- **Location:** `app/models/tax_config.py` :: 203-222
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** models-schema
- **Claim:** FicaConfig declares ss_rate default=0.0620 (line 204), ss_wage_base default=176100 (208), medicare_rate default=0.0145 (212), medicare_surtax_rate default=0.0090 (216), medicare_surtax_threshold default=200000 (220) -- all Python float/int literals passed as `default=` to db.Numeric columns. The 0.0620/0.0145/0.0090 values are binary floats, exactly the imprecision E-11/E-28 prohibits; tests/test_schemas/test_c24_domain_reconciliation.py::TestC24_5AssumedReturnDefault fixed the structurally identical InvestmentParams.assumed_annual_return (was default=0.07000 float, changed to Decimal('0.07000')) but the FicaConfig defaults were never converted. The shekel-decimal-from-float checker (tools/pylint/shekel_checkers.py only flags Decimal(<float>) constructor calls, not `default=<float>` on a Column) does not catch this, so it passed the gate.
- **Why it matters:** Any code path that reads Column.default.arg (ORM-side default resolution, introspection, a future seed that pulls the column default) sees a float and propagates float imprecision into FICA tax math; the audit explicitly classified this exact pattern as a defect worth a pinned test for investment_params, so the same column shape on FICA rate columns is an unfixed instance of a known bug.
- **Suggested fix:** Change each float `default=` to a Decimal-from-string, e.g. default=Decimal('0.0620'), matching the InvestmentParams.assumed_annual_return fix, and add the FicaConfig columns to a default-type assertion mirroring TestC24_5.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUAL: app/models/tax_config.py:203-222 declares exactly the float/int literals claimed -- ss_rate default=0.0620 (204), ss_wage_base default=176100 (208), medicare_rate default=0.0145 (212), medicare_surtax_rate default=0.0090 (216), medicare_surtax_threshold default=200000 (220), all as Python `default=` on db.Numeric columns (server_default is the correct SQL-string counterpart, e.g. db.text("0.0620")). C24-5 fix is real and structurally identical: app/models/investment_params.py:104-107 uses default=Decimal("0.07000"), with a comment at :95-103 explaining the pre-fix float 0.07000 was the E-11/E-28 defect. The shekel-decimal-from-float checker only flags Decimal(<float>) constructor calls, not default=<float> on a Column -- consistent with the claim that it passed the gate.

REAL ISSUE: The Python default= is reachable in principle (SQLAlchemy emits the Python default on an ORM INSERT that omits the column). The three ORM construction sites -- app/services/auth_service.py:470, app/routes/salary/tax_config.py:126, scripts/seed_tax_brackets.py:127 -- all currently pass **data containing all five fields (DEFAULT_FICA at auth_service.py:405-421 always supplies all five as Decimal(...); FicaConfigSchema at app/schemas/validation.py:943-962 marks all five required=True), so the float is not resolved at runtime today. But the float literal is still non-compliant per E-11/E-28 and Column.default.arg introspection sees a float. No production code reads .default.arg (grep found only the comment at investment_params.py:101), so no live money-math path consumes the float -- hence LOW, not MED.

NOT TEST-COVERED: tests/test_models/test_c25_column_invariants.py:314 (test_fica_configs_rate_defaults_fire_on_raw_insert) uses a RAW SQL INSERT (db.text), which exercises only the PostgreSQL server_default, never the Python default.arg. test_f134_columns_have_restored_server_default (:153-176) also asserts only server_default via pg_attrdef. The C24-5 test pattern (tests/test_schemas/test_c24_domain_reconciliation.py:317-330, col.default.arg isinstance Decimal) was applied to investment_params but NOT mirrored to fica_configs. So the Python-default-type assertion is genuinely absent.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: docs/audits/financial_calculations/08_findings.md HIGH-06 (:1101, :1135-1137, :2390) names ONLY investment_params.assumed_annual_return as the float-default facet; FicaConfig float defaults are not listed there, not in the quality-pass register, and not P-1/P-3.

Fix is mechanical (default=Decimal('0.0620') etc. + a mirror default-type test), not a financial/design judgment, so CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION.

### 46. [DECIMAL/DEFECT] Truthiness used on Decimal money: `or "0"` in create_account and `if data.get('inflation_rate')`
- **Location:** `app/routes/accounts/crud.py` :: 162 (crud.py); salary/items.py:344 and 517
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** crud.py:162 does `Decimal(str(data.pop("anchor_balance", "0") or "0"))`. Since the schema already loads `anchor_balance` as a Decimal, a legitimately-submitted zero opening balance arrives as `Decimal("0.00")`, which is FALSY, so `Decimal("0.00") or "0"` evaluates the right operand `"0"` -- the value happens to stay 0 but the branch is driven by money-truthiness, exactly what coding-standards forbids ('A zero balance is not a missing balance'). The same anti-pattern appears in salary/items.py:344 and :517 (`if data.get("inflation_rate"):` skips the /100 conversion for a 0% rate; harmless in value because 0/100=0 but driven by truthiness), while the adjacent percentage handling correctly uses `is not None` (items.py:76, 244).
- **Why it matters:** Relying on Decimal truthiness is a latent bug pattern in a money app: the next refactor that changes the surrounding logic (e.g. preserving a sentinel, or a field where 0 and missing must differ) will silently mishandle exactly-zero values. It also flags the file as not honoring its own stated standard.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `is None` checks: `raw = data.pop("anchor_balance", None); anchor_balance = raw if raw is not None else Decimal("0")`; and `if data.get("inflation_rate") is not None:` in items.py.
- **Verifier evidence:** All three claims verified against the committed code.

crud.py:162 reads exactly: `anchor_balance = Decimal(str(data.pop("anchor_balance", "0") or "0"))`. AccountCreateSchema (app/schemas/validation.py:1318-1327) declares `anchor_balance = fields.Decimal(places=2, as_string=True)` -- NOT required, and a `@pre_load` strips empty strings. I reproduced marshmallow load + the line via Python: a submitted "0" loads to `Decimal('0.00')` which is FALSY, so `Decimal('0.00') or "0"` evaluates the right operand `"0"` -- the branch is driven by Decimal-truthiness, exactly what coding-standards forbid. Final value is `Decimal('0')` in all of {zero, empty, absent} cases, so there is NO current money defect; the value is correct by construction.

salary/items.py:344 and :517 read exactly `if data.get("inflation_rate"):`. The deduction schema field (app/schemas/validation.py:821-824) uses `_PERCENT_INPUT_RANGE` = `validate.Range(min=Decimal("0"), max=Decimal("100"))` -- min INCLUSIVE -- so a 0% rate is a legitimate submission. A submitted Decimal("0") is falsy, so the `/Decimal("100")` conversion is skipped; but 0/100=0, so the stored value is identical and correct. Confirmed the adjacent percentage handling at items.py:76 and :244 correctly uses `if data.get("percentage") is not None:`, so the file is internally inconsistent.

Standard violated: .claude/rules/coding.md / docs/coding-standards.md: "Do not rely on truthiness for business logic. Write `if amount is None:`, not `if not amount:`. A zero balance is not a missing balance."

NOT already known: the existing truthiness guard test `test_no_truthiness_on_financial_values` (tests/test_services/test_retirement_dashboard_service.py:944) calls `inspect.getsource(retirement_dashboard_service)` -- scoped to that ONE service module; it does not cover accounts/crud.py or salary/items.py. The create-account test at tests/test_routes/test_accounts.py:347 DOES POST `anchor_balance: "0"` but only asserts the duplicate-name guard ("created"/"already exists"); it never asserts the stored `current_anchor_balance == Decimal("0")`, so the zero-create value path is unverified. The quality-pass rows for crud.py (53809b5, quality-pass.md:400) and salary/items.py (b137e06, quality-pass.md:410) covered create_account bundling and the tm-return collapse respectively -- neither flagged or ACCEPTed the `or "0"` / `if data.get("inflation_rate"):` truthiness. Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable.

Severity LOW: no actual money mismanagement today (both branches yield the identical correct value); this is a genuine but latent violation of the codebase's own stated standard -- a trap a future refactor (where 0 and missing must differ) would silently break. The suggested `is None` fix is correct and low-stakes; whether to apply now is a minor developer judgment but does not change that the finding is accurate and real.

### 47. [DRY/DEFECT] Account ownership check re-inlined 7+ times bypassing get_or_404, silently dropping the IDOR audit-log event
- **Location:** `app/routes/accounts/anchor.py` :: 67-69, 176-178, 190-192, 240-242, 319-321, 335-337; also investment.py:92-94, accounts/detail.py:307, loan/_helpers.py:75
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** anchor.py loads Account six times via db.session.get(Account, id) then checks 'if account is None or account.user_id != current_user.id: return Not found, 404' (67-69, 176-178, 190-192, 240-242, 319-321, 335-337); investment.py:92-94 does the same in growth_chart even though that file already imports and uses get_or_404 at line 61. get_or_404 (auth_helpers.py:122-179) implements this exact ownership rule AND emits the structured access_denied_cross_user / resource_not_found log_event that audit finding F-144 added as the IDOR forensic trail (auth_helpers.py docstring 25-31). These inline copies emit no such event.
- **Why it matters:** Beyond DRY: cross-user probes of anchor-balance and investment endpoints (high-value, fresh-login-gated routes) leave no application-tier security log, defeating the F-144 IDOR detection that every get_or_404 site provides. A one-sided change to the ownership/logging rule would not propagate to these 7+ hand-rolled copies.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace each inline db.session.get + cross-user check with account = get_or_404(Account, account_id); if account is None: abort(404).
- **Verifier evidence:** CODE VERIFIED. anchor.py has 6 inline checks `db.session.get(Account, account_id)` + `if account is None or account.user_id != current_user.id: return "...", 404` at lines 67-69, 176-178, 190-192, 240-242, 319-321, 335-337 (response bodies vary: "Not found" / "Account not found"). investment.py growth_chart inlines the same at lines 92-94 (returns "",404) while the SAME file's dashboard/POST handlers use get_or_404(Account,...) at 61,155,258. detail.py:306-308 inlines it while detail.py:137,220 use get_or_404. loan/_helpers.py:74-76 inlines it. Citation nit: the finding lists the investment path as app/routes/accounts/investment.py; the real file is app/routes/investment.py (content claim correct).

get_or_404 (auth_helpers.py:154-179) implements the identical ownership rule AND emits log_event(EVT_RESOURCE_NOT_FOUND, INFO) on missing-PK and log_event(EVT_ACCESS_DENIED_CROSS_USER, WARNING) on cross-user -- the F-144 forensic trail (module docstring 25-31; findings.md:5526-5551, "Fixed in C-14"). The inline copies emit NEITHER. CLAIM "these inline copies emit no such event" CONFIRMED.

REACHABILITY: every cited anchor/investment route is @require_owner-decorated, but require_owner (auth_helpers.py:104-118) only log_events the role-deny (companion), not the cross-user owner-vs-owner case. The IDOR test fixture second_user (conftest.py:1410-1416) sets no role_id, so require_owner's getattr fallback (line 106) treats User B as OWNER -> owner-vs-owner probes pass require_owner and hit the silent inline check. So the cross-user IDOR event IS dropped on a reachable path.

NOT TEST-COVERED: test_access_control.py exercises these exact routes (test_inline_anchor_update_blocked:133, test_true_up_blocked:174, anchor-form/display, hysa_detail:212) but asserts ONLY status==404 (_assert_not_found:49). The cross-user event IS asserted for get_or_404 (test_auth_helpers.py:503-519) proving it is a live contract, but NO test asserts these inline routes emit it -- the gap is genuinely uncovered.

NOT ALREADY-KNOWN (precise sense): quality-pass.md row 29 (anchor.py, ab16669) ACCEPTed the refactor's behavior-equivalence (conflict helper, success-merge, "6 returns map 1:1 to 6 HTTP outcomes") but never evaluated get_or_404-vs-inline.
