F-087 (findings.md:3969) covers the 302-vs-404 convention on a DIFFERENT axis -- these routes already return 404 so they are NOT in F-087's list. Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable. Closely adjacent to F-087's deferred maintainability theme but a distinct observation.

SEVERITY: MED overstated. F-144 itself is Low; F-087 is Low (proposed deflation to Info). Access is correctly DENIED (404) in every case -- the gap is logging/observability + DRY, not data exposure. Corrected to LOW.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION not CONFIRMED: the inline checks are verbatim-preserved legacy from the pre-split monolith (anchor.py created in 85cdba4 "behaviour preserved verbatim"; module docstring says so). The developer has a documented disposition to leave 404-returning legacy inline patterns at Low/Info priority (F-087 deflation). Retrofitting get_or_404 is a prioritization judgment on F-144/F-087 follow-through, and the suggested fix as written would NOT preserve the per-site response-body differences ("Not found" vs "Account not found" vs "") for the HTMX fragments -- a developer call on whether that matters.

### 48. [LAZY/DEFECT] Orphaned, unreachable '# pylint: enable=duplicate-code' in retirement.update_settings
- **Location:** `app/routes/retirement.py` :: 386
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** Line 386 is '# pylint: enable=duplicate-code' sitting INSIDE the if errors: block, immediately after the return render_template(...), 422 statement (retirement.py:369-385). There is no matching '# pylint: disable=duplicate-code' anywhere in the file (grep confirms only the enable exists). It is both dead code (after a return, never reached) and a no-op directive (pylint silently ignores a lone enable, so useless-suppression does not flag it -- verified: pylint app/routes/retirement.py --enable=useless-suppression rates 10.00/10).
- **Why it matters:** A reader sees the enable and reasonably assumes a scoped disable block exists above; there is none. It is misleading leftover from a removed disable and violates the project's fixed-place disable-rationale convention (a disable/enable pair must be intentional and documented).
- **Suggested fix:** Delete the stray '# pylint: enable=duplicate-code' line at retirement.py:386.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/routes/retirement.py:350-399. Line 386 is exactly "        # pylint: enable=duplicate-code", sitting inside the `if errors:` block immediately after `return render_template(...), 422` (lines 369-385) -- so it is unreachable dead code. grep confirms it is the ONLY pylint directive in the file; there is NO matching `# pylint: disable=duplicate-code` anywhere. `pylint app/routes/retirement.py --enable=useless-suppression` => 10.00/10 (a lone `enable` is silently ignored, so no gate flags it). All three sub-claims of the finding hold.

Git archaeology confirms the mechanism precisely: commit 6475429c (2026-06-04, "document 13 incidental duplicate-code clusters") added a PAIRED block -- `# pylint: disable=duplicate-code` plus an 8-line rationale at ~line 367, and `# pylint: enable=duplicate-code` at line 386. The re-audit commit 3d34aa8c (2026-06-07, run w1a7fwxl3, "remove 4 dead duplicate-code disables") deleted the disable directive and its rationale in a single hunk (`@@ -366,14 +366,6 @@`, 14 lines -> 6) but NEVER touched line 386 (`git show 3d34aa8c -- app/routes/retirement.py` has exactly one hunk, no reference to the enable). The enable was simply missed. The other three siblings in that commit (dashboard_service.py:667, models/account.py:159, accounts/detail.py:121) were one-sided `disable`s with no `enable` partner, so they had nothing to orphan -- retirement was the only paired block and only half was removed.

The project's own gate cannot catch this: tools/pylint/shekel_checkers.py:58-60 shows `_DISABLE_RE` deliberately matches `disable=` only, not `enable=`; pylint `unreachable` does not fire on comment lines.

already_known=false: not P-1/P-3 (both financial). The disable it once paired with was deleted, so it is not a documented disable. quality-pass.md has rows for retirement_dashboard_service.py (line 122) and retirement_gap_calculator.py (lines 136, 201-210, 352-354) but NO row covering this orphaned enable in routes/retirement.py::update_settings; grep for "orphan"/"enable=duplicate"/"stray enable" in the cleanup docs returns nothing relevant.

Severity LOW is correct: zero behavioral/financial impact (cosmetic), but a genuine leftover that misleads readers and violates the project's intentional-disable convention. Suggested fix (delete line 386) is correct.

### 49. [LAZY/DEFECT] Dangling `# pylint: enable=duplicate-code` after a return, with no matching disable
- **Location:** `app/routes/retirement.py` :: 386
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** Line 386 is `# pylint: enable=duplicate-code` placed AFTER the `return ..., 422` on line 385 inside `update_settings`, and there is no `# pylint: disable=duplicate-code` anywhere in retirement.py (confirmed via grep: the only hit is the enable on line 386). It is therefore an enable with no matching disable, sitting after a return. `pylint app/routes/retirement.py --enable=useless-suppression,unreachable` rates 10.00/10 and flags nothing, so every mechanical gate misses it.
- **Why it matters:** It is a leftover artifact from the duplicate-code cleanup. It falsely signals to a reader that a duplicate-code-suppressed region exists in this function (it does not), and the surrounding hand-written ~10-kwarg context block it sits next to is the real cruft it was paired with. Dead/misleading directives erode trust in the disable annotations the project relies on.
- **Suggested fix:** Delete line 386.
- **Verifier evidence:** app/routes/retirement.py:386 is exactly `# pylint: enable=duplicate-code`, placed immediately after `return ..., 422` on line 385 inside update_settings() (read lines 340-399). grep -n "# pylint" over the whole file returns ONLY line 386 -- there is no matching `# pylint: disable=duplicate-code` anywhere in retirement.py, and the module header (lines 1-30) has no module-level disable. So it is an enable with no preceding disable, and it sits after a return (flow-unreachable). It is inert: an enable only reverts a prior disable, so it suppresses/reverts nothing, yet it falsely signals to a reader that a duplicate-code-suppressed region exists in this function. `pylint app/routes/retirement.py --enable=useless-suppression,unreachable` rates 10.00/10 and flags nothing -- useless-suppression fires only on a disable that suppresses nothing (not a dangling enable), and the comment is not treated as an unreachable statement -- so every mechanical gate misses it; only human reading catches it. Not a P-1/P-3 item, not a documented justified disable (carries no `Pylint:` why-comment; the rationale gate does not apply to enable), and not tied to the quality-pass items referenced. Genuine but cosmetic/maintainability only: no financial, behavioral, or test impact. Fix = delete line 386.

### 50. [LAZY/DEFECT] update_tax_config silently no-ops (no flash, no row) on first save when flat_rate is omitted
- **Location:** `app/routes/salary/tax_config.py` :: 61-93
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** In `update_tax_config`, when no `StateTaxConfig` row exists yet and the submitted `flat_rate` is None (the schema does not mark `flat_rate` required, validation.py:975), the `else` branch's `if flat_rate is not None:` (tax_config.py:74) is false, so NO config is created and NO flash is emitted -- yet the handler still runs `_regenerate_all_salary_transactions()` and commits (tax_config.py:86-90) and redirects. The user submits the form, nothing is created, and they get no success/error feedback. (When a row already exists, the `standard_deduction` is updated even if flat_rate is None, but at least flashes 'updated'.)
- **Why it matters:** A tax-config save that silently does nothing with no message is a misleading UX in a financial setting -- the user believes they configured a state rate that was never persisted, and projections silently keep using the prior (or no) rate. Per CLAUDE.md rule 'fail loud, not with silent defaults.'
- **Suggested fix:** In the new-config/no-flat-rate branch, flash a clear 'A flat rate is required to create a state tax config.' (danger) and return before the regenerate/commit; or make flat_rate required when creating.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read all cited code. CLAIM IS ACCURATE on every point:

1. app/routes/salary/tax_config.py:55-56 -- flat_rate defaults to None, only set when data.get("flat_rate") is not None.
2. app/schemas/validation.py:975-978 -- StateTaxConfigSchema.flat_rate has NO required=True (only places=2, as_string, Range(0,100)). The class (line 965) has only a strip_empty_strings @pre_load (968-970) that drops "" values and NO @validates_schema, so a submitted empty/absent flat_rate passes validation and arrives as None via data.get (line 56). Confirmed via grep: no validates_schema between class def (965) and end of class (988).
3. tax_config.py:67-84 -- when no existing row (else, line 72) AND flat_rate is None, the guard `if flat_rate is not None:` (line 74) is False, so NO StateTaxConfig is created and NO flash fires.
4. tax_config.py:86-93 -- it nonetheless commits, calls _regenerate_all_salary_transactions(), commits again, and redirects -- the user gets zero feedback and no row.
5. Asymmetry confirmed: the existing-row branch (line 67-71) always flashes "...updated." and updates standard_deduction even when flat_rate is None.

REAL ISSUE, EDGE-ONLY: The browser form input is marked HTML `required` (app/templates/settings/_tax_config_sections.html:60-61), so a normal browser user cannot trigger this; it requires a scripted/HTMX/curl POST that omits flat_rate. So it is NOT a normal-flow defect and NOT money-corruption (nothing wrong is persisted; the prior/no rate simply remains). It IS a genuine silent no-op with no feedback, contrary to the project's "fail loud, not with silent defaults" rule. Not rule-13 gold-plating because the schema genuinely permits the omission. TEST GAP confirmed: all 9 tax-config POST tests in tests/test_routes/test_salary.py (1393-1412, 1436-1446, 1986-1992, 2074-2081) supply flat_rate; grep found no test for missing/empty flat_rate creation.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md (the only tax-related ACCEPT rows are #3 query-family and the P-3 negative-deduction row), not in plan.md, no inline pylint disable in tax_config.py, and distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction).

Severity LOW is correct: not reachable via the normal UI, no incorrect financial data persisted. The cleanest fix is to make flat_rate required when creating (add required=True or a @validates_schema requiring it for new rows) or flash danger + return before commit -- a small input-validation choice rather than a financial-logic decision, so CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION.

### 51. [LAZY/DEFECT] Unreachable 'new_balance < 0' rounding guards in _apply_override_payment and _apply_contractual_payment
- **Location:** `app/services/amortization_engine.py` :: 406-409 (_apply_override_payment), 457-461 (_apply_contractual_payment)
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** loan-amort
- **Claim:** In _apply_override_payment the only path reaching line 406 has principal_portion < balance (the principal_portion >= balance case returns early at 403-405), so balance - principal_portion is strictly positive and round_money(positive) can never be < 0 -- the guard at 408-409 is dead code. In _apply_contractual_payment, extra is capped by min(extra_monthly, balance - principal_portion) and floored at 0 (lines 455-456), so balance - principal_portion - extra >= 0, making the new_balance < 0 branch at 459-461 equally unreachable. I verified the override path cannot produce a negative pre-clamp balance.
- **Why it matters:** CLAUDE.md rule 13 forbids 'error handling for impossible scenarios.' These guards' comments claim to 'guard against sub-penny negative balance from rounding,' but the prior caps make that impossible, so the comments mislead a future maintainer into believing rounding can drive these negative (it cannot here) and the extra-folding logic at 460 is never exercised by tests.
- **Suggested fix:** Remove the unreachable new_balance < 0 branches (and their comments), or, if kept as defense-in-depth, replace the comment with an assertion documenting they are unreachable given the upstream caps.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/services/amortization_engine.py:381-462 and app/utils/money.py:45-72.

FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- both guards are genuinely unreachable:
- _apply_override_payment: line 403 `if principal_portion >= balance:` returns early at 404-405. So line 406 is reached ONLY when principal_portion < balance, i.e. `balance - principal_portion` is STRICTLY positive. round_money (app/utils/money.py:72: quantize with ROUND_HALF_UP) of a strictly-positive Decimal can never be negative, so the `new_balance < 0` branch at 408-409 cannot fire.
- _apply_contractual_payment: line 455 `extra = min(extra_monthly, balance - principal_portion)` then line 456 `extra = max(extra, 0.00)`, so 0 <= extra <= balance - principal_portion, making the line-457 argument `balance - principal_portion - extra >= 0`. round_money(>=0) >= 0, so the branch at 459-461 (and the `extra += new_balance` fold at 460) is unreachable.
  Empirically confirmed: round_money of any non-negative Decimal (tested 0, 1E-9, 0.0049, 0.005, 0.4999999) is always >= 0; round_money of any strictly-positive Decimal is always >= 0.

The misleading-comment claim also holds: lines 407 and 458 say "Guard against sub-penny negative balance from rounding," but ROUND_HALF_UP of a non-negative value cannot produce a negative, so rounding cannot drive these negative given the upstream caps.

REAL ISSUE (minor): genuine dead code + a comment that overstates what round_money can do; rule 13 (no error handling for impossible scenarios) applies. NOT a correctness defect -- no money is mismanaged; severity LOW, not the only-evidence-of-a-bug kind. The caps that make the guards dead ARE tested: tests/test_services/test_amortization_engine.py:1093 (test_overpayment_cap_final_row exercises the contractual early-return cap) and :1006 (test_override_below_interest_negative_amortization exercises the override path); the guard branches themselves are NOT exercised by any test (none can be).

NOT already_known: quality-pass.md:120 marks amortization_engine.py "REVIEWED -- clean (7 ACCEPT)" and commit c4f01e6 (plan.md:2248) introduced these helpers, but the 7 enumerated ACCEPT rows (quality-pass.md:198,211,306) concern the AmortizationRow/PayoffRequest/ProjectionInputs param-object/DTO disables, and the dead-code that was actually examined (commit 0e8b986, plan.md:2247) was replay_confirmed_history/_build_payment_lookups -- a different item. These specific rounding guards were never individually flagged-and-accepted, and they are not P-1/P-3 nor a documented disable.

NEEDS-DECISION rather than CONFIRMED because (a) the finding itself offers two valid fixes (remove the dead branches vs. keep as defense-in-depth with a corrected comment/assertion) and which is correct under rule 13 vs. idiomatic financial cents-clamping is a developer judgment, and (b) the file already carries an overall "reviewed-clean" verdict, so reopening it is a developer call.

### 52. [SECURITY/DEFECT] Sensitive-scrubber comment claims a bare `token` key is redacted, but the regex catalogue only covers access_token/refresh_token
- **Location:** `app/utils/logging_config.py` :: 178-184
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** utils-infra
- **Claim:** The comment at lines 178-179 states ``api[_-]key`` and ``token`` catch the third-party SDK debug-line shape, but _SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES (lines 154-190) contains only `access[_-]token` and `refresh[_-]token`, never a standalone `token`. A log line such as `token=abcdef123` therefore passes the message/args scrub un-redacted; `token` is also absent from _SENSITIVE_EXTRA_FIELDS, so an `extra={'token': ...}` would only be caught if it matched a pattern, which it does not.
- **Why it matters:** The comment misleads a future maintainer into believing bare bearer/session tokens in a logged third-party debug line are scrubbed when they are not. In a money app this is a residual credential-leak path, and the inaccurate comment defeats the defense-in-depth audit the module documents.
- **Suggested fix:** Either add `r"token"` (anchored) to _SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES and `"token"` to _SENSITIVE_EXTRA_FIELDS, or correct the comment to say only access/refresh token forms are matched.
- **Verifier evidence:** CONFIRMED (raised to NEEDS-DECISION because the fix is a developer judgment call). Cited code reads exactly as the finding states. app/utils/logging_config.py:178-179 comment: "``api[_-]key`` and ``token`` catch the third-party SDK debug-line shape." But _SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES (lines 180-184) contains only r"cookie", r"authorization", r"api[_-]key", r"access[_-]token", r"refresh[_-]token" -- no standalone r"token". grep for 'r"token"'/'"token"' in the file returns nothing. Empirically verified: _scrub_text("token=abcdef123") -> "token=abcdef123" (un-redacted) and _scrub_text("token: secret999") -> unchanged, while _scrub_text("access_token=abcdef123") -> "access_token=[REDACTED]" and refresh_token redacts. The (?<![A-Za-z0-9_]) lookbehind on access[_-]token/refresh[_-]token requires the access/refresh prefix, so a bare token= has nothing to match. Extra-field path: bare "token" not in _SENSITIVE_EXTRA_FIELDS (lines 236-262, only access_token/refresh_token present); that path is exact-name match, so extra={'token': ...} is not caught, and the pattern fallback only matches embedded key=value forms (verified _SENSITIVE_PATTERNS[1].search('plain-bearer-abc') is None). is_real_issue: genuine inaccurate comment that over-claims scrub coverage; the only test touching this (tests/test_utils/test_logging_scrubber.py:396) uses "token password=hunter2 end" merely as a leading decoy to verify password= matching, NOT bare-token redaction -- so the gap is uncovered by tests. Severity stays LOW: the module docstring (lines 336-338) explicitly states it is "Defense-in-depth, not the primary control," so this is a documentation/comment-accuracy defect in a secondary control, not a primary leak. already_known=false: docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/{plan,quality-pass}.md reference logging_config only for import-cycle KEEP disables (logging_config:543) and R0801 attribution (logging_config:1) -- nothing about the scrubber comment or token coverage; not P-1/P-3. NEEDS-DECISION because the two fixes differ materially: adding r"token" would also redact benign keys like csrf_token/next_token in logs (over-redaction), vs. correcting the comment to claim only access/refresh forms -- a developer call on whether bare bearer/session tokens warrant catch-all coverage.

### 53. [SECURITY/DEFECT] set_cookie underscore form is in the extras redaction set but not the message/args regex catalogue
- **Location:** `app/utils/logging_config.py` :: 180,236-262
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** utils-infra
- **Claim:** _SENSITIVE_EXTRA_FIELDS includes `"set_cookie"` (line 255) but _SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES only has `r"cookie"` (line 180). Because the value regexes anchor the key with the negative lookbehind `(?<![A-Za-z0-9_])` (lines 207, 221) and `_` is inside that class, the underscore form `set_cookie=...` inside record.msg or record.args is NOT matched by the pattern scrub (the `_` before `cookie` blocks it). Only the hyphen form (`set-cookie`, `Set-Cookie`) matches, since `-` is outside the lookbehind class.
- **Why it matters:** A future caller who logs a `set_cookie=<session>` fragment in a free-form message string (not as a discrete extra) would leak the signed session cookie, despite the module asserting cookie headers are covered. Inconsistent coverage between the extras path and the text path is a silent gap.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `set[_-]cookie` to _SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES so both the underscore and hyphen forms are scrubbed in msg/args text, matching the extras set.
- **Verifier evidence:** Verified against the committed file (git status: working tree clean except an untracked unrelated doc; cited lines confirmed via `git show HEAD`).

FACTUAL ACCURACY (confirmed):
- /home/josh/projects/Shekel/app/utils/logging_config.py:180 -- the regex catalogue `_SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES` contains only `r"cookie"` (no `set` prefix variant).
- :255 -- the extras set `_SENSITIVE_EXTRA_FIELDS` contains the underscore form `"set_cookie"`.
- :207 and :221 -- both value-scrub patterns anchor the key with the negative lookbehind `(?<![A-Za-z0-9_])`. `_` is inside that class.

MECHANISM (confirmed empirically): I reconstructed the exact KEY_GROUP/SEP/patterns and ran the actual `_scrub_text` logic:
  'set_cookie=session-abc123'  -> UNCHANGED (leaked)
  'set_cookie="signed-session-token"' -> UNCHANGED (leaked)
  'set-cookie=session-abc123'  -> 'set-cookie=[REDACTED]'
  'Set-Cookie: session=abc123' -> 'Set-Cookie: [REDACTED]'
  'cookie=abc123'              -> 'cookie=[REDACTED]'
A standalone lookbehind test confirms why: for `set_cookie` the char before `cookie` is `_` (in the class) so the lookbehind fails; for `set-cookie`/`Set-Cookie` the char is `-` (outside the class) so it matches via the bare `cookie` key.

IS-REAL-ISSUE: Genuine but minor, defense-in-depth, internal-consistency gap. The actual HTTP wire header `Set-Cookie` (and `Cookie`) IS covered by the text path -- the code comment at :174-176 states the `cookie` key is intended to cover "the HTTP Set-Cookie / Cookie header forms," and the hyphenated header forms are in fact scrubbed. The uncovered `set_cookie` underscore form is the Flask method-name shape, not the wire header. The defect is the asymmetry: the extras path (:255) deems `set_cookie` worth redacting wholesale, but the msg/args text path silently does not match it. The module's own docstring (:126-139, :298-342) frames the scrubber as catching exactly this class of hypothetical future careless caller, so this is NOT rule-13 gold-plating of an impossible scenario -- the whole module targets that scenario. A leaked Set-Cookie value is the signed session cookie.

TEST COVERAGE: tests/test_utils/test_logging_scrubber.py:119-129 (`test_cookie_header_redacted`) tests only the bare `cookie="..."` form; no test exercises any `set_cookie`/`set-cookie` form in msg/args. So the gap is uncovered.

ALREADY-KNOWN: Not P-1, not P-3 (those are loan-escrow and negative-deduction). Not in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md or plan.md (greps for set_cookie/scrubber/_SENSITIVE_* in the cleanup docs returned nothing relevant; the only quality-pass mention of logging_config:514 concerns a module-level disable, unrelated). Not a documented disable.

SEVERITY: Correctly LOW. Defense-in-depth secondary control (not the primary secret-handling control, which is encrypted DB columns / signed session never logged); the on-the-wire header form is already covered; exploitation requires a future caller to log a non-header underscore form verbatim. The suggested fix (`set[_-]cookie` in _SENSITIVE_KEY_NAMES) is straightforward and correct with no design tradeoff, so this is CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION.

### 54. [TEST-QUALITY/DEFECT] Test asserts gross using the code-under-test's own bare-quantize formula -- cannot catch the rounding-mode defect
- **Location:** `tests/test_services/test_investment_projection.py` :: 337-338
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** Line 337 computes expected_gross = (Decimal("100000") / 26).quantize(Decimal("0.01")) -- textually the same expression (including the absent rounding mode) as the code under test at investment_projection.py:98: (salary / pay_per_year).quantize(TWO_PLACES). Asserting result.gross_biweekly == expected_gross therefore re-derives the expectation from the implementation's own formula and rounding mode rather than an independently hand-computed value with a stated rounding decision.
- **Why it matters:** testing-standards requires service tests to assert exact hand-computed values with the arithmetic shown. Because the assertion mirrors the code, the test would still pass if the code's rounding mode is wrong, so it provides no protection against the F2 defect. ($100000/26 is not a half-cent boundary, so the modes coincide here, but the pattern is the gap.)
- **Suggested fix:** Assert a literal expected value (e.g. Decimal("3846.15")) with a comment showing the arithmetic and the chosen rounding mode, independent of the implementation expression.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE (confirmed). tests/test_services/test_investment_projection.py:337 -> `expected_gross = (Decimal("100000") / 26).quantize(Decimal("0.01"))`; :338 -> `assert result.gross_biweekly == expected_gross`. Code under test app/services/investment_projection.py:98 -> `gross = (salary / pay_per_year).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, with TWO_PLACES = Decimal("0.01") (:28), salary = Decimal("100000"), pay_per_year = 26. After constant substitution the two expressions are textually identical, INCLUDING the absent rounding mode -- the test re-derives the expectation from the implementation's own formula, not a hand-computed literal. Verified 100000/26 = 3846.153846... is NOT a half-cent boundary: default ROUND_HALF_EVEN, ROUND_HALF_UP, and ROUND_DOWN all give 3846.15, exactly as the finding's why_it_matters concedes. So the assertion would still pass under a wrong rounding mode -- no protection against a rounding-mode regression.

REAL ISSUE (LOW). .claude/rules/testing.md / docs/testing-standards: "Service tests assert exact computed values -- include a comment showing the arithmetic ... not result > 0." 337-338 violates this (formula-mirror, no rounding decision stated). The author clearly knows the correct style: line 136 asserts `Decimal("233.33")`, line 527 asserts `Decimal("269.23")` with comment "7% of ($100,000 / 26) = 7% of $3846.15 = $269.23" -- so 337-338 is the weaker instance, not the norm. Not rule-13 gold-plating; not covered elsewhere. NOTE the pattern is systemic in this file (also lines 116-117, 154, 272-273, 542-543, 671-672), so the single citation understates the scope but is correct.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN. quality-pass.md:367 (row 20, G1/G2/G3) ACCEPTed this exact file's test quality with the GENERAL claim "Assertions are hand-computed Decimals with arithmetic comments" -- which lines 337-338 contradict; the register never specifically examined/accepted this formula-mirror, so this is a counterexample to an ACCEPT, not an accepted item. P-1 (plan.md:2155) is loan P&I/escrow threshold; P-3 (plan.md:2199) is the negative-deduction `# BUG` (a different assertion at :345/:364). The referenced rounding-mode "F2 defect" is not tracked in plan.md's P-list.

Severity LOW (not a financial defect by itself -- modes coincide at this value; it is a latent test-quality weakness). HIGH confidence: every claim independently verified against committed code and registers.

### 55. [TEST-QUALITY/DEFECT] Stale docstring reference to a non-existent loan_resolver._add_months_to_date in the loan-resolver test helper
- **Location:** `tests/test_services/test_loan_resolver.py` :: 121-125
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** utils-infra
- **Claim:** The test-local _add_months helper docstring (line 124) says it ``Mirrors :func:`loan_resolver._add_months_to_date```, but no such function exists anywhere in app/ (grep for `def _add_months_to_date` returns nothing; the loan resolver does not define it). The mirrored production helper is actually rate_period_engine._add_months / app.utils.dates.add_months.
- **Why it matters:** A test helper whose docstring names a function that does not exist gives false confidence that the test pins parity with a real production code path. A maintainer reading it cannot verify the mirror is faithful, and the named anchor cannot be grep-traced -- weakening the test's stated guarantee.
- **Suggested fix:** Update the docstring to reference app.utils.dates.add_months (the canonical helper) and ideally import it directly so the test exercises production code rather than a hand-copied mirror.
- **Verifier evidence:** tests/test_services/test_loan_resolver.py:124 literally reads "Mirrors :func:`loan_resolver._add_months_to_date` so the tests" -- verbatim as the finding claims. grep -rn "def _add_months_to_date" app/ tests/ returns nothing; the only match for the bare string _add_months_to_date anywhere is the docstring text at line 124 itself, so the named function does not exist. The actual day-clamped month-adders are app/utils/dates.py:13 `def add_months` and app/services/rate_period_engine.py:212 `def _add_months`, both clamping the day to the month's last day via calendar.monthrange -- the same behavior the test helper (lines 121-138) re-implements with a hardcoded last_day_lookup table plus a manual leap-year branch. grep for add_months / utils.dates inside app/services/loan_resolver/ (files __init__.py, _payoff.py, _periods.py, _state.py) returns nothing, so the loan_resolver package neither defines nor imports any such helper -- the docstring is wrong on both the function name and the owning module. The mirror is behaviorally faithful (the lookup table equals calendar.monthrange), so this is purely a stale/incorrect docstring reference, not a computational divergence. Not P-1, not P-3 (loan-escrow / negative-deduction), not a documented inline disable, and not a quality-pass ACCEPT row (those cover app/ production files, not test docstrings). Genuine low-severity test-quality defect: a non-grep-traceable parity anchor that cannot be verified by a maintainer. Suggested fix to point at app.utils.dates.add_months is sound; importing it directly is an optional judgment beyond the docstring correction.

### 56. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] add_rate_change unconditionally overwrites params.interest_rate, corrupting the system-of-record rate when a backdated rate change is recorded
- **Location:** `app/routes/loan/escrow_rates.py` :: 81-91
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** add_rate_change inserts a RateHistory row at data['effective_date'] and then sets params.interest_rate = data['interest_rate'] (line 91) unconditionally, ignoring whether the new entry is the most recent by effective_date. RateHistory is queried by effective_date.desc() everywhere (loan_payment_service.py:136; escrow_rates.py:49-54), and params.interest_rate is the documented system-of-record 'base_rate' consumed by the payoff/refinance calculators (loan/_helpers.py:259 base_rate = Decimal(str(params.interest_rate)); used in calculators.py target-date and refinance paths). If a user records a historical/backdated rate change (effective_date earlier than an existing newer rate), params.interest_rate is overwritten with the OLDER rate, so the loan card's base rate and the calculator baselines silently revert to a superseded rate.
- **Why it matters:** Backdating a missed rate-change entry is a normal correction workflow for ARM loans. Overwriting the current rate with a backdated one mis-states the loan's current interest rate, which flows into refinance break-even and payoff what-if dollar figures -- real-money projections. Test coverage (test_loan.py:664-739) only adds forward-dated rate changes, so this case is uncovered.
- **Suggested fix:** Only assign params.interest_rate when data['effective_date'] is >= the max existing RateHistory.effective_date for the account (i.e. the new row is the current rate); otherwise leave params.interest_rate untouched.
- **Verifier evidence:** CITED LINES VERIFIED: escrow_rates.py:91 `params.interest_rate = data["interest_rate"]` is indeed unconditional, with no check that the new entry is the newest by effective_date (read lines 81-118). RateHistory is queried .desc() at loan_payment_service.py:136 and escrow_rates.py:52. _helpers.py:259 `base_rate = Decimal(str(params.interest_rate))`. The RateChangeSchema (validation.py:1707-1738) puts NO ordering constraint on effective_date; only a composite unique(account_id, effective_date) blocks exact-date duplicates, so a backdated-out-of-order entry IS reachable through normal use. Tests at test_loan.py:664-739 add only single forward-dated changes and actually assert params.interest_rate gets overwritten (test_rate_change_create: asserts params.interest_rate == 0.07000); the backdated-out-of-order case is uncovered.

REAL DEFECT CONFIRMED, BUT NARROWER THAN CLAIMED: The loan-card display IS corrupted -- dashboard.html:114 and the OOB swap in _rate_history.html:3-8 render `params.interest_rate|to_percent` directly as the "current interest rate", refreshed from params after every rate change. A backdated entry overwrites params.interest_rate with the OLDER rate, so the card shows the wrong current rate while the adjacent rate-history table (desc) still shows the newer entry on top -- a self-contradicting display and a corrupted system-of-record column.

HOWEVER THE FINDING'S HEADLINE IMPACT IS OVERSTATED: The claim that calculator baselines/refinance break-even/payoff what-if dollar figures "silently revert to a superseded rate" is largely inaccurate. _build_refinance_comparison (calculators.py:310-364) uses state.monthly_payment/total_interest/current_balance/schedule from the resolver, NOT params.interest_rate. The resolver derives the current rate via _rate_at_date (rate_period_engine.py:303-311) and _find_applicable_rate (amortization_engine.py:326-332), both of which use the MOST RECENT rate change with effective_date <= target_date and fall back to base_rate ONLY for dates before the first rate change. So a backdated overwrite of base_rate does NOT change the current-period rate that drives refinance/payoff dollar figures; it only affects projection of periods before the first recorded rate change (deep history). The target-date payoff path (calculators.py:173-186) passes both base_rate and rate_changes, layered identically, so it too is dominated by the latest change for the current period.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not a documented disable, not a quality-pass ACCEPT row, not P-1 (escrow threshold) or P-3 (negative deduction).

NEEDS-DECISION because the safe fix is a financial/design judgment: the suggested guard (only assign params.interest_rate when effective_date >= max existing) is reasonable, but the developer should decide whether params.interest_rate should instead be derived from the latest RateHistory on every mutation (add/edit/delete) -- the current write-on-add design is what makes the column driftable. Corrected severity LOW: the practical blast radius is the displayed current rate plus pre-first-change historical projection, not the headline what-if dollar figures the finding cites.

### 57. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] RaiseCreateSchema/RaiseUpdateSchema require effective_year, making the NULL-year recurring raise the model and paycheck calculator explicitly support unreachable via the web UI
- **Location:** `app/schemas/validation.py` :: 696-698, 743-754
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** models-schema
- **Claim:** RaiseCreateSchema.effective_year = fields.Integer(required=True) (validation.py:696-698) and RaiseUpdateSchema inherits it (743). The only write routes use these schemas (app/routes/salary/_helpers.py:82 _raise_schema=RaiseCreateSchema(); items.py:66,220). But the model deliberately permits NULL effective_year for recurring raises (app/models/salary_raise.py:108 nullable=True, CHECK ck_salary_raises_valid_effective_year admits NULL at 65-69, uq_salary_raises... uses postgresql_nulls_not_distinct for exactly this case at 76-81), and the paycheck calculator has a live, documented branch for it: app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:605-608 `if not eff_year: # No start year -- apply once if month reached this year`. tests/test_services/test_paycheck_calculator.py:351 test_recurring_raise_no_effective_year constructs effective_year=None directly. The schema/route make that domain capability uncreatable; tests/test_schemas/test_validation.py:789 test_missing_effective_year_rejected even codifies the block.
- **Why it matters:** Either a genuine, code-supported feature (an indefinitely-recurring annual raise with no anchor year) is dead/unreachable through the UI, or the calculator branch and its NULLS-NOT-DISTINCT unique constraint are dead complexity. The model, the constraint, the calculator, and the schema disagree about whether effective_year is mandatory for recurring raises -- a real-money projection branch whose only exercising path is a direct service test, not a user flow.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide the contract: if recurring raises may omit the year, make effective_year required only when is_recurring is False (cross-field rule) and drop the required=True; otherwise remove the calculator's NULL-year branch and the nulls-not-distinct unique as dead code.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every cited line verified true. SCHEMA: app/schemas/validation.py:696-698 `effective_year = fields.Integer(required=True, validate=validate.Range(min=2000, max=2100))`; RaiseUpdateSchema(RaiseCreateSchema) at :743 inherits it. ROUTES: the only `SalaryRaise(` construction in app/ is app/routes/salary/items.py:79, gated by `_raise_schema`/`_raise_update_schema` (app/routes/salary/_helpers.py:82-83); grep of app/ confirms no other write path. MODEL: app/models/salary_raise.py:108 `effective_year nullable=True`; CHECK ck_salary_raises_valid_effective_year (:65-69) admits NULL; uq_salary_raises_profile_type_year_month (:76-81) uses postgresql_nulls_not_distinct=True with a docstring (:36-42) explicitly justifying NULL-year recurring raises. CALCULATOR: app/services/paycheck_calculator.py:605-608 has the live `if not eff_year:` branch. TESTS: tests/test_services/test_paycheck_calculator.py:351 test_recurring_raise_no_effective_year (docstring at :354 calls it "a legacy edge case -- the UI now requires effective_year"); tests/test_schemas/test_validation.py:789 test_missing_effective_year_rejected codifies the schema block; tests/test_routes/test_c24_range_check_sweep.py:963 test_effective_year_null_accepted asserts the DB still accepts NULL. ROOT-CAUSE PROOF via git: in the original Phase 2 commit 17c414f the schema was `effective_year = fields.Integer()` (NOT required) while the model was already nullable=True -- the contract was coherent and NULL-year was UI-creatable. Commit 42720ca (C-24 security sweep) added required=True, and migration b4c5d6e7f8a9 (docstring: "Recurring raises require effective_year to compound correctly") backfilled away every NULL on recurring raises -- deciding the feature is unwanted -- but left the model nullability, nulls-not-distinct unique, DB CHECK NULL allowance, and calculator NULL-year branch in place as vestigial complexity no UI can reach. So model/constraint/calculator/schema genuinely disagree. Template app/templates/salary/_raises_section.html:121-122 confirms effective_year is a `required` input defaulted to now_year. This is a SOLID/cohesion + dead-complexity inconsistency, NOT a money-miscomputation defect (backfill ensured live rows have years; new rows are forced to). Not P-1/P-3. No pylint disable in the files. quality-pass.md has paycheck_calculator.py rows (lines 328-334) but none touch _apply_raises NULL-year, effective_year nullability, the schema requirement, or the unique constraint -- so not already accepted. Resolution (re-enable NULL-year in the UI as a real feature, or remove the dead NULL-year machinery) is a design judgment for the developer, hence NEEDS-DECISION; severity corrected to LOW since no projection is wrong today.

### 58. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Existing-payback lookups omit is_deleted filter while the backing unique index excludes soft-deleted paybacks
- **Location:** `app/services/credit_workflow.py` :: 188-194
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** transfer-txn
- **Claim:** All three existing-payback queries -- mark_as_credit idempotency (credit_workflow.py:188-194), unmark_credit cleanup (credit_workflow.py:321-325), and sync_entry_payback (entry_credit_workflow.py:117-121) -- use filter_by(credit_payback_for_id=txn.id).first() with NO is_deleted filter. The unique index uq_transactions_credit_payback_unique (transaction.py:62-70) is explicitly partial on 'is_deleted = FALSE', meaning the schema is designed to allow a soft-deleted payback to coexist with a new active one. The queries would return the soft-deleted row, so mark_as_credit's idempotency could return a soft-deleted payback as 'success', and sync's UPDATE branch (123-148) could resurrect/mutate a soft-deleted payback instead of creating a fresh one.
- **Why it matters:** Today paybacks are ad-hoc (template_id=None) and the delete route hard-deletes them, so the bug is latent; but the index predicate proves soft-deleted paybacks are an anticipated state, and any future code path that soft-deletes a payback (carry-forward move, bulk archive) would immediately mis-handle CC debt -- returning an invisible payback as live, or doubling it past the unique index. The queries and the index disagree on what 'the' payback is.
- **Suggested fix:** Add Transaction.is_deleted.is_(False) to all three credit_payback_for_id lookups so they agree with the partial unique index's predicate.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE on all three sites. credit_workflow.py:188-192 (mark_as_credit idempotency) and :321-325 (unmark_credit cleanup) both use db.session.query(Transaction).filter_by(credit_payback_for_id=txn.id).first() with no is_deleted filter. entry_credit_workflow.py:117-121 (sync_entry_payback) uses the identical filter_by, and its UPDATE branch (123-148) mutates existing_payback.estimated_amount + re-links entries on whatever row that returns. transaction.py:62-70 confirms uq_transactions_credit_payback_unique is partial: postgresql_where="credit_payback_for_id IS NOT NULL AND is_deleted = FALSE", and the comment at :58-60 states this is deliberate so a re-mark after soft-delete is legal.

REAL ISSUE (consistency / latent-correctness), but CURRENTLY UNREACHABLE. Exhaustive scan of every is_deleted=True write on a Transaction (transfer_service.py:728/737/835/852/888 = transfers+shadows only; templates.py:531/663 = filtered template_id==template.id; mutations.py:366 = only the `if txn.template_id:` branch) shows NO path can soft-delete a payback: create_cc_payback_transaction (credit_workflow.py:404) and _create_payback always set template_id=None, so the delete route (mutations.py:364-369) HARD-deletes paybacks (else branch), template archival never matches (template_id is NULL), and account deletion (accounts/crud.py:580-582) is a hard .delete(). So the bad state (source still Credit + only payback soft-deleted) cannot arise in the committed code today. The two existing tests covering soft-deleted paybacks (test_c19_credit_payback_unique.py:348-388, 479-522) only reach it by manually setting first.is_deleted=True AND resetting the source to Projected -- which sidesteps the idempotency block via is_credit(txn)=False, so they do NOT cover the source-stays-Credit case the finding flags.

NOT a documented disable, NOT in quality-pass.md (only a transfer_service _build_shadow row exists there), NOT P-1/P-3. The C-19 remediation (remediation-plan.md:4032-4113) added the partial index + FOR UPDATE + route IntegrityError catch but never specified an is_deleted filter on the service-level idempotency SELECT.

Why NEEDS-DECISION not REFUTED: the omission genuinely contradicts (a) the binding database.md rule 'Filter soft-deleted rows: .filter(Model.is_deleted.is_(False)) unless deleted rows are explicitly needed', and (b) the sibling active-lookup _get_shadow_transactions (transfer_service.py:209-222) which DOES filter is_deleted=False against an index with the identical predicate. The index predicate proves soft-deleted paybacks are anticipated state, not an impossible scenario, so adding the filter is not pure rule-13 gold-plating. But it is latent today, so whether to harden now vs. when a payback soft-delete path is introduced is a developer design call. Severity corrected MED->LOW: zero reachable impact in the current codebase.

### 59. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Suggested-contribution remaining-periods window is inconsistent with the YTD window, risking a gap or overlap around 'today'
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py` :: 374-388, 206-238
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (MED confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `_compute_suggested_contribution` counts `remaining_periods` as periods with `p.start_date >= today AND p.start_date.year == today.year` (line 376-380), then spreads `limit - ytd` over them (line 381-388). The YTD it subtracts is computed by `_ytd_contributions` over periods `p.start_date <= current_period.start_date` (line 228-232). `today` and `current_period.start_date` are not the same anchor: the current period typically starts before today, so the period containing today is counted in YTD (start <= current) yet excluded from `remaining_periods` (start < today), or vice-versa depending on alignment.
- **Why it matters:** The 'spread the rest of the cap over the rest of the year' suggestion can omit or double-allocate the in-progress period, nudging the suggested per-period transfer slightly off. Low stakes (a non-binding UX suggestion) but the two windows should share one boundary.
- **Suggested fix:** Define both windows against the same reference (either `current_period` or `today`) so the period containing the reference is consistently in exactly one of YTD-already-contributed vs remaining.
- **Verifier evidence:** The two windows use different anchors, as claimed, but the finding misattributes the YTD code's location. CONFIRMED mechanics: (a) remaining_periods in `_compute_suggested_contribution` (app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:375-380) counts periods where `p.start_date.year == today_date.year AND p.start_date >= today_date`, anchored on `date.today()`; (b) the subtracted YTD comes from `ctx.inputs.ytd_contributions` (call site line 613-614), computed by `_ytd_contributions` -- which is NOT in the cited file/lines. The finding cites "app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py" lines "206-238 ... 228-232", but those dashboard lines contain `_load_projection_context`/`_ProjectionContext` (read lines 190-238). The actual `_ytd_contributions` is in app/services/investment_projection.py:206-238, summing periods where `p.start_date.year == current_year AND p.start_date <= current_period.start_date` (lines 227-232) -- the finding's "(line 228-232)" matches that file, so the description of the predicate is correct, only the filename is wrong.

`get_current_period` (app/services/pay_period_service.py:111-118) returns the period with `start_date <= today <= end_date`, so the current period (P_cur) contains today and normally `P_cur.start_date < today`.

Partition analysis: Case A (typical, today mid-period, P_cur.start < today): P_cur is in YTD (start <= current start) and excluded from remaining (start < today) -> P_cur is in exactly ONE set; periods before P_cur are YTD-only, periods after are remaining-only. This is a CLEAN partition -- no gap, no double-allocation, contrary to the finding's "omit or double-allocate" framing for the typical case. The status filter `status_contributes_to_balance` (app/utils/balance_predicates.py:144) excludes only Credit/Cancelled, so even a projected current-period contribution counts in YTD, closing the "gap" the finding worried about.

Real defect is the narrow Case B (today == P_cur.start_date, the exact day a period begins): P_cur satisfies both `start <= current start` (YTD, equal) and `start >= today` (remaining, equal), so P_cur is double-counted -- in YTD-already AND in the remaining spread. That is a genuine single-day off-by-one where the two windows fail to share one boundary, exactly as the finding's "vice-versa depending on alignment" notes.

Tests: tests/test_routes/test_investment.py:193-219 only pin the zero-cap and none-cap early returns; the docstring at :136-137 explicitly says the window logic is "unpinned." No test exercises remaining_periods vs. YTD boundary alignment. tests/test_services/test_investment_projection.py:176-238 test `_ytd_contributions` in isolation, never against the suggestion's remaining-window. So the boundary inconsistency is uncovered.

Not already-known: not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction); not a documented disable; the quality-pass row for these helpers (test docstring B7) covers only the zero/none-cap branches and leaves the window logic unpinned.

Impact is low: a non-binding UX per-period suggestion, wrong only on the single calendar day a period starts, and the typical-case partition is defensible/intended (don't re-spread the cap over a period already counted in YTD). The correct fix (anchor both windows on the same reference, and decide whether the in-progress period should be a "remaining" period) is a financial/UX design judgment for the developer -> NEEDS-DECISION at LOW.

### 60. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] _compute_pre_anchor_interest knowingly overstates interest in pre-anchor year periods
- **Location:** `app/services/year_end_summary_service/_balances.py` :: 592-652
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** _compute_pre_anchor_interest applies the CURRENT anchor balance to every pre-anchor period of the target year to estimate interest (line 640: `balance = account.current_anchor_balance`), and the docstring itself states 'This slightly overstates interest (the actual balance was lower before contributions).' The result is added into investment_growth / growth_total for the savings-progress section (_savings.py:128).
- **Why it matters:** The year-end savings-progress 'growth' figure for an interest-bearing account whose anchor is set after Jan 1 is biased high by design; in a money app a knowingly-overstated interest figure on a year-end summary is a reporting accuracy concern, not just display polish.
- **Suggested fix:** Reverse-project the balance back through the pre-anchor periods (as the investment path does in _derive_investment_jan1) before accruing interest, instead of holding the anchor balance flat.
- **Verifier evidence:** CODE CONFIRMS THE CLAIM. app/services/year_end_summary_service/_balances.py:640 is literally `balance = account.current_anchor_balance or ZERO`, and lines 642-650 apply that flat balance to every pre-anchor period of the target year via calculate_interest, summing into total_interest. The docstring at lines 606-608 explicitly states: "This slightly overstates interest (the actual balance was lower before contributions), but is a reasonable approximation for display purposes." The result is added into growth_total at _savings.py:128 (growth_total += _compute_pre_anchor_interest(...)), which becomes investment_growth in the returned dict (_savings.py:149) and is rendered at app/templates/analytics/_year_end.html:303. So the figure is biased high by design exactly as the finding states.

ASYMMETRY WITH THE INVESTMENT PATH IS REAL. The investment branch (_savings.py:240-297 _derive_investment_jan1, and _balances.py:394 _reverse_project_periods) DOES reverse-project the balance back through pre-anchor periods via growth_engine.reverse_project_balance (app/services/growth_engine.py:482) before accruing, whereas the interest branch holds the anchor flat. The finding's comparison is accurate.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN. Distinct from P-1 (loan escrow threshold, app/services/loan_resolver/_state.py) and P-3 (negative paycheck deduction). The savings-progress/display-aggregation files are not in those financial cores.

TEST COVERAGE DOES NOT CONSTRAIN IT. tests/test_services/test_year_end_summary_service.py:2132 test_hysa_pre_anchor_jan1 only asserts investment_growth > ZERO (line 2159) and jan1_balance > ZERO -- no hand-computed value pins the pre-anchor interest, so the overstatement is untested/unbounded by tests. test_savings_hysa_with_interest (line 1688) is also a > ZERO assertion. Ran TestSavingsProgressPreAnchor: 7 passed in 2.18s.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION RATHER THAN CONFIRMED: (1) the developer explicitly documented this as an accepted display approximation, so reclassifying it requires their call; (2) the suggested fix (reverse_project_balance) is the growth-engine's investment-inverse formula -- applying it to an interest account is conceptually wrong, so a correct remedy needs an interest-specific back-computation, which is a financial/design judgment. It is a genuine systematic reporting bias on a money figure (not rule-13 gold-plating, since a post-Jan-1 anchor is an ordinary supported scenario per the entire TestSavingsProgressPreAnchor class), but whether and how to correct it is the developer's decision. Severity LOW is correct: bounded by partial-year interest on the (anchor - true pre-anchor) delta, one field, one account class.

### 61. [CORRECTNESS/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Year-end transfers section attributes by period membership while spending attributes by COALESCE(due_date, start_date)
- **Location:** `app/services/year_end_summary_service/_transfers.py` :: 42-64
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** reporting
- **Claim:** _compute_transfers_summary includes a transfer purely on `pay_period_id.in_(period_ids)` (periods whose start_date is in the year), with no year re-check. By contrast _compute_spending_by_category (_spending.py:71-75) and _compute_payment_timeliness re-filter each row with _attribution_year() using COALESCE(due_date, pay_period.start_date). A transfer in a period that straddles the Dec/Jan boundary is attributed differently from a same-period expense.
- **Why it matters:** In the year-end summary the Transfers section can count a boundary-period transfer in a different calendar year than the Spending section counts a sibling expense in the same period, producing internally inconsistent year totals on the same report.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide one attribution rule for the year-end report and apply it to transfers too (transfers have a due/effective date concept via their period), or document why transfers use pure period membership.
- **Verifier evidence:** CONFIRMED the finding (could not refute it). The claim is factually accurate and a genuine internal-consistency defect.

FACTUAL ACCURACY:
- app/services/year_end_summary_service/_transfers.py:42-53: _compute_transfers_summary filters ONLY on Transfer.pay_period_id.in_(period_ids) (plus user/scenario/is_deleted/status). No _attribution_year re-check; lines 56-64 sum amounts unconditionally.
- _spending.py:71-75: _compute_spending_by_category re-filters each row with `if _attribution_year(txn) != year: continue`. _spending.py:298: _compute_payment_timeliness does the same. _attribution_year (_spending.py:364-374) = COALESCE(due_date, pay_period.start_date).year.
- _data.py:47-59,108: year_period_ids = periods whose start_date is between Jan 1 and Dec 31. PayPeriod (pay_period.py:25-26,37) is a biweekly range whose end_date can fall in the next year (the __str__ explicitly handles start_date.year != end_date.year), so a period straddling Dec/Jan is normal and is included by start_date.

REAL ISSUE (not intended / not safe-by-construction / not test-covered):
- Transfer.due_date EXISTS (transfer.py:170) and is POPULATED: transfer_recurrence.py:107 sets due_date=_compute_due_date(plan.rule, period) -- the same engine transactions use; transfer_service.py:322/445/668-675 mirror due_date to the transfer and both shadows. So a monthly-rule transfer landing in a late-December period gets a January due_date.
- transfer.py:160-169 (the model's own documented contract) states: "Consumers of a due date (calendar, dashboard, year-end, spending-trend) read the shadow Transaction.due_date." The transfers section violates this -- it reads neither the parent due_date nor the shadow due_date; it uses pure period membership.
- All sibling analytics services use COALESCE(due_date,start_date): spending_trend_service.py:191-213, budget_variance_service.py:311-312, calendar_service.py:146-147,486-496 -- and they include transfers by querying the SHADOW Transaction rows, not the parent Transfer table.
- Demonstrable inconsistency on ONE report: _spending.py's _query_settled_expenses (lines 342-361) has NO transfer_id filter (grep for transfer/shadow in _spending.py returned nothing), so a transfer's EXPENSE shadow is ALSO counted in the Spending section, COALESCE-attributed. For a boundary-period transfer with a January due_date: the expense shadow is attributed to year+1 (excluded from this year's Spending), while the parent transfer is attributed to this year (included in Transfers). Same money event, two calendar years, same report.
- Not test-covered: test helper _create_transfer_with_shadows (test_year_end_summary_service.py:184-238) sets NO due_date on the transfer or shadows, and no test in the file exercises a boundary/straddling period (grep for boundary/straddle/cross-year found none). The route test (test_analytics.py:771-813) also sets no due_date.
- Not gold-plating: boundary periods recur every year in a biweekly system; this is a real scenario.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN:
- quality-pass.md B2 (year_end) register rows (lines 434,454,461-465) cover only F1 (_ProjectionInputs reshape, ACCEPTED) and F2 (balance-map split, DONE) -- neither is attribution.
- Cluster #3 (line 559) DID extract monthly_attribution_clause and apply it to calendar/variance/spending-trend, but explicitly did NOT bring the year-end transfers section into that consistency effort. Distinct from P-1 (loan escrow) and P-3 (negative deduction).

VERDICT NEEDS-DECISION: the defect is real, but the correct fix is a developer judgment -- adopt COALESCE(due_date, start_date) attribution for transfers (via the parent due_date or by querying shadows like the other analytics services), or deliberately document why the Transfers section uses pure period membership. Severity LOW: only affects transfers whose due_date crosses the Dec/Jan boundary; totals are still internally inconsistent on the report but the magnitude is bounded to boundary-period transfers.

### 62. [DECIMAL/CORRECTNESS-RISK] period_subtotal rounds income and expense legs separately, breaking the documented balance-delta invariant under sub-cent legs
- **Location:** `app/services/balance_resolver.py` :: 575-581 vs 500-503 and 856
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** period_subtotal computes `rounded_income = round_money(income)`, `rounded_expense = round_money(expense)`, `net = rounded_income - rounded_expense` (lines 575-580), i.e. it rounds each leg before subtracting. balances_for carries the running balance at FULL precision (balance_calculator.py:104,109 add unrounded income/expense) and rounds each period snapshot once (line 501), and balance_as_of_date rounds the combined `prior_balance + income - expense` once (line 856). The docstring at lines 526-529 asserts `balances[p] - balances[prev] == period_subtotal.net` by construction. With income=100.005, expense=50.004 the balance delta is 50.00 but subtotal.net is 50.01 (verified). The two rounding strategies are not algebraically equal whenever a leg carries a sub-cent fraction.
- **Why it matters:** The grid footer subtotal and the balance row are supposed to reconcile to the penny (F-002 Pair C). The invariant holds today only because stored amounts and the live paycheck override are already cent-quantized; any future leg that produces a sub-cent fraction (a prorated/averaged amount, an entry-aware partial) would silently break cross-page equality. It is a latent correctness risk masked by current data shape, not a guaranteed invariant.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute net as round_money(income - expense) (round the combined net once) so the subtotal uses the same single-rounding strategy as the balance roll-forward, then derive displayed income/expense from the same rounding discipline.
- **Verifier evidence:** CODE IS AS CLAIMED. balance_resolver.py:575-580 rounds each leg then subtracts (rounded_income = round_money(income); rounded_expense = round_money(expense); net=rounded_income - rounded_expense). balance_calculator.py:104,109 accumulates running_balance at full precision (+income -expenses, no per-step rounding); balance_resolver.py:500-503 rounds each snapshot once; balance_resolver.py:856 rounds combined (round_money(prior_balance + income - expense)). Docstring 526-529 asserts balances[p]-balances[prev]==period_subtotal.net "by construction". I reproduced the divergence: income=100.005, expense=50.004 -> per-leg net=50.01, combined net=50.00 (differ). So the two rounding strategies are NOT algebraically equal for sub-cent legs. round_money is ROUND_HALF_UP quantize to CENTS (money.py:45-72).

NOT A LIVE BUG -- latent, masked by data shape. Every leg input is provably cent-quantized today: estimated_amount/actual_amount are Numeric(12,2) (transaction.py:169-170); entry.amount is Numeric(12,2) (transaction_entry.py:68); effective_amount returns those (transaction.py:248). _entry_aware_amount (balance_calculator.py:394) returns max() over those cent-quantized values via _entry_checking_impact. Income override net_pay is .quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP) (paycheck_calculator.py:260-265), flowed through live_projected_net (income_service.py:231,241). Expense override PITI = state.monthly_payment + context.monthly_escrow (loan_payment_service.py:590); monthly_payment = period_pi = round_money(...) (rate_period_engine.py:480,482), monthly_escrow = .quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP) (escrow_calculator.py:128). A sum of cent-quantized Decimals is cent-quantized, so round_money(leg) is a no-op and per-leg == combined; the invariant holds for ALL current data. Tests confirm: test_balance_resolver.py:731 test_period_subtotal_reconciles_balance_delta and test_cross_page_balance_equality.py:424 test_subtotal_reconciles_balance_delta both pass on cent-quantized cases (none exercise sub-cent legs). The finding itself concedes this is data-shape-masked.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION not REFUTED: the divergence is genuine and the docstring's "by construction" claim overstates what the code guarantees (it is data-shape-dependent, not structural). The one-line fix net=round_money(income - expense) makes the claim actually true with zero behavioral change on current data, but rule-13 tension exists (no path produces sub-cent legs today). Whether to harden vs. leave is a developer judgment.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: distinct from P-1 (loan escrow threshold compute_monthly_payment_baseline) and P-3 (negative deduction). Not a documented disable; nearby disables are protected-access (575-573 region) and unrelated. Mechanical R0801/quality-pass passes do not catch this semantic rounding-strategy divergence.

### 63. [DECIMAL/CORRECTNESS-RISK] Per-period contribution math uses default ROUND_HALF_EVEN while the growth engine and gap calculator use ROUND_HALF_UP
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_projection.py` :: 98, 101, 173
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** invest-retire
- **Claim:** `_compute_deduction_per_period` quantizes gross (line 98) and the percentage amount (line 101), and `_average_transfer_contribution` quantizes the average (line 173), all via bare `.quantize(TWO_PLACES)` which defaults to ROUND_HALF_EVEN. Every monetary quantize in growth_engine.py (lines 178, 183, 187, 345) and retirement_gap_calculator.py (lines 92-93, 130, 140, 157) explicitly passes `rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP`. CLAUDE.md requires rounding mode be explicit and consistent across paths that must agree.
- **Why it matters:** At an exact half-cent boundary the deduction-derived gross/contribution and the embedded employer-match gross basis round the opposite direction from the engine, producing a one-cent disagreement between the dashboard's per-period card and the engine's chart/year-end line -- the exact class of cross-surface divergence the HIGH-07 work tried to eliminate. Low likelihood (division by 26 rarely lands on .005) but a latent inconsistency.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP` to the three quantize calls so the contribution-input layer matches the engine's rounding convention.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE: app/services/investment_projection.py:98 `gross = (salary / pay_per_year).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, :101 `amt = (gross * amt).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, :173 `return (total_contrib / num_periods_with_contrib).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` are all bare quantize -> Python's default ROUND_HALF_EVEN. By contrast growth_engine.py:178,183,187-189,345 and :540, and retirement_gap_calculator.py:92-93,130,140,157 all pass explicit `rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP`. Verified asymmetry directly.

REAL ISSUE -- but for a STRONGER reason than the finding states. The project has an explicit documented house rounding convention in app/utils/money.py:5-11: "ROUND_HALF_UP is the only default ... Python's Decimal default of ROUND_HALF_EVEN (banker's rounding) is a silent source of one-cent drift at half-cent boundaries and must never be reached implicitly through a bare .quantize(Decimal(\"0.01\")) ... the convention every hand-computed financial test in this project assumes." Lines 98/101/173 do exactly the prohibited thing. round_money()/round_money_ceiling() are the sanctioned boundary helpers; neither investment_projection.py nor growth_engine.py imports money.round_money (verified via grep) -- growth_engine correctly inlines rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP, the input layer omits it.

The finding's "why_it_matters" (card-vs-chart cross-surface divergence) is PARTLY OVERSTATED: I traced both consumers. The deduction per-period amount uses the SAME _compute_deduction_per_period in path A (calculate_investment_inputs, feeds the dashboard per-period card) AND path B (build_contribution_timeline:342, feeds the engine chart/year-end), so they cannot round opposite each other on the deduction figure. gross_biweekly/employer_params is computed once in path A (_employer_params:202) and shared by the card (_compute_employer_per_period:401-409), the chart (_run_growth_projection:260), the what-if overlay (:763), and year-end (_savings.py:231); the HALF_UP in calculate_employer_contribution is applied identically to that shared HALF_EVEN basis on every surface. So no current card-vs-chart one-cent mismatch is demonstrable. The transfer averaging at :173 differs from the timeline by design (F-19 lump-sum-in-actual-period vs averaged), documented at _savings.py:214-218 -- that divergence is the averaging design, not the rounding mode.

The genuine defect is the convention violation itself: at an exact half-cent boundary (e.g. salary/26 or gross*pct landing on .xx5, total_contrib/periods on .xx5) these sites round DOWN where every other money path and every hand-computed test round UP. NOT already known: distinct from P-1 (escrow threshold) and P-3 (negative deduction); no documented disable on these lines.

TEST-QUALITY GAP (compounds it): tests/test_services/test_investment_projection.py:116-117,154,272,337,542-543,671-672 compute expected values with the SAME bare .quantize(Decimal("0.01")) as the code under test -- assertions computed by the production rounding mode, so they would NOT catch a HALF_EVEN-vs-HALF_UP divergence and instead enshrine the bare-quantize behavior.

CORRECTED SEVERITY LOW: real likelihood of hitting an exact .005 boundary on /26 or *pct is small, and no concrete cross-surface mismatch is currently reachable; but it is a clear, falsifiable violation of the codebase's own stated money.py rule. Fix is mechanical (add rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP to the three calls, or route through money.round_money), so CONFIRMED not NEEDS-DECISION.

### 64. [DRY/CORRECTNESS-RISK] 'Settled status' predicate hand-reproduced in two forms (ID-list vs is_settled column) with the ID set re-derived under 3+ names, uncentralized
- **Location:** `app/services/dashboard_service.py` :: 448-450, 654-656; also year_end_summary_service/_data.py:256-258, spending_trend_service.py:39-41+577-579, savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:146, balance_calculator.py:52, budget_variance_service.py:411, calendar_service.py:348, templates.py:686, transfers/templates.py:569
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** The rule 'is this transaction settled' is implemented two structurally-different ways that R0801 cannot cluster: (a) hardcoded ID-set status_id.in_([DONE, RECEIVED, SETTLED]) at dashboard_service.py:448-450 & 654-656 and year_end_summary_service/_data.py:256-258, plus a named copy spending_trend_service._get_settled_status_ids() (577-579) over _SETTLED_STATUSES=(DONE,RECEIVED,SETTLED) (39-41); (b) the semantic column txn.status.is_settled at savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:146, balance_calculator.py:52, budget_variance_service.py:411, calendar_service.py:348 and Status.is_settled.is_(True) at templates.py:686 / transfers/templates.py:569. Per app/ref_seeds.py:93-98 the is_settled=True rows are exactly {Paid,Received,Settled}, so they agree TODAY. There is no settled_status_ids() helper analogous to balance_excluded_status_ids().
- **Why it matters:** This is the identical drift hazard that balance_predicates.py centralized for excludes_from_balance (documented MED-02), but left unaddressed for is_settled. If a status's is_settled flag is changed or a new settled status is seeded, the hardcoded ID-list sites (dashboard totals, year-end summary, trend) would silently disagree with the is_settled-column sites (savings metrics, variance, calendar) -- two pages reporting different 'settled spending' for the same data.
- **Suggested fix:** Add settled_status_ids() and an is_settled SQL clause to balance_predicates.py derived from the is_settled column / cached IDs, and route all ten sites through it (mirroring balance_excluded_status_ids).
- **Verifier evidence:** All 10 cited sites verified accurate. ID-list form: dashboard_service.py:447-451 and 653-657 hardcode status_id.in_([DONE,RECEIVED,SETTLED]); spending_trend_service.py:38-42 (_SETTLED_STATUSES frozenset) + 577-579 (_get_settled_status_ids); year_end_summary_service/_data.py:253-259 (_get_settled_status_ids). Column form: savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:146, balance_calculator.py:52, budget_variance_service.py:411, calendar_service.py:348 all read txn.status.is_settled; routes/templates.py:685-686 and routes/transfers/templates.py:568-570 use Status.is_settled.is_(True). ref_seeds.py:93-98 confirms is_settled=True is exactly {Paid,Received,Settled}={DONE,RECEIVED,SETTLED}, and ref.py:210 confirms is_settled is the DB column -- so all sites resolve to the SAME set today by construction; NO number is currently wrong (correct-by-construction, not a live correctness defect). Verified app/utils/balance_predicates.py exposes balance_excluded_status_ids() + balance_contributing_clause() but NO settled_status_ids()/is_settled clause, so the claim "no helper analogous to balance_excluded_status_ids" is accurate; the drift hazard is the same in kind as the documented MED-02 that motivated that module. ALREADY-KNOWN crossover is strong and decisive: (1) docs/audits/security-2026-04-15/c-38-followups.md:162-167 independently identified "the settled expenses in a period filter" as a dedup target and recommended a deferred app/services/_period_window.py helper (no such file exists -> still deferred); (2) financial_calculation_audit_plan.md:632-635 flagged _sum_settled_expenses/_sum_paid_expenses as sharing structure that "should likely share a parameterized core"; (3) the pylint-cleanup quality-pass register (quality-pass.md:536-537,559, commit 3c709b8) explicitly examined the spending_trend<->dashboard settled pairing as cluster "3e", ruled it "FALSE (settled-vs-projected gate)" and recorded a deliberate decision to keep spending_trend's documented one-sided disable with dashboard needing none. The finding is BROADER than cluster 3e (it spans the ID-list-vs-is_settled-column structural divide across 10 sites, which R0801's near-textual matcher cannot cluster), so it is not FULLY subsumed -- but the core remediation question (centralize the settled predicate as balance_excluded was) has been raised in the audit trail and the developer's recorded posture is defer/keep-disables. Because nothing is numerically wrong today and the extraction-vs-defer call is a design/financial judgment the developer has already been partially making, NEEDS-DECISION with severity reduced to LOW.

### 65. [CORRECTNESS/JUDGMENT] RecurrenceRule.interval_n and offset_periods are nullable with Python-only defaults, forcing every consumer to defensively coalesce NULL
- **Location:** `app/models/recurrence_rule.py` :: 28-30
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** models-schema
- **Claim:** RecurrenceRule.interval_n = db.Column(db.Integer, default=1) and offset_periods = db.Column(db.Integer, default=0) (recurrence_rule.py:28-30) omit nullable=False and server_default, so a non-ORM insert (raw SQL, pg_dump reload) lands NULL, which the CHECK constraints ck_recurrence_rules_positive_interval/valid_offset permit (NULL passes a boolean predicate). Both columns are deliberately excluded from the F-068 NOT-NULL+server_default sweep (absent from tests/test_models/test_c25_column_invariants.py F_068_LOCKED_COLUMNS). Consumers compensate ad hoc: recurrence_engine.py:479-480 `rule.interval_n or 1` / `rule.offset_periods or 0`, savings_goal_service.py:270 `interval_n or 1`, obligations.py:92 `rule.interval_n or 1` -- but obligations_aggregator.py:106 passes rule.interval_n straight into amount_to_monthly (saved only because amount_to_monthly re-coalesces at line 270).
- **Why it matters:** A logic-bearing recurrence count with NULL semantics has no defined meaning, contradicts the project's 'NOT NULL by default; server_default for swept columns' invariant, and pushes the same `or 1`/`or 0` band-aid into five call sites where one missed coalesce becomes a TypeError or a divide-by-None in monthly-equivalent math.
- **Suggested fix:** Add nullable=False plus server_default=db.text('1') / db.text('0') (and the columns to the C-25 invariant test) so the storage tier guarantees the value and the scattered `or 1`/`or 0` fallbacks can be removed.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every claim verified against committed code (not docstrings):

1. COLUMN DEFINITIONS (app/models/recurrence_rule.py:28-30): interval_n = db.Column(db.Integer, default=1) and offset_periods = db.Column(db.Integer, default=0). No nullable=False, no server_default. Comments (lines 27,29) describe USAGE, not why nullable -- so the project's "NOT NULL by default; nullable columns justify nullability in a comment" rule (.claude/rules/database.md, Schema design) is unmet.

2. CHECK CONSTRAINTS (recurrence_rule.py:17-18): ck_recurrence_rules_positive_interval = "interval_n > 0", ck_recurrence_rules_valid_offset = "offset_periods >= 0". A NULL value yields UNKNOWN, which a CHECK treats as satisfied, so NULL passes both -- claim accurate.

3. LIVE DB STATE: migrations/versions/9dea99d4e33e_initial_schema.py:152-153 declares both columns nullable=True with no server_default; no later migration changes this. Confirmed by the audit schema dump docs/audits/security-2026-04-15/scans/schema-budget-recurrence_rules.txt:7-8 (both columns: nullable, no default). A raw/pg_dump-reload insert can land NULL.

4. F-068 SWEEP EXCLUSION: tests/test_models/test_c25_column_invariants.py F_068_LOCKED_COLUMNS (lines 43-68) contains neither column. F-068 (docs/audits/security-2026-04-15/findings.md:3266-3308) was scoped to BOOLEAN flags + sort_order integers (it lists budget.recurrence_rules.is_recurring -- a boolean -- but NOT interval_n/offset_periods). So these are outside the documented sweep; the finding's "deliberately excluded" wording slightly overstates intent (they were simply out of F-068's boolean/sort_order scope), but the substantive claim "not protected at the storage tier and not in the test" is correct.

5. CONSUMER COALESCES (all verified): app/services/recurrence_engine.py:479-480 `rule.interval_n or 1` / `rule.offset_periods or 0` (n is a modulus divisor at 481); app/services/savings_goal_service.py:270 `Decimal(str(interval_n or 1))` (divisor at 271); app/routes/obligations.py:92 `rule.interval_n or 1`. app/services/obligations_aggregator.py:106 passes rule.interval_n straight into amount_to_monthly -- which IS savings_goal_service.amount_to_monthly (def at savings_goal_service.py:201) and re-coalesces at line 270, so that pass-through is saved only transitively. The finding's "line 270" attribution is correct for both savings_goal_service and amount_to_monthly (same line).

ASSESSMENT: Genuine, un-tracked defect of the exact F-068 class (Python-only default + DB-nullable + no NULL meaning) left unfixed for two LOGIC-BEARING integer divisors. CHECK constraints do not catch NULL. Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable, not the recurrence quality-pass row (which is R0801 query-family cluster 3 at quality-pass.md:559, unrelated). Severity correctly LOW: all live consumers coalesce so there is no current crash; harm is latent (one missed `or 1` -> divide-by-None/TypeError, or a non-ORM insert landing meaningless NULL). The fix is a NOT-NULL + server_default('1')/('0') migration on a populated table plus a decision on removing vs keeping the scattered fallbacks -- a migration-design choice -- but the underlying defect is confirmed.

### 66. [CORRECTNESS/JUDGMENT] Category dropdown ordering ignores sort_order while the categories settings page honors it
- **Location:** `app/services/category_service.py` :: 31-35
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** list_active_categories orders by (group_name, item_name) only (category_service.py:34), and this feeds the category <select> on the template create/edit forms (templates.py:231,339). But the categories management page in settings orders the same rows by (sort_order, group_name, item_name) (settings.py:198). Category inherits SortOrderMixin (app/models/category.py:17), so sort_order is a real, user-arrangeable column. Result: a user who reorders categories via sort_order on the settings page sees that order there but a different (sort_order-ignoring) order in every template form dropdown.
- **Why it matters:** The special mandate calls out category dropdown ordering consistency. A user-configured ordering that is honored on one page and silently ignored on the picker is a real usability inconsistency, and makes the explicit sort_order feature appear broken.
- **Suggested fix:** Add Category.sort_order as the leading order_by key in list_active_categories so the dropdown matches the settings management ordering.
- **Verifier evidence:** All cited facts verified in committed code.
