(1) app/services/category_service.py:31-35 -- list_active_categories orders ONLY by (Category.group_name, Category.item_name); docstring also says "ordered by group_name then item_name". (2) Callers: app/routes/templates.py:231 (new_template) and :339 (edit_template) feed `categories` to templates/form.html, which renders the category_id <select> (form.html:82-86); plus 3 transfer form sites (transfers/templates.py:110,238; transfers/forms.py:55). (3) app/routes/settings.py:198 -- _load_categories_context orders the same rows by (Category.sort_order, Category.group_name, Category.item_name). (4) app/models/category.py:17 -- Category(UserScopedMixin, SortOrderMixin, ...); app/models/mixins.py:183-185 -- SortOrderMixin defines sort_order INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "user-assignable rank used to order rows in dropdowns and lists; lower sorts first, ties broken by name."

Real-issue corroboration: sort_order is genuinely populated and differs from alphabetical. auth_service.py:822-827 assigns sort_order=enumerate index over DEFAULT_CATEGORIES (auth_service.py:258-283), whose order is domain-grouped (Income, Home, Auto, Family, ...) NOT alphabetical -- so a fresh user's settings page shows Income first (sort_order=0) while the dropdown shows Auto first (alphabetical). test_auth_service.py:464-476 asserts sort_order == range(24); test_transfer_categories_have_valid_sort_order (441-462) asserts non-null + unique values. Sibling proof of intended convention: account_service.py:239 -- list_active_accounts orders by (Account.sort_order, Account.name) and feeds the SAME forms (templates.py:232,340), so within one form accounts honor user ordering but categories do not.

Not already known: plan.md:2184-2192 records this EXACT defect for ACCOUNTS as P-2 ("every sibling form honours the user's sort_order"), rated Low, and FIXED in commit a608d77 (plan.md:2233) by switching to order_by(Account.sort_order, Account.name). The category dedupe (commit b58adf1, plan.md:2234) explicitly preserved (group_name, item_name) as "no behavior change," leaving categories un-fixed. No tracked P-item, quality-pass ACCEPT row, or disable covers the CATEGORY sort_order ordering -- the quality-pass register has no category_service ordering row, and grep for category+sort_order+dropdown in docs/ returns nothing. Distinct from P-1/P-3.

No test guards the ordering: test_categories.py:1642-1657 (and the /grid dropdown test ~1479) assert only presence/absence of options via select_option_values, never order. So the defect is uncovered and the suggested fix (lead with Category.sort_order, mirroring the P-2 account fix) is sound. Severity corrected MED->LOW to match the developer's own Low rating of the identical account defect (P-2): display-ordering only, no monetary miscomputation.

### 67. [DECIMAL/JUDGMENT] project_annual_escrow quantizes each component before summing, unlike calculate_monthly_escrow's sum-then-round
- **Location:** `app/services/escrow_calculator.py` :: 182,184
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** project_annual_escrow does `annual_total += annual.quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP)` per component (line 182) then `annual_total.quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP)` again on the sum (line 184) -- premature per-component rounding before summation. calculate_monthly_escrow (line 125-128) and committed_monthly (obligations_aggregator.py:144-149) both keep intermediate sums at full precision and round once. For three components each contributing an annual with a sub-cent fraction, per-component rounding then summing diverges by a cent from a true sum-then-round (verified).
- **Why it matters:** It is an internally inconsistent rounding discipline within the same module: two of three escrow functions round-once, one rounds-per-item. With inflation multipliers (line 180) producing fractional cents this can yield a yearly projection a cent off from the equivalent monthly*12. Lower stakes because the inflation path itself is approximate, but it contradicts the project's documented 'round once at the boundary' rule.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop the per-component quantize at line 182 and round only the final annual_total at line 184, matching calculate_monthly_escrow.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE -- confirmed by reading app/services/escrow_calculator.py:
- Line 182: `annual_total += annual.quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP)` rounds EACH component before adding to the running total (intermediate rounding).
- Line 184: `annual_total.quantize(TWO_PLACES, ROUND_HALF_UP)` rounds the sum again.
- By contrast calculate_monthly_escrow (lines 125-128) keeps `total += monthly` at full precision and quantizes once at return; committed_monthly in app/services/obligations_aggregator.py (lines 144-149) does `total += monthly` at full precision and rounds once via round_money(total). So the finding's characterization of all three functions is exact.

DIVERGENCE IS REAL -- reproduced with a 3-component inflated case (4800@3.3%, 2400@4.1%, 1200@2.7%, offset=2): round-then-sum yields 8988.53 vs sum-then-round 8988.54, a one-cent difference. The finding's "diverges by a cent (verified)" is correct.

VIOLATES A DOCUMENTED RULE -- app/utils/money.py module docstring lines 4-5: "Full-precision Decimal arithmetic everywhere in the codebase; rounding happens once, here, at the display or persistence boundary"; round_money docstring lines 48-50: "Use this at the boundary; keep intermediate arithmetic at full Decimal precision." Line 182's per-component quantize is intermediate rounding, contradicting this canonical rule that the two sibling functions follow.

NOT TEST-COVERED -- tests/test_services/test_escrow_calculator.py:142-248 (TestProjectAnnualEscrow) only uses round annual amounts (4800/2400/1200) with rates (0.03/0.05/-0.02/0.50) that never produce the multi-component fractional-cent collision, so no existing test would distinguish round-once from round-per-component, and none asserts the round-once discipline for this function.

SCOPE/SEVERITY CAP -- exhaustive grep (app/routes, app/services, app/templates, scripts, *.html, *.js) shows project_annual_escrow has ZERO production callers; it is referenced only by its own def (escrow_calculator.py:150) and the test file. The dashboard's _project_next_year_escrow (app/routes/loan/dashboard.py) is a separate local helper that calls calculate_monthly_escrow, not this function. So no user-facing money is currently affected -- the defect is latent. This keeps severity at LOW (finding's LOW is correct).

NOT ALREADY KNOWN -- not P-1 (loan escrow baseline in loan_resolver/_state.py), not P-3 (negative deduction), not a documented disable; the function is dead/test-only code, distinct from the quality-pass accept set.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION rather than CONFIRMED: the fix is a genuine judgment call -- (a) round-once vs. displaying per-component-rounded rows whose displayed cents sum to the shown total is a legitimate financial-display choice, and (b) because the function has no caller, the developer should decide whether to fix the rounding to match the round-once rule, wire it into a projection view, or delete it as dead code. The suggested fix (drop per-component quantize at 182, keep only line 184) is the consistency-preserving option but the developer must confirm the intended display behavior.

### 68. [DRY/JUDGMENT] Income/expense aggregation rule is re-implemented in the analytics route instead of supplied by calendar_service
- **Location:** `app/routes/analytics.py` :: 423-428
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-arch-solid
- **Claim:** `_build_calendar_weeks` computes per-day `income_total = sum(e.amount for e in entries if e.is_income)` and `expense_total = sum(abs(e.amount) for e in entries if not e.is_income)`. This is the identical business rule (income = signed sum of income entries; expense = sum of abs of non-income entries) already implemented in app/services/calendar_service.py:402-405 (`_assign_transactions_to_days`) at the month level. The same financial-classification logic lives in two layers with different shape, invisible to R0801. Additionally the route uses bare `sum()` (int 0 start) while the service uses `Decimal('0')`, so an empty day yields int 0 rather than Decimal.
- **Why it matters:** Financial aggregation belongs in the service per the layer boundary; duplicating the income/expense rule risks the calendar's per-day totals and the service's per-month totals diverging if the rule changes (e.g. how transfers or excluded statuses are treated), and the bare-sum int/Decimal mismatch is a latent type inconsistency.
- **Suggested fix:** Have calendar_service return per-day income/expense totals (alongside day_entries) so the route only renders them; if kept in the route, factor the rule into one shared helper and seed `sum()` with `Decimal('0')`.
- **Verifier evidence:** Both citations verified verbatim. ROUTE app/routes/analytics.py:423-428 inside _build_calendar_weeks: `income_total = sum(e.amount for e in entries if e.is_income)` and `expense_total = sum(abs(e.amount) for e in entries if not e.is_income)` -- bare sum(), int-0 default, per-DAY. SERVICE app/services/calendar_service.py:402-405 inside _assign_transactions_to_days: `if entry.is_income: total_income += entry.amount else: total_expenses += abs(entry.amount)`, seeded by total_income/total_expenses = Decimal("0") at lines 386-387, per-MONTH. The sign-classification rule (income = signed sum of is_income entries; expense = sum of abs of non-income) is genuinely the same in both, with int-vs-Decimal seed mismatch as claimed -- all factually accurate.

NUANCE that lowers severity below MED: the SUBSTANTIVE business logic is NOT duplicated. The income/expense classification (the is_balance_contributing filter at line 392, the is_income derivation `txn.transaction_type_id == income_type_id` at line 347 via _build_day_entry, and the cross-period dedup at lines 384/390/398) all live ONLY in the service. The route operates on already-classified DayEntry objects whose .is_income is precomputed (calendar_service.py:90,347), so the only thing duplicated is a trivial 2-line fold-by-sign, not the "rule" that decides what is income/expense. If the meaningful classification rule changed (transfers, excluded statuses), it changes in _build_day_entry/is_balance_contributing -- one place -- and both totals follow automatically; the route's divergence risk is limited to the sign-fold itself.

Service exposes no per-day totals today: MonthSummary (calendar_service.py:114-122) carries whole-month total_income/total_expenses plus raw day_entries dict, so the route is deriving something the service does not provide, not re-deriving an existing service output. The suggested fix (push per-day totals into the service) is a defensible layer-boundary improvement but is relocation of a trivial sum, a design judgment, not a defect repair.

int/Decimal mismatch is real but inert: template app/templates/analytics/_calendar_month.html:52-56 guards with `{% if day.income_total %}` (both int 0 and Decimal("0") are falsy) and renders via `"{:,.0f}".format(...)` which works on both types; the empty-cell branch already uses Decimal("0") (analytics.py:413-414). No observable defect manifests.

Tests: grep of tests/ found NO test exercising _build_calendar_weeks, income_total, or expense_total (only tests/test_services/test_calendar_service.py:998 tests the per-day FILTER, not per-day totals) -- so the route fold is uncovered, but this is low-risk given its triviality.

Already-known check: not P-1/P-3, no inline disable involved. quality-pass.md rows 38 and 408 review calendar_service.py's dataclasses and the _MonthBuildContext bundle but NOT this route/service total duplication; the register's "F4" (rows 435/455) is the unrelated LOAN _render_rate_history, not this analytics finding -- so not already documented.

### 69. [DRY/JUDGMENT] change_password and invalidate_sessions routes reimplement invalidate_other_sessions inline instead of calling the dedicated helper
- **Location:** `app/routes/auth.py` :: 578-584 (change_password); 611-614 (invalidate_sessions)
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** auth-sec
- **Claim:** session_helpers.invalidate_other_sessions exists specifically to bump user.session_invalidated_at, commit, and refresh SESSION_CREATED_AT_KEY with a single `now` (and emit the audit event). change_password sets `current_user.session_invalidated_at = now` then relies on stamp_login_session to write the cookie; invalidate_sessions sets the column directly then calls stamp_session_refresh. Neither uses the helper, so the single-now invalidate-other-sessions invariant lives in three places. The test_session_invalidation.py docstring (lines 837-846) explicitly flags this: 'the inline implementations in change_password and invalidate_sessions were not refactored to use the new helper'.
- **Why it matters:** The strict-less-than survive-current-session invariant (cookie created_at == db invalidated_at) is security-critical; three independent implementations multiply the chance one drifts (e.g. a future edit uses two now() calls in one site, pushing the cookie ahead and logging the current user out, or behind and surviving a later bump). Centralizing would also give these two paths the structured other_sessions_invalidated audit event they currently lack.
- **Suggested fix:** Refactor both routes to call invalidate_other_sessions(current_user, reason) (with the appropriate reason), removing the inline column write; for change_password keep stamp_login_session for _fresh_login_at/activity but let the helper own the created_at + DB bump.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every literal claim in F4 verified against committed code.

FACTUAL ACCURACY (all confirmed):
- app/routes/auth.py:578-584 (change_password): `now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)`; `current_user.session_invalidated_at = now`; `record_security_event(...)`; `db.session.commit()`; then `stamp_login_session(now)` (line 584). Inline reimplementation of the column-bump + cookie refresh, exactly as claimed.
- app/routes/auth.py:611-614 (invalidate_sessions): `now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)`; `current_user.session_invalidated_at = now`; `db.session.commit()`; `stamp_session_refresh(now)`. Inline, as claimed.
- app/utils/session_helpers.py:233-306: invalidate_other_sessions exists for exactly this -- bumps session_invalidated_at with a single internal `now` (line 296), commits (298), refreshes SESSION_CREATED_AT_KEY (300), and emits EVT_OTHER_SESSIONS_INVALIDATED (302-306). Confirmed only two callers use it: auth.py:893 (backup_code_consumed) and auth.py:1271 (mfa_disabled). So the single-now invalidate-other-sessions logic genuinely lives in 3 places.
- Audit-event gap confirmed: change_password logs EVT_PASSWORD_CHANGED (585), invalidate_sessions logs EVT_SESSIONS_INVALIDATED (615); neither emits other_sessions_invalidated.
- Test docstring quoted verbatim: tests/test_adversarial/test_session_invalidation.py:841-846 states "the inline implementations in change_password and invalidate_sessions were not refactored to use the new helper (out of scope for C-08)".

WHY NEEDS-DECISION (not CONFIRMED): the suggested fix is NOT a clean drop-in and the inline form is a deliberate, documented design choice, so the correct resolution is a developer security/design judgment:
1. change_password (auth.py:571-583, comment "The stamp lives BEFORE the second commit so both writes land in one transaction") deliberately bundles the session_invalidated_at bump AND record_security_event into ONE commit sharing ONE `now`, so the audit_log row, the banner column, and the cookie all carry identical microseconds. record_security_event does NOT commit by design (security_events.py:159-161). invalidate_other_sessions does its OWN commit (session_helpers.py:298) with its OWN internal `now` (296). Calling the helper here would split the atomic transaction and break the single-`now` correlation the comment exists to guarantee.
2. invalidate_sessions needs stamp_session_refresh (created+activity, NOT fresh-login); the helper only writes SESSION_CREATED_AT_KEY, so the route would still need a second cookie write with a second `now`.

NOT a present defect: behavior is correct today and pinned by dedicated regression tests (test_session_invalidation.py:848-894 TestExistingInvariantsPreserved, plus :740-748 single-now regression guard) that lock the bump so a future refactor cannot silently drop it. So this is a latent DRY/maintenance risk, LOW severity (correct).

ALREADY-KNOWN check (false): grepped docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/. quality-pass.md:412 reviewed auth.py and recorded invalidate_other_sessions ORDERING in the MFA branches (reauth/mfa_confirm/mfa_verify) as UNCHANGED -- it does NOT cover the change_password/invalidate_sessions inline duplication. deep-quality-hunt.md:974-975 records a DISTINCT session_helpers finding about the READER side (_fresh_login_is_within/_idle_session_is_fresh/_mfa_pending_is_fresh triplication), explicitly the consumer side, not this producer/invalidation-side F4. Not P-1/P-3. So F4 is not already documented.

### 70. [DRY/JUDGMENT] Retirement settings 422 re-render passes ~10 template kwargs the partial never reads, hand-duplicating settings._empty_section_context()
- **Location:** `app/routes/retirement.py` :: 369-385
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** The validation-error re-render passes `accounts=[]`, `grouped={}`, `filing_statuses=[]`, `tax_types=[]`, `bracket_sets=[]`, `fica_configs=[]`, `state_configs=[]`, `account_types=[]`, `types_in_use=set()`, `mfa_enabled=False`. The dashboard template includes only the active section's partial (`{% elif active_section == 'retirement' %}{% include 'settings/_retirement.html' %}`), and `_retirement.html` references only `errors`, `settings`, and `form_data` (verified by grep over the partial). The skeleton references no section vars unconditionally. So all ten extra kwargs are unused, and they re-state a partial, drifting copy of `settings._empty_section_context()`.
- **Why it matters:** Gold-plating (rule 13) and a DRY hazard: the hardcoded subset can silently drift from `_empty_section_context()` in settings.py (it already omits the companion/categories keys), so a future change to the dashboard skeleton that newly references one of those keys would break only this route, with no compile-time link between the two lists.
- **Suggested fix:** Render with just `settings`, `form_data`, `errors` (the only keys the retirement partial uses), or import and splat `settings._empty_section_context()` then override the error slice.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read app/routes/retirement.py:369-385 -- the 422 re-render passes exactly the 10 claimed kwargs (accounts=[], grouped={}, filing_statuses=[], tax_types=[], bracket_sets=[], fica_configs=[], state_configs=[], account_types=[], types_in_use=set(), mfa_enabled=False) plus settings/form_data/errors. grep over app/templates/settings/_retirement.html shows it references ONLY form_data, errors, settings (lines 1,10-31). dashboard.html:119-135 includes only the ACTIVE section's partial via {% elif active_section == 'retirement' %}{% include 'settings/_retirement.html' %}; the section vars appear ONLY inside that {% if/elif %} dispatch, and {% block scripts %} (141-152) references only active_section -- no unconditional reference to any of the 10 kwargs. So all 10 are dead at runtime for the retirement 422 path. The subset is a drifting partial copy of app/routes/settings.py:156-185 _empty_section_context() (18 keys), omitting 8 incl. companion/category keys (categories, archived_categories, group_names, icon_choices, active_companions, inactive_companions, edit_companion_id, form_values) -- confirming the DRY-drift claim. In the SAME file family, settings.py:355-382 _render_companions_section already splats _empty_section_context() then overrides only its slice, and the quality-pass register (docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:386-387) explicitly endorsed centralizing this exact context to stop the drift; the retirement route was never brought into that pattern. Not test-locked: tests/test_routes/test_retirement.py 422 tests (e.g. test_update_settings_invalid_swr:986-1006) assert only status_code==422 + unchanged DB, never the kwargs. already_known check: no quality-pass ACCEPT row covers retirement.py update_settings's hand-listed context (rows 122/136/143 cover retirement_dashboard_service, retirement_gap_calculator, settings.py only); the duplicate-code disable that once sat here was removed today by commit 3d34aa8 solely because it "suppresses nothing," NOT because the kwargs were validated correct -- and that commit left an orphaned `# pylint: enable=duplicate-code` at retirement.py:386 (grep: 0 disable, 1 enable in-file) and the dead-kwargs divergence untouched. Neither P-1 nor P-3. Verdict CONFIRMED (not NEEDS-DECISION): the fix is a deterministic cleanup -- render with settings/form_data/errors only, or splat _empty_section_context() and override the error slice to match the ratified companion-render pattern -- not a money/design judgment.

### 71. [DRY/JUDGMENT] 'First active checking account by sort_order,id' query duplicated across the two account resolvers
- **Location:** `app/services/account_resolver.py` :: 60-68 vs 121-131
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** resolve_grid_account step 3 (lines 60-68) and resolve_analytics_account fallback (lines 121-131) contain the identical query: 'ref_cache.acct_type_id(CHECKING)' then 'query(Account).filter_by(user_id=..., is_active=True, account_type_id=checking_type_id).order_by(Account.sort_order, Account.id).first()'. The 'first active checking account' rule -- which account is the user's canonical checking account -- is defined twice in one file with different variable shaping. The 'is this the checking type' predicate (account_type_id == acct_type_id(CHECKING)) is separately reproduced at ~11 sites across services and routes, each re-resolving checking_type_id.
- **Why it matters:** A change to canonical-checking selection (e.g. add a tiebreaker, prefer a flagged primary account) must be edited in both resolver branches or the grid and analytics pages pick different accounts for the same user.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract a 'first_active_checking_account(user_id)' helper both resolvers call; consider an Account.is_checking property to centralize the 11 inline type predicates.
- **Verifier evidence:** Core claim verified by reading app/services/account_resolver.py. resolve_grid_account step 3 (lines 60-66) and resolve_analytics_account fallback (lines 121-131) contain the identical "first active checking account" query: both compute checking_type_id = ref_cache.acct_type_id(AcctTypeEnum.CHECKING), then run db.session.query(Account).filter_by(user_id=user_id, is_active=True, account_type_id=checking_type_id).order_by(Account.sort_order, Account.id).first(). The two blocks differ only in cosmetic shaping (grid uses inline filter_by kwargs at line 63; analytics uses multiline kwargs at lines 124-128), which is exactly why R0801's near-textual matcher misses it. The canonical-checking-account business rule is thus defined twice in one file.

Real-issue assessment: genuine DRY violation. resolve_grid_account has 7 callers (dashboard_service.py:60, transfers/_helpers.py:184/222, transfers/forms.py:29, transfers/mutations.py:254/472, grid.py:123/612/695) and resolve_analytics_account has 4 (budget_variance_service.py:241, calendar_service.py:162/212, spending_trend_service.py:142). A future change to canonical-checking selection (tiebreaker, primary-flag preference) edited in only one branch would make grid and analytics pages resolve different accounts for the same user. tests/test_services/test_account_resolver.py covers the grid path's checking selection (test_no_setting_returns_checking:25, test_deterministic_ordering:189) but NO test asserts the two resolvers pick the SAME account, so the divergence risk is uncaught.

Secondary "~11 inline type predicates" claim is PARTIALLY INACCURATE but does not affect the verdict. grep of AcctTypeEnum.CHECKING shows the other sites are heterogeneous, NOT copies of this query: anchor_service.py:231 / accounts/anchor.py:108 / accounts/crud.py:354 are boolean "is THIS account checking" anchor-true-up guards; auth_service.py:805 creates a checking account at signup; loan/dashboard.py:505, investment_dashboard_service.py:433, year_end_summary/_data.py:268 pick "first checking in a pre-fetched list"; savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:170 collects ALL checking ids. They already share the centralized acct_type_id(CHECKING) cache lookup (the DRY-correct id resolution); only the == account_type_id comparison is repeated, and an Account.is_checking property is a lower-value, separable suggestion.

already_known = false: account_resolver.py does not appear in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md, plan.md, or deep-quality-hunt.md, nor in any documented disable; not P-1 or P-3. Severity LOW is correct: today's two copies are textually equivalent so behavior is consistent; the defect is latent future-divergence risk, not a present miscalculation. The DRY fix (extract first_active_checking_account(user_id)) is clear; the is_checking-property part is a minor design call, so a developer-side decision exists but the core extraction is unambiguous -- hence CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION.

### 72. [DRY/JUDGMENT] amortization_engine uses bare '/ 12' for the months-per-year factor while the rest of the financial core uses the named MONTHS_PER_YEAR constant
- **Location:** `app/services/amortization_engine.py` :: 219, 514, 626
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** loan-amort
- **Claim:** calculate_monthly_payment (line 219), _recast_for_rate_change (line 514), and project_forward state setup (line 626) all divide the annual rate by a bare literal 12 to get the monthly rate. app/utils/money.py defines MONTHS_PER_YEAR = Decimal('12') as 'the canonical' month-conversion factor, and rate_period_engine.py (lines 369, 558) and interest_projection.py (line 142) consistently import and use it. amortization_engine imports round_money from app.utils.money but not MONTHS_PER_YEAR.
- **Why it matters:** The project rule is 'name every business-rule literal' and a named constant for this exact factor already exists and is used by sibling modules. The numeric results are identical (Decimal/int == Decimal/Decimal), so this is not a correctness bug -- but the inconsistency means a reader cannot grep MONTHS_PER_YEAR to find every annual->monthly conversion, and the months-per-year semantics are spelled three different ways across the same financial core.
- **Suggested fix:** Import MONTHS_PER_YEAR from app.utils.money and replace the three bare '/ 12' divisors with it, matching rate_period_engine and interest_projection.
- **Verifier evidence:** VERIFIED ACCURATE: amortization_engine.py:219 `monthly_rate = annual_rate / 12`; :514 `period_rate / 12 if period_rate > 0 else Decimal("0")`; :626 `inputs.annual_rate / 12 if inputs.annual_rate > 0 else Decimal("0")` -- all three divide an annual rate by the bare literal 12 (docstring :477 also spells it `annual_rate / 12`, correctly not flagged as a code site). money.py:42 defines `MONTHS_PER_YEAR = Decimal("12")`, documented at money.py:27-33 as the canonical month-conversion factor "defined exactly once here". amortization_engine.py:24 imports `from app.utils.money import round_money` only -- NOT MONTHS_PER_YEAR. Sibling financial-core modules consistently use the constant for annual->monthly rate conversion: rate_period_engine.py:369 (`annual_rate / MONTHS_PER_YEAR`), :558; interest_projection.py:142 (`apy / MONTHS_PER_YEAR`); and additionally debt_strategy_service.py:484 and escrow_calculator.py:67,125. amortization_engine is the lone outlier in the loan/interest core. NOT A CORRECTNESS BUG: confirmed via python that `Decimal('0.06')/12 == Decimal('0.06')/Decimal('12')` -> True; results are bit-identical. NOT ALREADY KNOWN: not P-1 (loan escrow threshold) or P-3 (negative deduction). The amortization_engine quality-pass row (quality-pass.md:120 "REVIEWED -- clean, 7 ACCEPT, the bundle exemplar") and every plan.md entry (commits 0e8b986/c4f01e6/7cc8fe1) concern parameter-object/decomposition refactors (ProjectionInputs, _ProjectionState, AmortizationRow, PayoffRequest) -- nothing in quality-pass.md, plan.md, or remediation_follow_up.md examined the `/ 12` vs MONTHS_PER_YEAR question. The lines predate the cleanup (git -S shows they last changed in 0e8b986, which only removed dead code / touched surrounding lines) and were never specifically reviewed or accepted. The finding is a valid DRY/named-literal consistency gap per coding.md ("Name every business-rule literal") and money.py's own SSOT framing. Out-of-scope note: other bare `/ 12` survivors exist (retirement_dashboard_service.py:682, pension_calculator.py:65) but are not part of this loan-core finding. LOW severity because purely cosmetic/readability with zero numeric impact.

### 73. [DRY/JUDGMENT] calculate_monthly_payment inlines the literal 12 instead of MONTHS_PER_YEAR used by sibling amortization paths
- **Location:** `app/services/amortization_engine.py` :: 219
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** calculate_monthly_payment computes `monthly_rate = annual_rate / 12` with a bare int literal 12 (line 219), while the project canonicalizes the months-per-year factor as app.utils.money.MONTHS_PER_YEAR (Decimal('12')) and uses it in rate_period_engine._amortize_forward (line 369), debt_strategy_service._accrue_interest (line 484), and escrow_calculator. The module docstring for money.py:31-33 states the factor 'is defined exactly once' and 'any future 26/12 inlining is a regression of D6-05.'
- **Why it matters:** It is a documented anti-regression: the canonical monthly-conversion constant exists specifically so the divisor is not re-inlined. annual_rate/12 (int) vs annual_rate/MONTHS_PER_YEAR (Decimal) produce identical Decimal results today, so this is a maintainability/DRY consistency issue, not a value defect, but it is exactly the inlining the standard flags.
- **Suggested fix:** Import MONTHS_PER_YEAR from app.utils.money and use it for the /12 at line 219 (and any other inlined 12 month divisor in this engine).
- **Verifier evidence:** Factually accurate. app/services/amortization_engine.py:219 reads `monthly_rate = annual_rate / 12` with a bare int literal; the module imports ONLY `round_money` from app.utils.money (line 24), never MONTHS_PER_YEAR. The cited sibling canonical-constant paths verified: rate_period_engine.py:369 `annual_rate / MONTHS_PER_YEAR`; debt_strategy_service.py:484 `... / MONTHS_PER_YEAR`; escrow_calculator.py:67 and :125 `/ MONTHS_PER_YEAR` (it imports MONTHS_PER_YEAR at line 12). The money.py:31-33 docstring states verbatim that the factor "is defined exactly once here; any future 26/12 inlining is a regression of D6-05."

Real issue, and BROADER than the finding states: the same inlined `/ 12` rate-conversion divisor occurs three times in this one file -- amortization_engine.py:219 (calculate_monthly_payment), :514 (_recast_for_rate_change: `period_rate / 12`), and :626 (project_forward state init: `inputs.annual_rate / 12`). The finding cites only line 219. Value-equivalent today: I verified `Decimal(r)/12 == Decimal(r)/Decimal('12')` for r in {0.06, 0.0725, 0.045, 0.10, 0.0333} (all True, identical results), because Python coerces the int operand to Decimal at context precision. So this is a maintainability/DRY anti-regression consistency issue, not a money-value defect -- exactly as the finding characterizes it. Not rule-13 gold-plating (the constant already exists and is used by siblings); not safe-by-construction in the DRY sense (a future change to the divisor convention would silently skip these three sites).

Not already known. deep-quality-hunt.md discusses MONTHS_PER_YEAR/D6-05 only for escrow_calculator (line 356, round-each vs sum-then-round) and routes/investment.py:53 (`_PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR = 26` int duplication, line 939), plus a separate `_months_between` calendar-span `*12` finding (lines 589-608) -- none address the amortization_engine rate-conversion `/12` inlining. quality-pass.md:120 marks amortization_engine.py "REVIEWED -- clean (7 ACCEPT)" but those ACCEPT rows are param-object/DTO disable justifications (quality-pass.md:198,211,306), not this divisor. Not P-1 (escrow threshold) nor P-3 (negative deduction); not a documented inline disable.

Verdict CONFIRMED rather than NEEDS-DECISION: the fix is mechanical and non-judgmental (import MONTHS_PER_YEAR and substitute at lines 219, 514, 626). Severity LOW is correct because all three sites are value-equivalent today and no money is mismanaged.

### 74. [DRY/JUDGMENT] live_amount_overrides is rebuilt independently in three balance_as_of_date sub-paths, recomputing salary/loan derivations per call
- **Location:** `app/services/balance_resolver.py` :: 851-853 (target), 891-893 (prefix), plus per-period in period_subtotal 565-568
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** balance-grid
- **Claim:** balance_as_of_date builds amount_overrides twice within one call: once for the prefix span inside _project_to_period_before (lines 891-893) and once for the target period (lines 851-853). Each call re-imports and re-runs income_service.live_projected_net and loan_payment_service.live_loan_transfer_amounts (live_amount_overrides, lines 398-405). balances_for and period_subtotal each build their own as well. Unlike the grid (which builds it once and threads it via amount_overrides=), balance_as_of_date never threads a single override map across its prefix+target span.
- **Why it matters:** The live-override builders re-run paycheck/tax and loan-resolver computations; doing it twice (prefix and target) per calendar balance request is redundant work on the calendar surface. It is also a maintainability smell -- the 'build once, thread everywhere' pattern the grid established is not followed here.
- **Suggested fix:** Build the override map once over the union of prefix+target transactions in balance_as_of_date and thread it into both _project_to_period_before (via a new param) and _sum_period_as_of.
- **Verifier evidence:** Cited lines verified against committed code. live_amount_overrides is called independently in four places: balance_resolver.py:851-853 (target span in balance_as_of_date), 891-893 (prefix span in _project_to_period_before), 565-568 (period_subtotal), and 487-490 (balances_for). live_amount_overrides (371-405) imports income_service + loan_payment_service and calls live_projected_net + live_loan_transfer_amounts. The grid threads a SINGLE map instead: grid.py:485 builds it once and passes amount_overrides= into _build_grid_balances (494) and _build_grid_subtotals (532); balance_as_of_date does NOT thread across its prefix+target sub-paths.

Redundancy is real and substantive: live_projected_net (income_service.py:218-232) runs paycheck_calculator.project_salary over the FULL pay-period set once per distinct SalaryProfile present in the candidate set; live_loan_transfer_amounts (loan_payment_service.py:658-665) resolves each distinct loan's PITI via _resolve_loan_piti. A recurring biweekly paycheck / derive-from-loan transfer appears in BOTH the prefix span (anchor..target-1, line 882-885) and the target span (target period, line 847-849), so project_salary and _resolve_loan_piti genuinely re-execute for the same profile/loan within one balance_as_of_date call. On the calendar surface the cost is multiplied: calendar_service.py:453 calls _compute_month_end_balance (-> balance_as_of_date) once per month inside the year-view month loop.

Suggested fix is valid: the override map is keyed by transaction_id (dict[int, Decimal]) and live_projected_net sources all_periods internally (income_service.py:222), so a union map over prefix+target txns yields identical per-txn values and would NOT break the boundary invariant locked by test_calendar_equals_resolver_at_period_boundary (test_balance_resolver.py:946-1004, asserts balance_as_of_date == balances_for at period end_date).

Minor overstatement in the claim: 're-imports' overstates -- the from-import at line 398 is a cached sys.modules lookup, not a re-execution; the real cost is the re-run of the salary/loan derivations, which is accurate.

Not already-known: not P-1 (loan escrow threshold) or P-3 (negative deduction); no documented disable on these lines; quality-pass.md touches balance_resolver only for the 3-bucket entry-partition extraction (row 2, 65cd4c2) and accounts/detail.py F-6 reuse -- neither addresses the prefix/target override-map threading.

This is a DRY/efficiency cleanup on a correct path (numbers are right; only compute is redundant), so LOW is appropriate. The fix requires adding a param to _project_to_period_before and _sum_period_as_of -- a signature change / design choice, but a straightforward one with no correctness fork.

### 75. [DRY/JUDGMENT] sync_entry_payback re-derives the credit-entry sum inline instead of reusing compute_entry_sums
- **Location:** `app/services/entry_credit_workflow.py` :: 111-114
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** transfer-txn
- **Claim:** sync_entry_payback computes total_credit by filtering txn.entries for is_credit and summing (111-114). entry_service.compute_entry_sums (385-405) already computes (sum_debit, sum_credit) over the same entry collection using the identical is_credit partition. The payback amount -- the money the user owes next period -- is therefore derived by a hand-rolled copy of the credit-sum business rule rather than the shared helper.
- **Why it matters:** The CC Payback amount must always equal the sum of credit entries. Having that sum defined in two places (the canonical compute_entry_sums and this inline copy) is the exact drift class CLAUDE.md DRY/SOLID targets: a future change to how credit entries are summed (e.g. excluding cleared credit, or a sign convention) would have to be made in both, and a miss silently mis-sizes real projected debt.
- **Suggested fix:** Import and use entry_service.compute_entry_sums(txn.entries) to obtain sum_credit (guarding the import cycle if needed), or extract a shared sum_credit_entries helper consumed by both.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUALLY ACCURATE. app/services/entry_credit_workflow.py:111-114 builds `credit_entries = [e for e in txn.entries if e.is_credit]` then `total_credit = sum((e.amount for e in credit_entries), Decimal("0"))`. app/services/entry_service.py:385-405 (compute_entry_sums) partitions the SAME entry collection on the SAME `entry.is_credit` flag, accumulating `sum_credit += entry.amount`. The credit-sum business rule is genuinely defined in both places. compute_entry_sums is the canonical helper, reused at entry_service.py:444 and dashboard_service.py:293 -- so the inline version is the odd one out. This is exactly the kind of semantic (non-textual) duplication R0801 misses, and it is NOT in plan.md (the only entry_credit_workflow row, plan.md:1083, is the unrelated _create_payback body 205-212 vs credit_workflow:238-245) nor in the quality-pass.md register; it is not P-1/P-3.

REAL but the finding's suggested fix is underspecified on two material constraints, making this a developer design call rather than a mechanical reuse: (1) IMPORT CYCLE is live, not hypothetical -- entry_service.py:31 already does `from app.services.entry_credit_workflow import sync_entry_payback`, so entry_credit_workflow importing compute_entry_sums from entry_service at module level would be circular (AST-confirmed edge entry_service -> entry_credit_workflow). The finding flags this only parenthetically; it is in fact the dominant constraint and rules out option 1 as written. (2) SHAPE MISMATCH -- sync_entry_payback needs the credit_entries LIST itself (consumed at lines 125, 129, 134-136, 209-210 to link entries to the payback), not just the Decimal sum. compute_entry_sums returns only (sum_debit, sum_credit) and discards the list, so reuse would force a second pass over txn.entries or a new helper return shape. Not safe-by-construction (no test pins the two summations to agree), not gold-plating, not test-covered as equivalent.

The right fix (extract a cycle-safe shared helper -- e.g. a sum_credit_entries / list-returning partition in app/utils/balance_predicates.py consumed by both, vs. accepting the local inline copy since the list is needed in place) is a DRY/SOLID design judgment for the developer, so NEEDS-DECISION at LOW severity. Decimal discipline is intact in both (Decimal("0") seed prevents int-0 drift); no correctness defect today.

### 76. [DRY/JUDGMENT] build_entry_sums_dict recomputes the E-21 'remaining' rule inline instead of calling compute_remaining
- **Location:** `app/services/entry_service.py` :: 444-447
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** transfer-txn
- **Claim:** build_entry_sums_dict computes remaining = estimated - (debit + credit) inline (445-447), which is exactly the body of compute_remaining (557-558: estimated_amount - sum of all entry amounts). Its sibling builder build_entry_lists_dict calls compute_remaining (512) for the identical quantity. The two grid-feeding builders thus implement the same E-21 declared-base rule two different ways in one module; R0801 misses it because the shapes differ (compute_entry_sums + arithmetic vs a direct call).
- **Why it matters:** compute_remaining's docstring (525-558) is the single E-21 contract ('budget base is estimated_amount unconditionally'). If that rule ever changes (e.g. excludes credit entries, or rounds), build_entry_lists_dict updates automatically but build_entry_sums_dict silently diverges -- the grid cell's over_budget styling and the dashboard bill row would disagree on the same transaction.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace lines 445-447 with remaining = compute_remaining(estimated, txn.entries) and keep total only for the debit/credit/total/pct outputs.
- **Verifier evidence:** Verified the arithmetic equivalence directly. build_entry_sums_dict (app/services/entry_service.py:444-447) computes: debit,credit = compute_entry_sums(txn.entries); total = debit+credit; estimated = Decimal(str(txn.estimated_amount)); remaining = estimated - total. compute_remaining (557-558) computes: total_spent = sum((e.amount for e in entries), Decimal("0")); return estimated_amount - total_spent. compute_entry_sums (398-405) partitions every entry into credit/debit by is_credit, so debit+credit == sum of all entry amounts == total_spent; the two remaining values are arithmetically identical, expressed with different shapes. Its sibling build_entry_lists_dict calls compute_remaining(txn.estimated_amount, entries) at line 512 for the identical quantity. All five functions live in the same module, so calling compute_remaining adds no import (line 512 already does it). The claim is factually accurate.

The issue is genuine and in fact broader: a THIRD copy exists in dashboard_service._compute_entry_progress (app/services/dashboard_service.py:293-295), which already calls BOTH compute_entry_sums (293) for debit/credit/total AND compute_remaining (295) for remaining -- exactly the finding's suggested fix -- with over_budget expressed as total > estimated (301) vs build_entry_sums_dict's remaining < Decimal("0") (454). So the E-21 declared-base rule (compute_remaining docstring 525-558, the single E-21 contract) is implemented in three shapes; if it ever changes, build_entry_lists_dict and dashboard update via the call, build_entry_sums_dict's inline copy silently diverges -- the grid cell's over_budget styling and the dashboard bill row would disagree. The Decimal(str(...)) round-trip at 446 is also redundant (estimated_amount is db.Numeric(12,2) per transaction.py:169, already a Decimal). Tests (tests/test_routes/test_grid_entries.py:230,249) assert remaining with hand-computed values, so present-day behavior is correct and the values match -- but the tests do not protect against the future-divergence risk the finding describes.

Not already known: quality-pass.md row 36 for entry_service.py is scoped only to the create_entry/EntryDetails refactor (commit d641e06) and never mentions build_entry_sums_dict, compute_remaining, or this E-21 duplication. R0801 register (plan.md) row 68 pairs entry_service:583-608 with dashboard_service:575-593, not these lines -- R0801's textual matcher misses this because the shapes differ, exactly as claimed. Not P-1/P-3. No inline pylint disable exists in the file.

CONFIRMED (not NEEDS-DECISION): the fix is a same-module DRY consolidation (replace 445-447 with remaining = compute_remaining(estimated, txn.entries) and keep total for debit/credit/total/pct), not a financial/design judgment. Severity corrected to LOW: behavior is currently correct and test-covered; this is a maintainability/divergence-risk DRY defect, not a live correctness bug, so MED overstates it.

### 77. [DRY/JUDGMENT] Two 'suggested per-period contribution' computations duplicate the limit/periods rule, both with the wrong (implicit) rounding mode
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py` :: 386-388
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** _compute_suggested_contribution returns (remaining_limit / max(remaining_periods,1)).quantize(TWO_PLACES) at lines 386-388 (bare quantize, ROUND_HALF_EVEN). routes/investment.py:200 independently computes (limit / 26).quantize(TWO_PLACES) for the same UX concept (a per-period contribution suggestion under the annual limit). The two share the same business rule (spread the annual limit over periods, round to cents) in different shapes, both omitting the explicit rounding mode -- invisible to R0801's textual matcher.
- **Why it matters:** Same semantic computation in two places with two formulas and the same latent rounding-mode defect; a fix to one (e.g. switching to round_money or to remaining-periods semantics) will not propagate to the other.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract a single suggested-contribution helper that takes (annual_limit, ytd, remaining_periods) and rounds with round_money; have both the route and the dashboard service call it.
- **Verifier evidence:** Both cited lines verified against the committed source. app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:386-388 -- `_compute_suggested_contribution` returns `(remaining_limit / max(remaining_periods, 1)).quantize(TWO_PLACES)` with TWO_PLACES = Decimal("0.01") (line 68) and NO `rounding=` arg, so it reaches Python's default ROUND_HALF_EVEN. app/routes/investment.py:200 -- the transfer-creation default does `(limit / _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR).quantize(TWO_PLACES)`, also bare (TWO_PLACES at line 51, _PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR = 26 at line 53). Both encode the same UX concept "suggested per-period contribution under the annual contribution limit": the service value is rendered as result["suggested_amount"] (line 613), the route value is the default_amount when the user supplies no override (lines 188-200).

Rounding defect is real and documented-as-forbidden: app/utils/money.py:5-11 states ROUND_HALF_UP "is the only default... the convention every hand-computed financial test in this project assumes" and that "Python's Decimal default of ROUND_HALF_EVEN... must never be reached implicitly through a bare .quantize(Decimal("0.01"))." round_money (line 45) is that boundary helper. Neither investment file imports it (grep: no round_money / app.utils.money import in either). Divergence demonstrated: Decimal("3.25")/26 = 0.125 -> bare gives 0.12, round_money gives 0.13 (one cent at exact half-cent boundaries).

Semantic duplication is real and R0801-invisible: same rule "spread the annual limit over periods, round to cents" in two shapes (full limit/26 vs remaining_limit/remaining_periods). Corroborating extra: routes/investment.py:53 `_PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR = 26` (int) duplicates the canonical money.py:41 `PAY_PERIODS_PER_YEAR = Decimal("26")`, whose docstring (lines 31-33) says it is "defined exactly once here; any future 26/12 inlining is a regression of D6-05."

Not test-covered: the only tests of _compute_suggested_contribution (tests/test_routes/test_investment.py:193-219) exercise zero-cap and none-cap, both -> 0.00/0; no positive half-cent case pins the rounding mode. The 269.23 values (test lines 836-977) are user-supplied override amounts ("amount": "269.23"), not computed suggestions. No whole-app structural guard bans bare quantize -- the C17-6 sweeps are per-service (savings_dashboard, loan, year_end), none covers investment.

Not already known: quality-pass.md row 5 for investment_dashboard_service.py (commit e3dbea7) is "REVIEWED (M4: type-precision, bundle-caveat, test-gap)" -- no mention of bare-quantize / rounding-mode. Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). No documented disable applies.

Severity LOW is correct: the value is a UI suggestion/default the user can override before the transfer is created, and the divergence is one cent only at exact half-cent boundaries -- but it is a genuine deviation from the documented round_money standard plus genuine semantic/constant duplication.

### 78. [DRY/JUDGMENT] Progress-percentage uses int() truncation in some surfaces and ROUND_HALF_UP in others for the same 'percent funded' concept
- **Location:** `app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py` :: 322
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-decimal
- **Claim:** _compute_limit_info computes pct = min(100, int(ytd_contributions / limit * 100)) at line 322 (truncates toward zero via int()), and savings_dashboard_service/_goals.py:121-123 likewise uses int(acct_balance / resolved_target * 100). Meanwhile app/utils/money.py provides percent_complete (clamped, quantized ROUND_HALF_UP) used by dashboard_service.py:553 and entry_service.py:591 for the same 'percent of target' concept. So two rounding behaviors (truncate vs HALF_UP) exist across progress-bar surfaces for one semantic computation.
- **Why it matters:** A user at 49.7% funded sees 49% on the investment/savings cards but would see 50% via percent_complete elsewhere -- inconsistent progress reporting for the same underlying ratio, and a re-implementation of a centralized helper that already exists.
- **Suggested fix:** Route the integer progress-bar percentages through percent_complete (or a shared int-percent helper) so all 'percent funded' surfaces agree on clamping and rounding.
- **Verifier evidence:** Could not refute -- every load-bearing claim is independently confirmed in the committed code.

FACTUAL ACCURACY (all verbatim):
- app/services/investment_dashboard_service.py:322 -- `pct = min(100, int(ytd_contributions / limit * 100))` (int() truncates toward zero).
- app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_goals.py:121-123 -- `progress_pct = min(100, int(acct_balance / resolved_target * 100))` (same int() truncation).
- app/utils/money.py:106-133 -- `percent_complete(total, target)` clamps to [0,100] and quantizes with ROUND_HALF_UP (line 128). Its docstring (lines 108-110) explicitly claims it is "The single numeric contract behind every 'percent funded' / progress-bar surface."
- app/services/dashboard_service.py:553 and app/services/entry_service.py:591 both route through `percent_complete`.

DIVERGENCE REPRODUCED EMPIRICALLY (python repl with the actual constants): for a 49.7%-funded ratio (497/1000): percent_complete -> Decimal("49.70"); the budget dashboard renders it via `"{:.0f}".format(...)` (app/templates/dashboard/_savings_goals.html:20) -> "50". The investment card (app/templates/investment/dashboard.html:88 renders limit_info.pct) and the savings card (app/templates/savings/dashboard.html:380 renders gd.progress_pct) render the int()-truncated value -> "49". Same underlying ratio, two displayed percentages -- exactly the inconsistency claimed.

REAL ISSUE: genuine semantic duplication of one "percent funded" concept implemented 3x with two rounding behaviors (HALF_UP vs truncate), and two of the surfaces the helper's own docstring claims to cover do NOT call it. Not intended/tested: test_services/test_savings_dashboard_service.py:169 pins progress_pct==50 only for 5000/10000 (exactly 50%, no fractional part), and :389 only asserts `> 0`; test_routes/test_investment.py:143-191 pins only the zero/None-cap branches, not a fractional truncation boundary. So the int() truncation is incidental, not a deliberately-pinned contract.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN: quality-pass.md rows 5 (investment_dashboard_service) and 6 (savings_dashboard_service pkg) are REVIEWED for type-precision/bundle-caveat/test-gap and untyped-params-bag respectively -- neither row, nor the B7 fix-batch, mentions the percent rounding inconsistency or the un-reused percent_complete helper. Not P-1, not P-3, not a documented disable.

VERDICT: NEEDS-DECISION (not REFUTED) -- the finding is accurate and real, but the correct fix is a developer judgment: which rounding wins for the integer progress label (truncate vs HALF_UP), and whether to route through percent_complete or add a shared int-percent helper. Severity LOW confirmed: balances/contributions remain correct Decimals; only the integer progress label diverges by at most 1 percentage point (cosmetic + DRY), no money is mismanaged.

### 79. [DRY/JUDGMENT] Three near-identical session-freshness helpers duplicate the same ISO-parse-and-bound algorithm across three files
- **Location:** `app/utils/auth_helpers.py; app/__init__.py; app/routes/auth.py` :: auth_helpers.py:311-361 (_fresh_login_is_within); __init__.py:595-667 (_idle_session_is_fresh); auth.py:220-265 (_mfa_pending_is_fresh)
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** both  |  **Cluster:** auth-sec
- **Claim:** All three helpers implement the identical sequence: read an ISO string from flask_session, datetime.fromisoformat, except (TypeError, ValueError) -> fail-closed, reject tzinfo is None, compute elapsed = datetime.now(timezone.utc) - parsed, and bound elapsed against a timedelta threshold. They differ only in two policy bits: missing-key handling (_fresh_login_is_within and _mfa_pending_is_fresh return False; _idle_session_is_fresh returns True) and future-dated handling (the two session helpers treat elapsed<0 as fresh; _mfa_pending_is_fresh rejects it). R0801 cannot detect this because variable names (raw/fresh_at vs raw/last_activity vs raw/pending_at), the threshold source, and the two policy bits differ enough to defeat the near-textual matcher.
- **Why it matters:** These are security gates for idle timeout, step-up re-auth, and the F-002 MFA-replay window. A correctness fix to the shared parse/naive/future-date logic (e.g. a Python fromisoformat edge case, or tightening the future-date posture) must be applied in three places by hand; missing one silently weakens one gate. The 'kept duplicated' rationale in the docstrings refers to test-only _LogCapture helpers, not these production gates.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract a single `_iso_age_within(session_key, threshold, *, missing_is_fresh: bool, future_is_fresh: bool) -> bool` in session_helpers and have all three call sites pass their two policy flags.
- **Verifier evidence:** Read all three cited sites. auth_helpers.py:346-361 (_fresh_login_is_within): raw=flask_session.get(FRESH_LOGIN_AT_KEY); raw is None -> return False; try datetime.fromisoformat except (TypeError,ValueError) -> False; tzinfo is None -> False; elapsed=datetime.now(timezone.utc)-fresh_at; elapsed<timedelta(0) -> return True (fresh); return elapsed<=threshold (threshold is the passed timedelta arg). __init__.py:647-667 (_idle_session_is_fresh): IDENTICAL sequence EXCEPT raw is None -> return True (chicken-and-egg, line 648-653) and threshold=timedelta(minutes=app.config["IDLE_TIMEOUT_MINUTES"]) (line 666). auth.py:245-265 (_mfa_pending_is_fresh): IDENTICAL sequence EXCEPT `if not raw: return False`, future-dated (elapsed<0) -> return False (reject, line 259-264), threshold=_MFA_PENDING_MAX_AGE (module const auth.py:101). So the claim's three differentiators all hold: (a) missing-key policy (False/True/False), (b) future-date policy (fresh/fresh/reject), (c) threshold source (arg / config / module const). This is genuine cross-file semantic duplication R0801's near-textual matcher cannot catch (different var names raw/fresh_at vs raw/last_activity vs raw/pending_at, three threshold sources, two flipped policy bits). NOT already known: grepped docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md and plan.md -- no ACCEPT row or R0801 cluster covers this trio (only categories.py / accounts/anchor.py 2-site extracts appear). session_helpers.py is the PRODUCER/stamping side (stamp_login_session etc.); these three are the unconsolidated READER side. The finding's note that the docstrings' "kept duplicated" rationale refers to test-only _LogCapture helpers, not these gates, is consistent with what I found. NOT a present defect: each helper's distinct policy is independently tested -- test_auth_helpers.py:386 (future-fresh), test_step_up.py:393/410/428 (idle malformed/naive/future-fresh), test_session_invalidation.py:355/390/421/456 (mfa missing/malformed/future-reject/naive). So behavior is currently correct; the duplication is a latent maintenance risk (a shared-logic fix must be made in 3 places). Severity LOW not MED: the shared core is ~5 trivial lines, fully test-pinned per gate, and the deliberate per-gate threat-model docstrings give real value the suggested flag-driven _iso_age_within would erode. Whether to consolidate vs keep explicit is a design judgment for the developer, hence NEEDS-DECISION.

### 80. [LAZY/JUDGMENT] _TEMPLATE_UPDATE_FIELDS allowlists fields (is_active, sort_order) the update schema can never produce
- **Location:** `app/routes/templates.py` :: 56-60
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-other
- **Claim:** `_TEMPLATE_UPDATE_FIELDS` includes `is_active` and `sort_order`, but `TemplateUpdateSchema` (validation.py:385-411, inheriting TemplateCreateSchema 303-349) declares no `is_active` or `sort_order` field, and BaseSchema uses EXCLUDE for unknowns. So `_update_schema.load(request.form)` never yields those keys, and `_apply_fields_and_propagate_rename`'s `if field in _TEMPLATE_UPDATE_FIELDS` loop can never set them. The create form (form.html) also does not submit them.
- **Why it matters:** The allowlist is broader than the schema can ever populate, which is dead/misleading: a reader auditing what `update_template` can mutate sees `is_active`/`sort_order` and must cross-reference the schema to learn they are unreachable. If a future schema change adds `is_active` as a loadable field, a template archive could silently happen through update_template WITHOUT the projected-transaction soft-delete that archive_template performs, a data-consistency footgun the allowlist currently hides.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop `is_active` and `sort_order` from `_TEMPLATE_UPDATE_FIELDS` (they are managed by the archive/unarchive routes), or add a comment that they are deliberately unreachable via the current schema.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every factual claim verified against the committed code. _TEMPLATE_UPDATE_FIELDS at app/routes/templates.py:56-60 includes "is_active" and "sort_order". The consuming loop is _apply_fields_and_propagate_rename at app/routes/templates.py:191-193: `for field, value in data.items(): if field in _TEMPLATE_UPDATE_FIELDS: setattr(...)` -- it can only set keys present in `data`, which comes from `_update_schema.load(request.form)` at line 397.

Schema chain confirms neither field is loadable: TemplateCreateSchema (validation.py:303-349) declares name/default_amount/category_id/transaction_type_id/account_id/is_envelope/companion_visible plus recurrence fields -- no is_active, no sort_order. TemplateUpdateSchema (validation.py:385-411) inherits it and overrides only those same fields plus effective_from/version_id. BaseSchema.Meta has `unknown = EXCLUDE` (validation.py:157-158), so unknown form keys are dropped, never surfacing in `data`. I confirmed the only `sort_order = fields.Integer` (validation.py:450) belongs to CategoryCreateSchema (class at 445), and the two `is_active = fields.Boolean()` declarations (validation.py:1242, 1346) belong to SavingsGoalUpdateSchema (class at 1211) and AccountUpdateSchema (class at 1330) -- none in the Template chain. grep of app/templates/templates/form.html for is_active/sort_order returns no matches (exit 1). archive_template (templates.py:521) and unarchive_template (templates.py:565) set template.is_active directly; archive ALSO soft-deletes projected transactions (templates.py:527-531), which update_template does not -- corroborating the finding's footgun rationale. No test posts is_active/sort_order through update_template.

Git history: the allowlist was introduced as a mass-assignment guard in commit 61f8131 ("Fix audit findings: ... mass assignment guards ...") already containing is_active+sort_order; at that commit too, is_active(418)/sort_order(146) belonged to SavingsGoalUpdateSchema/CategoryCreateSchema, never the Template chain. So the two entries have been dead since inception. The pylint-10 cleanup commit 1c26575 (which created _apply_fields_and_propagate_rename) did NOT touch the constant.

Not already known: the quality-pass register row for templates.py at docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:336 ACCEPTs _apply_fields_and_propagate_rename under rubric dimensions A4/C2/F2 (helper-extraction cohesion, per the rubric defs at lines 62-101), NOT the allowlist's over-listing; the constant was outside the cleanup diff the reviewer examined. Not a documented disable, not P-1, not P-3.

Severity LOW (not the finding's stated LOW changed): the superset allowlist still filters correctly, so it is dead/misleading code (LAZY), not a present correctness or security defect; the data-consistency hazard is future-conditional on a schema change. Real, low-severity, mechanically-uncatchable.

### 81. [LAZY/JUDGMENT] Inconsistent validation-failure status codes across mutating routes (400 vs 422) for the same client-error class
- **Location:** `app/routes/transactions/mutations.py` :: 303-305
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** routes-fin
- **Claim:** Schema-validation failures use different HTTP statuses across sibling mutating routes with no documented rationale: update_transaction returns 400 (mutations.py:303-305 jsonify(errors=errors),400) and create_inline/create_transaction return 400 (create.py:66-67,114-115), while the entry routes return 422 for the identical 'Marshmallow validate() found errors' case (entries.py:218-220 create_entry, 307-309 update_entry) and mark_done returns 400 on MarshmallowValidationError (mutations.py:555-556). The same validation-failure semantics are mapped to two different status codes within the audited area.
- **Why it matters:** Divergent status codes for one error class make the HTMX client's error handling and any future API consumer inconsistent, and signal a copy-paste-era drift rather than a deliberate contract. It is a maintainability/consistency smell, not a functional bug.
- **Suggested fix:** Pick one status for schema-validation failures (422 is the more correct 'well-formed but semantically invalid' code) and apply it uniformly across the transaction/entry mutating routes, or document why create/update intentionally differ.
- **Verifier evidence:** All cited status codes verified against committed code: app/routes/transactions/mutations.py:303-305 returns `jsonify(errors=errors), 400` on `_update_schema.validate()` errors; create.py:65-67 (create_inline) and 112-114 (create_transaction) both return `jsonify(errors=errors), 400`; mutations.py:553-556 (mark_done) returns `jsonify(errors=exc.messages), 400` on MarshmallowValidationError. By contrast app/routes/entries.py:218-220 (create_entry) and 307-309 (update_entry) return `str(errors), 422` for the identical Marshmallow `validate()`-found-errors case. The transfers routes (transfers/mutations.py:93,193,249,410) also use 400. So the same validation-failure class maps to two different status codes within the audited area -- claim is accurate.

CORRECTION to the finding: it claims "no documented rationale." There IS a documented standard at docs/coding-standards.md:222: "Appropriate status codes. 2xx for swap, 422 for validation errors, 204 for no-content." Under that standard the entries.py 422 routes are CORRECT and the transaction/transfer 400 routes VIOLATE the documented contract. The finding's suggested fix (standardize on 422) matches the existing standard, but the author did not realize the standard already exists.

Both behaviors are pinned by hand-written tests: tests/test_routes/test_entries.py:489,506,519,536,712 assert 422 for amount=0/negative/missing-fields/empty-description; tests/test_routes/test_c27_input_validation_sweep.py:226,248,275 and tests/test_routes/test_mark_paid_entries.py:306 assert 400. docs/implementation_plan_section9.md:2042 also specifies 422 for entry create validation.

Functional impact is nil for the current client: app/static/js/app.js:169 (htmx:responseError) only special-cases [data-carry-forward-confirm]; HTMX treats all 4xx uniformly (no swap) for these routes, and the differing bodies (jsonify(errors=...) vs str(errors)) are not consumed/displayed for transaction/entry routes. Response-body shape also diverges, compounding the smell.

Not already known: not P-1, not P-3, not a pylint disable; the quality-pass register row 30 (docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:148) covers entries.py's _execute_entry_update extraction but says nothing about the 400/422 divergence.

NEEDS-DECISION because: it is a real, accurate consistency defect that contradicts the project's own documented 422 standard, but (a) it has zero functional effect on the HTMX client, and (b) "fixing" the 400 routes to 422 requires changing the hand-computed 400 assertions in test_c27_input_validation_sweep.py / test_mark_paid_entries.py, which under CLAUDE.md rule 5 the developer must confirm as an intended contract change. Severity LOW is correct.

### 82. [SOLID/JUDGMENT] dashboard_service._get_debt_summary recomputes the entire savings dashboard to pluck one key and swallows three exception types
- **Location:** `app/services/dashboard_service.py` :: 570-588
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-arch-solid
- **Claim:** `_get_debt_summary` calls `savings_dashboard_service.compute_dashboard_data(user_id)` (line 582) - which (per _orchestrator.py:35-137) loads accounts, computes per-account projections, the canonical paycheck breakdown, savings-goal progress, emergency-fund metrics, net worth, and archived accounts - then discards all of it except `dashboard_data.get("debt_summary")`. The same module's own deferred-import comment (lines 576-578) states this path 'pulls the heaviest service import chain (+27 modules, measured).' The result is wrapped in `except (ValueError, KeyError, AttributeError)` returning `None` (lines 584-588).
- **Why it matters:** Two problems: (1) Efficiency/SRP - the main dashboard runs the full savings-dashboard computation (including a live paycheck/tax calculation) just to obtain one debt sub-dict; the focused producer `_compute_debt_summary` already exists in savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:282 but is not reused. (2) Error-masking - an AttributeError or KeyError from that large computation (exactly the failure mode a refactor introduces) is logged at warning level and the debt summary silently vanishes from the user's dashboard, violating the 'never ignore a problem / fix root causes' rule and hiding real-money debt information.
- **Suggested fix:** Expose a narrow public debt-summary producer in savings_dashboard_service that computes only the debt path, call it directly, and let genuine programming errors propagate instead of catching ValueError/KeyError/AttributeError.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every literal claim in the finding is accurate. app/services/dashboard_service.py:582 calls savings_dashboard_service.compute_dashboard_data(user_id) and line 583 discards everything except dashboard_data.get("debt_summary"). The deferred-import comment "+27 modules, measured" is at lines 576-578. The catch of (ValueError, KeyError, AttributeError) -> warning log -> return None is at lines 584-588. The orchestrator (app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_orchestrator.py:35-137) does run the full chain: _compute_account_projections (line 67), a live calculate_paycheck via _get_current_paycheck_breakdown (lines 80-82), _compute_goal_progress (89-91), emergency-fund metrics (94-101), total_savings (98), archived accounts (135). The focused producer _compute_debt_summary exists at app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:282-328 and is not directly reused by the main dashboard.

HOWEVER the finding's reasoning and suggested fix are partly wrong, which lowers severity:
(1) The suggested "narrow debt-only producer" would REGRESS behavior. The main dashboard template app/templates/dashboard/_debt_summary.html:11-21 renders debt_summary.dti_ratio and dti_label. Those fields are NOT produced by _compute_debt_summary (it returns only total_debt/total_monthly_payments/weighted_avg_rate/projected_debt_free_date, _metrics.py:323-327). DTI is added by _apply_dti_metrics (_orchestrator.py:114-125 -> _metrics.py:350-381), which requires gross_biweekly from the canonical paycheck breakdown -- the exact "heavy" calculate_paycheck call the finding wants to avoid. _compute_debt_summary itself consumes loan_params/monthly_payment/payoff_date/is_paid_off/current_balance that come only from _compute_account_projections (_projections.py:388-397 via _accumulate_loan_debt, _metrics.py:243-277). So a faithful debt+DTI path still needs loan projections + escrow load + the paycheck engine; the genuinely-wasted work is the non-loan account projections, goal progress, EF metrics, net worth, archived accounts -- real but bounded inefficiency (one extra dashboard render on page load), not "discards all of it."
(2) The error-masking concern is legitimate: a future KeyError/AttributeError (a real programming bug) is swallowed at warning level and the debt panel silently vanishes, which runs against rule 4. But whether the dashboard should degrade gracefully (current intent) vs. let programming errors propagate and 500 the page is a design judgment, not a clear-cut bug.

Not P-1, not P-3, no quality-pass ACCEPT row covers this, and the only documented disable here (import-outside-toplevel, lines 576-579) is unrelated to the SRP/error-masking concern. Test coverage is thin: tests/test_services/test_dashboard_service.py:854 only asserts the no-debt -> None path. Net: a real maintainability/efficiency smell plus a debatable defensive catch, not a confirmed correctness defect; the correct remedy (refactor narrow producer carrying DTI, and/or narrow the except) is a developer design call.

### 83. [SOLID/JUDGMENT] pension_calculator reaches into paycheck_calculator's private _apply_raises via fabricated duck-typed objects
- **Location:** `app/services/pension_calculator.py` :: 99-117
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-arch-solid
- **Claim:** project_salaries_by_year does a function-local `from app.services.paycheck_calculator import _apply_raises` (line 99 - a leading-underscore private function), then constructs ad-hoc `_FakeProfile`/`_FakePeriod` classes (lines 100-108) solely to satisfy the shape `_apply_raises(profile, period)` expects (profile.annual_salary, profile.raises, period.start_date). This is the ONLY external caller of `_apply_raises` (grep across app/ shows pension_calculator.py:114 is the sole call site; the only other reference, savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:62, is a docstring mention, not a call).
- **Why it matters:** The raise-application business rule (sort order flat-before-percentage, recurring compounding count, one-time gating) is owned privately by paycheck_calculator but silently consumed by a second service through a private symbol plus mock objects. If paycheck_calculator's private signature or attribute expectations change during a refactor, pension projections break with no compile/lint signal, and the two raise-application code paths can diverge - directly affecting projected retirement salary and pension benefit. The fake-object indirection also defeats type checking on the real contract.
- **Suggested fix:** Promote the raise-application logic to a public, parameter-typed function in a shared module (e.g. paycheck_calculator.apply_raises(annual_salary, raises, year, month) -> Decimal) and have both paycheck_calculator and pension_calculator call it, eliminating the private reach-in and the _Fake* classes.
- **Verifier evidence:** Factual claims verified against committed code. pension_calculator.py:99 does `from app.services.paycheck_calculator import _apply_raises` (function-local, leading-underscore private). Lines 101-108 define `_FakePeriod` (start_date) and `_FakeProfile` (annual_salary, raises) duck-typed objects; line 114 calls `_apply_raises(profile, period)`. (Minor imprecision: the finding lists Profile-then-Period but code defines Period first; immaterial.) The contract consumed is confirmed at paycheck_calculator.py:572-624 -- `_apply_raises(profile, period)` reads profile.annual_salary, profile.raises, period.start_date, with the M-01 sort (flat-before-percentage), recurring-compounding count, and one-time gating business rules. grep across app/ confirms pension_calculator.py:114 is the SOLE external call site; the only other app/ reference is a docstring at savings_dashboard_service/_metrics.py:62 (verified: prose in a docstring, not a call). Both production callers of the public wrapper route through retirement_dashboard_service.py:433 and :617, so the reach-in is contained but real.

Real-issue assessment: this is a genuine SOLID/cohesion smell -- a second service consuming another service's leading-underscore private symbol via fabricated mock objects, defeating type checking on the implicit contract. NOT safe-by-construction: a refactor of _apply_raises's param shape would break pension projections with no lint/compile signal. NOT rule-13 gold-plating. Partially mitigated by tests (tests/test_services/test_pension_calculator.py:194,213,235 exercise the REAL _apply_raises via project_salaries_by_year, so a signature drift would surface as a test failure, not silently in prod) -- but the design fragility (private reach-in + _Fake* indirection) persists regardless.

Not already-known: the quality-pass/pylint-cleanup docs document only the adjacent `import-outside-toplevel` disable as KEEP for leaf-purity (plan.md:854) and the retirement_dashboard decomposition (plan.md:2263); neither the quality-pass register nor docs/audits/financial_calculations/06_dry_solid.md (which mentions pension_calculator only for the TWO_PLACES constant at :641) flags this _FakeProfile/_apply_raises reach-in. It is not P-1 or P-3.

Severity lowered MED->LOW: both call sites share the identical _apply_raises function today, so there is NO live computation divergence and NO current financial miscalculation -- the harm is future fragility/maintainability, and tests do exercise the real function. Verdict NEEDS-DECISION because the accurate, real concern's correct resolution (promote to a public typed shared function vs. accept the intentional internal coupling for the stated leaf-purity reason) is a design judgment for the developer.

### 84. [SOLID/JUDGMENT] transfer_recurrence imports two private functions from recurrence_engine, coupling to another module's internals
- **Location:** `app/services/transfer_recurrence.py` :: 32
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-arch-solid
- **Claim:** `from app.services.recurrence_engine import _compute_due_date, _resolve_generation_plan` imports two underscore-prefixed (private-by-convention) functions and calls `_resolve_generation_plan` at line 65. Two modules now share recurrence_engine's internal generation-plan contract with no public surface; a refactor of those private helpers silently changes transfer generation.
- **Why it matters:** Cross-module dependence on private functions makes the recurrence-plan logic effectively public without a stable contract or tests guaranteeing the shape both callers rely on, raising the chance that a change to the transaction engine quietly breaks transfer recurrence.
- **Suggested fix:** Promote the shared generation-plan/due-date logic to a public function (e.g. in _recurrence_common) that both recurrence_engine and transfer_recurrence import, making the shared contract explicit.
- **Verifier evidence:** FACTUAL: app/services/transfer_recurrence.py:32 reads verbatim `from app.services.recurrence_engine import _compute_due_date, _resolve_generation_plan`; `_resolve_generation_plan` is called at line 65, `_compute_due_date` at line 107. Both are underscore-prefixed in the defining module (recurrence_engine.py:73 def `_resolve_generation_plan`, recurrence_engine.py:610 def `_compute_due_date`). So the claim "two underscore-prefixed private functions imported, _resolve_generation_plan called at line 65" is exact.

REAL-ISSUE (mitigated): the cross-module consumption of underscore-private symbols is a genuine cohesion smell, but heavily mitigated and NOT cleanly fixable as suggested:
(1) Intentional + documented: transfer_recurrence.py:4-10 and 59-64, plus _recurrence_common.py:8-24, explicitly describe the two engines as deliberate parallels sharing the model-agnostic preamble so they "cannot drift."
(2) Suggested fix (promote into _recurrence_common) is import-cycle-blocked: recurrence_engine.py:41 already imports FROM _recurrence_common; _resolve_generation_plan needs recurrence_engine.match_periods (recurrence_engine.py:122). _recurrence_common.py:21-24 states verbatim that hoisting it "would create an import cycle." So the finding's own remedy is infeasible.
(3) "No tests guaranteeing the shape" is partly false: _compute_due_date has a dedicated pure-function unit test (tests/test_services/test_recurrence_engine.py:2685-2722) and is exercised through transfer paths (tests/test_services/test_transfer_recurrence.py; tests/test_integration/test_loan_transfer_live_amount.py:209). A signature drift would fail tests, not silently break transfer generation.
(4) The scope is wider than the finding states: _compute_due_date is also imported cross-module by app/routes/transfers/templates.py:36/655, migrations/versions/48e2c7ee593d_...py:133, and scripts/backfill_transfer_due_dates.py:93 -- it is de-facto public API, like match_periods which was promoted for exactly this reason (docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/quality-pass.md:338, where reviewers chose NOT to promote _compute_due_date/_resolve_generation_plan).
