ALREADY-KNOWN: This exact recurrence/transfer coupling claim is not separately recorded, but its SOLID class is the precedent finding #51 (deep-quality-hunt.md:991-1003, pension_calculator reaching paycheck_calculator._apply_raises), graded LOW / NEEDS-DECISION. A separate, distinct finding about _resolve_generation_plan (the effective_from/IDOR boundary at deep-quality-hunt.md:391,398) is unrelated to F7's cohesion concern. It is NOT P-1/P-3 and NOT a documented disable.

VERDICT NEEDS-DECISION: accurate and a real (if low) cohesion concern, but the resolution is a developer design judgment -- accept the documented intentional sharing, or expose a public surface that avoids the import cycle (rename the symbols to public in recurrence_engine, which IS the de-facto-public home, rather than relocating to _recurrence_common as suggested). Severity LOW is correct: no current behavioral/financial defect, shared contract is test-covered.

### 85. [SOLID/JUDGMENT] get_accessible_transaction silently denies companion-visibility without any structured log event, diverging from the other ownership helpers
- **Location:** `app/utils/auth_helpers.py` :: 267-308
- **Verdict:** NEEDS-DECISION (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** auth-sec
- **Claim:** get_or_404 (122-179) and get_owned_via_parent (182-264) emit access_denied_cross_user / resource_not_found on every denial branch (the F-144/C-14 forensic contract). get_accessible_transaction returns None on the companion cross-owner and not-companion-visible denials (lines 301-307) with no log_event at all; the docstring (284-287) acknowledges it 'preserves verbatim the pre-extraction inline behaviour ... which were silent on the companion-visibility denial.' It also reads current_user.role_id / .id / .linked_owner_id directly rather than through _safe_user_id(), so an anonymous/misordered-decorator call raises AttributeError instead of being logged as an anonymous probe like the sibling helpers.
- **Why it matters:** A companion enumerating an owner's transaction IDs or probing companion_visible flags is exactly the cross-user probing the C-14 logging was added to surface, yet this helper (used by both the entry-CRUD and status-change routes) leaves no application-tier trace. The inconsistency means SOC dashboards see IDOR probes on some routes but are blind on the transaction routes.
- **Suggested fix:** Emit EVT_ACCESS_DENIED_CROSS_USER on the two companion denial branches and route user-id reads through _safe_user_id() so behavior matches get_or_404/get_owned_via_parent.
- **Verifier evidence:** Every factual claim verified against the committed code.

(1) get_accessible_transaction (app/utils/auth_helpers.py:267-308) returns None on the two companion denial branches (301-303: linked_owner mismatch OR not visible_to_companion) and the owner denial (306) with NO log_event anywhere in the function body (294-308). The docstring at 283-286 states verbatim: "Unlike get_or_404 / get_owned_via_parent, this helper does not emit a denial log_event; it preserves verbatim the pre-extraction inline behaviour ... which were silent on the companion-visibility denial." CONFIRMED.

(2) The two sibling helpers DO emit on every denial branch: get_or_404 (122-179) emits EVT_RESOURCE_NOT_FOUND (156-164) and EVT_ACCESS_DENIED_CROSS_USER (168-177); get_owned_via_parent (182-264) emits EVT_RESOURCE_NOT_FOUND (222-230), EVT_ACCESS_DENIED_CROSS_USER on parent-unloadable (238-248) and cross-user (252-261). CONFIRMED.

(3) get_accessible_transaction reads current_user.role_id (298), .linked_owner_id (301), .id (306) directly, not via _safe_user_id() (defined 60-74). An anonymous/misordered-decorator call therefore raises AttributeError rather than logging an anonymous probe -- exactly the path _safe_user_id's own docstring (64-72) was written to handle gracefully. CONFIRMED, though all current callers use @login_required (entries.py:190/205/281/330/378; transactions/mutations.py via require_owner+login), so this is the adversarial path, not the normal flow.

(4) Reachability + test gap: the companion cross-owner probe is reachable and exercised -- test_companion_guards.py:404 (test_companion_blocked_from_other_owner_transaction) and :387 (non-visible) assert ONLY status_code==404, never a log event. By contrast the F-144/C-14 logging contract IS test-pinned for the three sibling helpers: test_auth_helpers.py:506-519 (get_or_404 cross-user), :572-608 (get_owned_via_parent cross-user), :615-657 (require_owner owner-only). So the gap is genuinely uncovered. This is the C-14 IDOR-probe class (a companion enumerating an owner's txn IDs / probing companion_visible flags) leaving no application-tier trace on the entry-CRUD and status-change routes.

(5) Not gold-plating, not safe-by-construction: access IS correctly denied (404) in every branch, but the divergence from the module's own stated F-144 contract (docstring 25-31: "Every ownership-failure branch in this module emits a structured log_event") is real -- this helper is the one branch that does not.

ALREADY-KNOWN status: F5 is a near-twin of recorded finding #34 in docs/audits/pylint-cleanup/deep-quality-hunt.md:707-727 ("Account ownership check re-inlined 7+ times ... silently dropping the IDOR audit-log event"), ruled NEEDS-DECISION/LOW with identical reasoning (inline checks emit no F-144 event; verbatim-preserved legacy; developer has a documented disposition to leave 404-returning legacy inline patterns at Low/Info per the F-087 deflation). BUT #34 explicitly enumerates its sites (anchor.py, investment.py, accounts/detail.py, loan/_helpers.py) and does NOT include get_accessible_transaction. The extraction commit 86eb309 created this helper byte-identical from entries._get_accessible_transaction + transactions._get_accessible_transaction_for_status and the commit message states it "preserves the no-denial-log behaviour verbatim." quality-pass register #30 (entries.py, 6e3c32d) and #10 (transactions pkg) covered byte-equivalence only, never the denial-log divergence. Not a documented disable, not P-1/P-3. So F5 is a DISTINCT, not-yet-recorded site of the same class #34 already flagged.

WHY NEEDS-DECISION not CONFIRMED: like its twin #34, the disposition (retrofit EVT_ACCESS_DENIED_CROSS_USER + route reads through _safe_user_id, vs preserve the verbatim legacy at Low priority) is the F-144/F-087 follow-through judgment the developer already chose to treat as NEEDS-DECISION. Severity LOW (not the finding's stated LOW being wrong -- it agrees): access is denied correctly everywhere; the gap is observability/consistency, not data exposure.

### 86. [TEST-QUALITY/JUDGMENT] Only the no-debt path of _get_debt_summary is tested; the error-masking and with-debt paths are uncovered
- **Location:** `tests/test_services/test_dashboard_service.py` :: 848-855
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r2  |  **Cluster:** X-arch-solid
- **Claim:** `TestDebtSummary` contains a single test asserting `_get_debt_summary` returns None when there is no debt (line 854-855). There is no test for the with-debt success path and none that distinguishes the broad-except None (computation failed) from the legitimate no-debt None (dashboard_service.py:584-604). The two outcomes are indistinguishable, so a regression that makes debt computation throw would still pass this test while silently hiding real debt.
- **Why it matters:** The one assertion cannot detect the most dangerous regression (debt silently swallowed), giving false confidence that the debt card on the main dashboard is correct.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a with-debt test asserting the returned summary's exact figures, and a test that a raised error inside compute_dashboard_data is not silently converted to None (or is logged and re-raised).
- **Verifier evidence:** Verified every claim against the committed code.

(1) test_dashboard_service.py:848-855 -- TestDebtSummary contains exactly ONE test method, test_debt_summary_no_debt (851-855). I confirmed it is the only def test_ between the class at 848 and the next class TestSpendingComparison at 861. Its single assertion is `assert result is None` (855) after calling `dashboard_service._get_debt_summary(seed_user["user"].id)` (854) with no debt seeded. CONFIRMED as claimed.

(2) dashboard_service.py:581-588 -- _get_debt_summary wraps `savings_dashboard_service.compute_dashboard_data(user_id)` then returns `dashboard_data.get("debt_summary")`; the except at 584 catches (ValueError, KeyError, AttributeError), logs a warning (585-587), and `return None` (588). So an error-path None and the legitimate no-debt None are indeed indistinguishable to the caller, and the one existing test would still pass if debt computation regressed to raise one of those exceptions -- silently hiding real debt on the main dashboard. (Minor inaccuracy: the finding cites "584-604"; the except block is actually 584-588 -- line 604 is the docstring of the next function _get_spending_comparison. The end-line is overstated but the block and its behavior are exactly as described.)

(3) No with-debt or error-distinguishing test for _get_debt_summary exists. grep for _get_debt_summary/debt_summary across tests: the with-debt success path IS covered, but through a DIFFERENT code path -- savings_dashboard_service.compute_dashboard_data directly (test_savings_dashboard_service.py:975-1796 covers single/multiple/escrow/paid-off/DTI) and the /savings route (test_savings.py:3018 TestDebtSummaryDisplay). app/routes/savings.py:110 calls savings_dashboard_service.compute_dashboard_data directly, NOT the dashboard_service wrapper. The main dashboard route (dashboard.py:30) is the only caller of _get_debt_summary, and its route tests (test_dashboard.py) contain ZERO debt references; test_dashboard_all_sections_present (123-134) asserts 6 sections but not "Debt Summary", and its fixture seed_full_user_data (conftest.py:1644-1769) seeds NO loan/debt account, so even incidentally the wrapper's with-debt path and broad-except path are never exercised. CONFIRMED.

(4) Not already known: the broad-except is compliant with the broad-exception-caught gate (it names three specific exceptions, not Exception), so it is not a documented disable. quality-pass.md references dashboard_service only for R0801/DRY clusters (lines 515-554), with no ACCEPT row for this test gap or the masking behavior. Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction).

The dangerous-regression concern (debt silently swallowed by the broad-except, undetectable by the lone test) is genuine and money-relevant, so the finding is a real test-quality defect, not gold-plating. LOW severity is appropriate: the underlying debt math is well-tested via the other path, so the residual risk is narrowly the wrapper's own success-extraction and error-masking behavior.

### 87. [TEST-QUALITY/JUDGMENT] live_projected_net test computes its expected value by re-running the same project_salary pipeline (assertion derived from code under test)
- **Location:** `tests/test_services/test_income_service.py` :: 160-208
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** paycheck-tax
- **Claim:** TestLiveProjectedNet._expected_net (lines 160-176) builds the expected dict by calling pay_period_service.get_all_periods + load_tax_configs + paycheck_calculator.project_salary -- the EXACT path live_projected_net itself uses internally (income_service.py:222-231). test_recomputes_live_ignoring_stored_amount (line 206-207) then asserts `overrides == {txn.id: expected}`. The only independent check is `overrides[txn.id] != Decimal('1.00')` (line 208).
- **Why it matters:** The equality assertion is tautological: any bug in project_salary or the net-pay arithmetic appears identically on both sides and the test still passes. It verifies only that live_projected_net delegates to project_salary, not that the produced net pay is correct. Per testing-standards (service tests assert exact computed values with the arithmetic shown), the expected net should be a hand-computed constant.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace _expected_net with a hand-computed Decimal constant for the seeded $104k profile (the docstring already derives $4,120.00 gross), asserting the actual net value rather than re-deriving it from the engine.
- **Verifier evidence:** CONFIRMED, accurate. tests/test_services/test_income_service.py:160-176 `_expected_net` re-runs the producer's own pipeline verbatim: pay_period_service.get_all_periods (L169), load_tax_configs (L170), paycheck_calculator.project_salary(profile, periods, tax_configs, calibration=profile.calibration) (L171-173), then {bd.period.period_id: bd.earnings.net_pay ...}[period_id] (L174-176). This is byte-identical to income_service.live_projected_net's internal path at app/services/income_service.py:222-231 (same get_all_periods, same load_tax_configs, same project_salary call, same net_pay map). The target test test_recomputes_live_ignoring_stored_amount (L178-208) asserts `overrides == {txn.id: expected}` (L207) with expected sourced from the re-derivation, plus only `overrides[txn.id] != Decimal("1.00")` (L208). The equality is therefore tautological for net-pay correctness: a bug in project_salary or the net arithmetic appears on both sides. It proves only delegation + cache-bypass, not the produced net value. The fix is feasible and not a design judgment: the test uses _create_profile with NO raise (no _add_one_time_raise) and seeds no tax configs, on period index 5 -- the IDENTICAL setup as the sibling TestLiveIncomeThroughBalanceResolver.test_stale_stored_income_overridden_by_live_net (L314-371), which re-derives the same way but ALSO hard-asserts `assert expected_net == Decimal("4000.00")` (L350). Every other test in the file pins a hand-computed constant (_RAISE_APPLIED_GROSS=4120.00 L48/L431, _NO_RAISE_GROSS=4000.00 L49/L453, Decimal("0") L470, Decimal("1234.56") L400). So the target test could assert `expected == Decimal("4000.00")`. Not P-1/P-3, not a documented disable, not in any quality-pass ACCEPT row I can cite. Severity downgraded to LOW because the co-located sibling test (L350) already pins the exact same net value ($4000.00, same no-raise/no-tax setup) with a hard constant, so a genuine net-computation regression would still be caught in the same file; the residual gap is the tautological assertion itself, which violates testing-standards ("Service tests assert exact computed values").

### 88. [TEST-QUALITY/JUDGMENT] Weak progress_pct assertions: comment states the exact formula but test asserts only '> 0', missing the truncation/clamp divergence
- **Location:** `tests/test_services/test_savings_dashboard_service.py` :: 384-389
- **Verdict:** CONFIRMED (HIGH confidence)  |  **Runs:** r1  |  **Cluster:** X-semantic-dup
- **Claim:** The income-relative progress test writes the exact arithmetic in a comment ('progress_pct = 1000 / resolved_target * 100', 386-387) but then asserts only 'gd[progress_pct] > 0' (389), violating the testing standard 'assert exact computed values ... not result > 0'. The 50% case at line 169 asserts == 50, a value where int-truncation and HALF_UP-rounding coincide, so no test pins the truncation behavior or the missing lower clamp that distinguishes this code from percent_complete (see F1).
- **Why it matters:** No test would catch a regression in or a fix of the divergent progress_pct rule (F1): swapping in percent_complete, or a sign/clamp bug, passes the existing assertions. The weak assertion masks the very behavior that differs from the canonical helper.
- **Suggested fix:** Assert the exact integer (e.g. a 99.6%-funded goal yields the expected pinned value) and add a negative-balance case asserting the documented lower-bound behavior.
- **Verifier evidence:** I was asked to REFUTE this but the code independently confirms it.

TEST FACTS (tests/test_services/test_savings_dashboard_service.py):
- Lines 386-387 write the exact arithmetic in a comment: "progress_pct = 1000 / resolved_target * 100." Line 389 then asserts only `gd["progress_pct"] > 0`. This is precisely the `result > 0` form the documented testing standard forbids (.claude/rules/testing.md: "Service tests assert exact computed values ... not `result > 0`"). The salary is deterministic (annual_salary=Decimal("75000.00"), line 359), so the exact progress_pct IS computable -- the weak assertion is a real gap, not an unavoidable nondeterminism.
- Line 169 asserts `== 50` for a 5000/10000 goal. 5000/10000*100 = 50 exactly, so int-truncation (int(50)=50) and ROUND_HALF_UP (50.00) coincide; this case cannot distinguish the truncation rule.
- The ONLY other progress_pct assertions in the whole suite are line 313 `== 0`, line 419 `== 0` (zero-target). grep over tests/ shows no case that pins int-truncation (e.g. a 99.6%-funded goal where int()->99 but HALF_UP->100) and no negative-balance case.

DIVERGENCE IS REAL (the F1 the finding hinges on):
- Inline code app/services/savings_dashboard_service/_goals.py:119-124 uses `min(100, int(acct_balance / resolved_target * 100))` -- int() truncation, upper clamp only, NO lower clamp.
- Canonical helper app/utils/money.py:106-133 (percent_complete) uses `.quantize(CENTS, rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)` AND both an upper clamp (line 129-130) and a lower clamp (line 131-132: `if pct < ZERO: return ZERO`).
- Therefore swapping the inline code for percent_complete, or introducing a sign/clamp regression, passes every existing assertion -- confirming why_it_matters.

NOT ALREADY KNOWN:
- quality-pass.md row 6 (savings_dashboard_service pkg) is REVIEWED but flags only "M2: untyped params bag, built-then-patched" -- nothing about test assertion strength or progress_pct truncation/clamp.
- Not P-1 (loan escrow) or P-3 (negative deduction). plan.md R0801 candidate 24 concerns source duplication of the progress computation, not this test's assertion.

Severity LOW is correct: this is a test-quality (assertion-strength + uncovered-edge) gap, not a live miscalculation in this finding's scope.
